When an intestinal disorder comes from cold and moisture, so that the retaining and digestive virtues which are in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and cannot be treated by any means of treatment; and you see the patient suffering greatly and with great strength, then make one large cautery on the stomach according to what has been mentioned earlier about the cautery of the stomach, around the belly button. And four small cauteries around the throat, each like a small key cautery, and two cauteries on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see moisture abounding and the patient suffering greatly, then make one cautery on the point of the chin, one cautery on each ear, and two small cauteries on the stomach near the large one; for treatment is helpful when there is good assistance.
de la cure des emorroydes	Of the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: .iij. sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et .i. cautere desoz la boude. ij. dois;	When hemorrhoids are in the fundament, one or more, and are old and large cold moist humors that have decayed, and they have been treated according to what we have mentioned earlier, but there is no benefit, then make cauteries: three on the spine of the back, that one which is directly behind the navel and tapers off towards the bottom, and one cautery below the belly button.
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on .i. grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et .i. autre sus le foie, et i. autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you think that his stomach is cooled and the food does not cook properly, and you see swelling of the face, then make one large cautery on the stomach as it was mentioned earlier, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen with a key-shaped cautery; leave the cautery on for a long time. Afterwards treat the wound until it is healthy again.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	Of the fleshy growth called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut off a veinlet, heat the cautery that appears like a razor, then place it completely aflame on that cut vein; and leave your hand there until the cautery reaches the base of the vein where blood flows. Do this once or twice; if there is much veinlet, cauterize each one as we have said; afterward, treat with beneficial ointments until they are sound; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on an artery, it will be more helpful.
de plaie mal curee	Of poorly-treated wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	If the patient cannot endure incision or opening, which we will discuss in its proper place, then there comes such a disease that can only be cured by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If a fistula appears and is inflamed and filled with rottenness and corrupted moisture, you should probe it with a subtle tent throughout its entire length, and ensure that you know the full depth of the tent. Afterward, heat the cautery that resembles a razor, and insert it into the fistula according to the quantity that the tent has entered; then continue applying the cautery until all the decayed and corrupted flesh is burned away, once, twice, or three times, depending on what is required; but beware of burning nerves that are nearby, as well as large veins. If the fistula reaches the bladder or intestines, be careful in those places, and do not apply the cautery except in a narrow area, and consider it not to be penetrating; afterward, treat the wound until it is healed, and if the wound remains dry and the matter has been removed for a long time, then know that the wound is entirely healed. But if the matter has not been removed, know that the wound is too deep and that decayed bone lies at its base; and so one of those we will discuss later.
de la maladie des reins	de la maladie dels rengs (Occitan)
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When cold pain comes to the kidneys and from gross winds, and it does not take on the nature of a woman's menses, then you must perform cautery on the kidneys on both sides with the clavicle cautery that we have mentioned earlier; and if we cauterize it in the middle, it will have three cauteries in a row, and this will provide greater relief.
de la vessie	Of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is weak and cold due to moisture so that the patient retains urine, then perform cautery on the front of the bladder where the pubic hair begins, one on the right side and one on the left side, each cautery being as long as a hazelnut; and also perform one cautery behind the back if needed, or two if necessary; and use the clavicle cautery according to the shape described earlier.
de la marris	Of the womb
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the womb is cold and moist and does not allow conception due to this, and the flowers are corrupted and their terms delayed; and when they do come, there is great pain: then it is necessary to perform three cauteries around the navel, as we have said for the bladder cautery, and two cauteries behind the back; and use the clavicle cautery, as we have said.
de la hainche	Of the hair
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When viscous moistures descend to the hair socket and cause it to move from its place, and the sign is that one thigh appears longer than the other when measured together, and the parting of the hair is found empty; then you must perform cautery on the patient above the hair socket with a circular cautery, encircling the socket as it turns so that the socket is within the circle; and use cauteries similar to those used for the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if these cauteries are not available, then perform three large olive-shaped cauteries and let them be as deep as all the others; and do this until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	Of pain in the hair
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain occurs in the hip joint, and it is due to coldness and moisture, and the patient has been treated for this as we have discussed previously but the treatment is ineffective, and the condition is chronic: then you must purge the patient of thick humors using foul-tasting pills or similar good pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	Afterward, perform cauterization; and the manner of cauterization is according to two methods: namely, using medicines together with burning or fire cautery. Fire cautery has many methods, one of which is as follows: you should cauterize on the hip joint three triangular cauteries in this shape, making them deep and wide, and have the space between each cautery be the size of a finger, and make the cauteries olive-shaped. Sometimes, cautery is performed in the middle on top of the hip joint, so there are four cauteries in total according to this shape
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you wish to perform cautery with the circular cautery that we mentioned earlier in the case of hip joint dislocation, do it in such a way that the circle contains the entire hip joint, and all the fat around the bone is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And this is the method used in sciatica when pain is felt in the hip joint but does not reach the thigh or leg. If it reaches the thigh and leg, make two cauteries where the patient feels the pain and one cautery above the ankle bone on the left side slightly forward; let these cauteries be scalpel-shaped and burn the thickness of the fat. And if the patient feels that the pain extends to two fingers' width from the heel, cauterize there using three or four "points" cauteries.
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if it is necessary, then make more cauteries; and if the pain is felt below the knee towards the thigh, perform a scalpel-shaped or circular cautery there. Be sure in all your cauteries that you do not let the cautery burn the nerves and large arteries, and do not cause greater harm and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	And I have seen many who performed cautery on the ankle bone of the foot, leaving it so that the leg became completely swollen and the foot as well; it was pierced and corrupted all over the foot. Afterward, a stomachache led to his death.
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere. // Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And if the pain is in two places at once, cauterize one and the other according to this manner.
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	**And let it be heated until it is all red and gleaming hot, then place it on the bad boil, turned towards the sound side; cauterize once with one cautery, leave it three days; afterwards make an emplaster of butter, leave the wound open for a long time; thereafter cure with ointment until it is healed.**
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	**Albucasis says that we use this cautery little for fear of its burning, and few people use it; yet this is one of the good cauteries, which can bear it well.**
de la dolor dou dos	**of the pain in the back**
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether from falling or impact or excessive bleeding, or from similar matter spread coldly, in none of these cases does fire cautery help except for that which comes from the infusing of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary that after the patient has been purged with fetid pills or others similar ones, three lines of incisions be made on their back where the pain is felt, and five cauteries or more be applied in each line according to the strength and quantity that the patient can endure; and let the cautery be done according to the cautery called "poins"; and if you see, make 3 or 4 cauteries at the middle clavicle bone according to this shape:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This illness often occurs in young children, and the sign of its onset is that they have difficulty breathing when lying down and are afraid; and you find on the back spine and on both sides the appearance that comes up over the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and wish to cure it, cauterize with the cautery of a cell according to this shape:
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	So that the cautery touches each part of the spine evenly. And if you see fit, then cauterize around the spine with the pointed cautery 2 or 3 lines deep, and let the points be close together. Afterward, dress the wound until it is healed according to what we have said, and make sure that you do not apply a cautery in spasm of the nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	de la dolor des jointes
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pain in the joints is caused by moistures that are spread throughout each limb of the body, and when pain comes to the foot, which doctors properly call "podagra," and when it is caused by coldness and cannot be cured by medicines, it is treated by cauterization in this manner: make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olivary according to this shape:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	"And if there is need that you press upon the face of the foot, make cautery over all the cautery that is called 'point'. And if pains extend to the knees and other joints, which happens often, make cautery upon each knee .iii. cauteries or .iiij. on each side, with all cauteries olive-shaped; and if you need more, then make more, but do not hold your hand longer than until the edge of the heart is burned."
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	"And if the pains extend to the knee and back, let him administer the cautery that we have spoken of in its chapter. And if there are pains in the hands, make pricks around the little finger at two lines; and if there remains any pain in the arms, make pricks upon each joint and upon the hair of the hand; and if the pains extend to the elbows or shoulders, cauterize each part, and give good care to the patient and take medicines. For if you give him good care and purge fleume, he shall be healed by the help of God."
de la routure dou syfac	"Of the cutting of the sciatic nerve"
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	"When cutting comes in angles, and the intestines descend to the thighs and it is newly happened, so that when you see him cure it, he should not eat that day; and let him use things that leave the stomach empty, so that the wind descends from his stomach; afterwards make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his elbow until the intestines are repaired, and stretch out the sinews to your two fingers, and seize with a pinch below the cut over the bone of the finger, and at one sign which should resemble half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery of which this is the shape:"
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	"Until it is white and gives forth sparks. Then stretch the intestines back to their place; and let the minister hold his hand upon them so that they do not return backwards; and open well the thighs of the patient, and put beneath him one cushion and one sergeant on each thigh, and another on his chest which holds his hands; then put the cautery on the sign with your whole hand, and press it with your right hand until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, repeat it again until you reach the bone; and be careful that the intestines do not slip out when you are making the cautery; so that you do not burn them; and that through this the patient does not die or suffer some other harm."
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	"And know that if you do not come to the bone with the cautery, your efforts are worth nothing. And it is necessary that the cauteries for children be subtle according to their size, and for large people they should also be large according to their measure; afterwards three days after the place of the cautery should be fomented with butter until the blistering is removed; afterwards cure him with other ointments until he is healed, and let the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound is well healed; and it is necessary that his diet be restricted so that the intestines do not slip out when he gets up to go to chambers."
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	"And after forty days, when he wants to get up, provide him with a well-made bandage, and let him wear it for another forty days; and let him have good rest, so that he does not work too much and be careful of excess in drinking and eating, and of raising his voice too high; and when he follows this teaching, then he is entirely healed. And I will say hereafter the cure of cutting in its chapter."
de la routure dou ventre	"de la routure du ventre"
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures come in other bellies and are known,
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But mark first the point of entry and draw a line across the width above the rupture, and another below it, and hold your hand amidst all the cautery with a key-shaped tool. But the first cauteries are lighter and gentler.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of past pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain occurs in any limb from falling or striking it, and this pain persists for a long time, and the cure with medicine does not work, then it must be cauterized with the cautery called "poins", and the cautery should be according to the length of the limb and its smallness, weakness, strength, location, twists, and severity of pain. If the first cautery is sufficient, that's good; but if not, repeat one more cautery on top of it, for it is customary for the cautery to be moved close to the affected limb. Therefore, you must continue with the cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	Of bonesetting
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	The menses are aided sometimes by cautery with great help, and especially the disease that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. When you see someone cauterizing, be careful if the disease is at its beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not descend or remain, and you doubt that corruption may spread throughout the illness, then make five cauteries on top: one in the middle of the forehead, and another towards the front at the end of the eyebrows; and two on the two horns, and one behind on the back of the head; and leave your hand there until the cautery reaches the bone, and until the scabs come out so that the vapors of the thick humors can escape from them; and cauterize on the muscle according to what is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the bonesetting is spread out everywhere and it clearly appears, then you must cauterize it with these cauteries that we have said on top of the head, and one on the nape of the neck, and two on the spine of the neck, and six on the spine of the back, and one large one on the ribcage and another near it, and two on each shoulder; and two on the ribs, and two on the tendons of the breast, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and be careful not to burn the nerves that are located on the back of the calf; and sometimes make a cautery on the bone of the wrist, and one on the bone of the stomach, and one on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And know that the more cauteries you make, the greater help you give and the more profit it brings; and know that the sick person does not feel any pain from the cautery as a healthy person would, because the body is already completely corrupted. And the cauteries should be large and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you will find in the manner of the irons. Afterward, cure the place with flour of millet with honey and other remedies until it is healed.
de enfleure	Here is how to treat inflammation:
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	"When swelling occurs in any limb and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, but is not yet gone, then apply cauteries to the limb according to its size; let the cautery be slightly penetrating into the flesh around the heart. Then treat it with ointments until it is gone. Sometimes a cautery is also performed on the hand, foot, back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the limb, and thus the swelling is removed. Nevertheless, no one should undertake this unless they are knowledgeable about the limbs and the exits of the moving nerves in the body."
de albaras	"of Albarus"
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	"When the disease called 'albaras' has begun and medical remedies are of no avail, then cauterize it with a slightly penetrating cautery according to the amount of flesh around the heart until the whiteness is removed and its color changes. Then treat it with flour of vetch and lentils mixed with rose oil, plantain leaves, pigeon's blood, and almond milk, each in equal parts; mix everything together, tie it up in a cloth, and apply it to the affected area until it heals."
li cure de chancre par cautere	"Treatment of Chancres by Cautery"
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When a chancre appears at the beginning and you see it stop, cauterize it with a cautery that resembles one circle, all around the edge of the chancre. But also, learned people say that one should make a cautery in the middle of the chancre; but this does not seem good to me, because I fear that it may be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen this happen before. And it is more appropriate that it be cauterized around, with the cautery called 'circule', as we have said concerning many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of swelling that cannot heal
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has an illness called "adubelati", which takes a long time to heal, either because of the excess it causes or because of the water in the patient's body when they are elderly (that is, too old) and have little blood, or because of the weather; if you see that it is hastening to heal: then cauterize it around with many small cauteries in prickling fashion; afterward, leave it thus. For it will hasten to heal itself
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see that it is piercing all the way through the cautery, then heat the cautery which has this shape:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And place your hand in the middle of that illness called "adubelati" until the cauteries have pierced through to the heart, and make the cauteries such that the patient feels drawn toward them in such a way that the course of corruption is relieved. Afterward, treat him until he is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the treatment of fire with iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another way of illness exists which is called "corrodens", and it is nothing other than a devouring of limb, for it consumes limbs just as fire consumes dry logs. If you see this disease in a place that can withstand cauterization with fire, then heat the small and large awl-shaped cauteries according to what is necessary for the place where the disease is located; afterward, cauterize all around until you have removed all corruption, so that nothing remains of it, and everything that is corrupted has been taken away. And then leave it for three days, and put on the cauterized places powdered with oil until the burns from the fire are removed, and all corruption. Afterward, treat with fleshing ointments. And if after three days healthy flesh does not appear, it is good; but if not, then recommence the cautery on what remains of the corrupted places. And this devouring has sometimes been cured with hot medicine in place of fire cautery; but nonetheless, fire cautery is of greater help, and I have already said the cure with hot medicine in the division: take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of warts that come on the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Very often, a disease called "callus" according to our understanding comes on the feet from without, and it is a large, flawed thing that bleeds on the foot. And there are two ways of cautery for this disease: fire cautery and hot water cautery.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if they are turned by defluxion away from the body, and this happens often in hands and feet, then you must bring cautery of hot water there; and it is done thus: take a tube of brass or iron, or a feather of a goose, and place it upon the nail and the cuticle, that is to say for warts. And place the tube upon so that it encompasses all around, then put some hot water within, and hold your hand well, and press your hand in turning so that the edge of the tube comes to the root of the nail, and may find the deep path of the hot water even unto the root; and let the patient endure a little the biting of the hot water for an hour. Then leave it thus, and it will deroot itself entirely with all its roots. Thus do one after another, until you have derooted all those that are on the body, then dress them with ointments that generate flesh.
li cure dou trembler	The treatment of trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone is trembling from coldness of the nerves, or from quartan fever or other [cause], you must perform four cauteries on them: two between each spine on the back, one at the foot, and one on the stomach near the navel. This will cause the trembling to cease and their health to be restored from the cold illness.
des pustules puans	For pus-filled pustules that smell bad
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Sometimes it appears on the body, bathing hot, or putrid pustules, which come from large corrupt matters. So when they first appear, one should perform cautery on each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery of myrtle wood, of which the point is held in fire, or of long Aristolochia root, or lenticular cautery. And sometimes they cauterize at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow further from then on, but the superfluities whence they come are disrupted, and they become clean; however, this should be done after blood evacuation.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there are great flows of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes from without, or at the incision of the boil, or at the cautery of the limb, and similar things; and it is very difficult to stop.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And nevertheless when this happens to anyone, so you should quickly put your two index fingers on the wound of the vein, and press very hard until the blood is pacified beneath your fingers, and that no drop comes out; then put on fire several olive cauteries both small and large until they are all red; then take one, either large or small according to the wound and where the artery is cut, and put the cautery on that vein where you hold your fingers, and hold the cautery there until the bleeding stops.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps out when you lift your fingers from the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, so take quickly another one of the cauteries that are on fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease doing this one after the other until the bleeding is stopped; and be careful that you do not burn the nerve that is nearby, and that no other harm comes to the patient; and know that when blood flows from the artery, it cannot be well stopped, especially if the artery is large, unless by one of the four ways that we have said: either by cautery, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by tying with a strong thread, or by medicines put on that have power to stop bleeding; and let it be tied and tightened appropriately.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Which will bring about stopping of bleeding is tying very tightly with rags or putting hot things on top, or similar things, if it profits little or not at all.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and he does not have a doctor or medicine present, so he should put his index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and press very hard until it is stopped above the wound and above the vein; and do not move your finger, but moisten it with cold water often that it be very cold until the blood is congealed and thickened and stopped; and then do afterwards what is necessary with cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of the surgeries of wounds
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all the diseases where it is necessary to cauterize with fire or with burning medicine, and the cauteries, their causes and instruments and forms; and I have put that chapter at the beginning down to the feet, and I will go in this chapter by the same way so that one can find more easily what one wants.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And before I begin this one, dear friend, it is necessary that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first one about cauteries, and therefore it requires greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there are many times evacuations of blood when opening the vein and cutting on an aposteme and in treating wounds and extracting splinters and cutting on stone, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many people die from it.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	"Yet I advise you not to undertake folly. For many kinds of people come seeking treatment, some who have become so attached to their illness that they die easily due to the frenzy they find in their disease, and from the severity of their ailment; one must fear these."
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	"And there are those who give their sense and say: 'Wait, I am healed'; yet the disease is deceitful. It does not behoove you to consent to those who come to you with this manner, but place greater consideration in your honor than in your greed, and do not open foolishly, but wisely, concerning those of whom you are certain, and from whom you may have taken and received praise; and use prediction and indication in the treatment of your patients toward their recovery, and this will help you achieve good reputation, glory, and the memory of praise."
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	"Dear son, May Our Lord grant you good understanding and uprightness, and if it pleases Him to inspire you with the holy breath of His hand, Amen."
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	"I have arranged this chapter in sections for you to consider, according to what is before the chapter on cupping, which I have outlined from beginning to end, so that you may find more easily what you will need."
dou chief plein d’aigue	"full head of water"
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this illness often comes to children at birth, and when the mother holds the child's head too tightly; sometimes it happens due to some unknown cause.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this illness outside of children, and in all those that I saw the bite healed quickly; therefore it seems to me that it is best to leave such cures alone.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw one child whose head was full of water, and the swelling increased each day so that it could not be supported; and the moisture became so great that it burst, and this moisture collected beneath the bone above the spine, between the heart and the bone; and the operation is such that if the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the swellings are small, you should cut a gash in the head, wide enough; and let it be as long as two fingers, so that the moisture may run out. And here is the form of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture has grown more and the swelling is larger, then make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and you see signs that the angles of the head are raised on each side, and water flows out when you press it with your hand from within, and this has not been answered: then you must make three incisions in the head according to this manner
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after the incision, draw out all the moisture. Afterward, compress the incisions with bandages and powders, and put wine and oil on them, and leave it thus for five days; then untie it, and dress the wound with tents and ointments, and let the head be bound evenly, and give the sick person dry food of broth made from the moisture until the member is strengthened and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another manner of incision is that you observe where the swelling of the aposteme and the gathering of water appear; for sometimes it appears before, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Therefore cut where the aposteme appears and the gathering of water, and make the incision according to what you can manage; but be careful not to cut an artery; for if it bleeds, then the sick person dies from the loss of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	de reume
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to someone that they have a disease called "catarrach" in the ears or the nostril, and the disease is chronic, and treatment with medicine does not help, then the last resort is to use cauterization along with cutting the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you cut the veins, it is necessary that the sick person leans back their head; after that, rub the place with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then wrap the sick person's neck tightly with one cloth; after that, observe where the vein runs, and the places of both are behind the ears, and close to each other; then mark the places with ink, then cut both with a sharp spatula in two parts, so that the incision comes down to the bone, and is as wide as the breadth of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, put the spatula under the artery and cut it above, cutting also like two fingers across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, then blood flows out continuously upward.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not appear to be felt, then you must measure the quantity of space between three fingers, then mark with ink and cut down to the bone; and this is how much blood should come out: six ounces, and perhaps a little more or less depending on what the sick person can tolerate, and the fullness of the artery. Then examine the wound: if there remains a point of the syphac on the bone, then cut it off so that no aposteme comes from it; afterward compress the wound and bind it, and treat with ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	de emigrainne
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When chronic migraine comes with severe catarrh and moisture from tears, and heat in the temples, along with long-standing madness and similar things, and even though medical treatments are used, none of them help, then cut the arteries of the temples and cauterize, as we have described.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of extracting them is that the sick person leans back their head and observes the artery that appears in the temple, for it beats visibly, but may be less so in some people who are too cold. And if it is hidden, then the sick person wraps their neck with several cloths; then rubs the place with a rough cloth, and rinses the place with hot water until the artery appears clearly. Then take the spatula which has this shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	Then lightly scrape the skin until you reach the artery; then lift it up with forceps and separate it well from the tissues that are underneath each part. And if the artery is small, turn it with the point of the nail, then cut off one part according to the quantity of two fingers' width. For if it is not cut, then all the blood will not flow out completely.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	"And draw six ounces of blood, up to three. And if the artery is large, then you must tie it in two places with a strong doubled silk thread, so that putrefaction does not come before the wound closes, and there are no bloody discharges; then cut away the excess that is between the two ties at this very moment, and then, if you wish, cauterize with the cutting cautery up to the bone until the head is severed. And this is the main work, if the patient has no fever and is of hot complexion."
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cautery helps to finish off moisture: therefore it is more helpful for dampness.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	And for the extraction of arteries, it is necessary that one fill the place with old cotton and put on well-made dressings; and when they are untied, care should be taken to cure them with dry medicines which cause flesh to grow, and dressings, until they heal. And if blood flows from the artery every time you work there, then hurry to cauterize with the cutting cautery, or fill the place with vitriol and press it with your hand so that the blood stops flowing; and if this is not present, then put your thumb on the place until the blood congeals, and wash the place with cold water until the blood ceases, and constrain it as necessary. And what is masterful and easier for extracting an artery is to cauterize the vein of this cutting cautery in two places, but let the cuts be well spaced to preserve their heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the material is too thin, it retains less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And there must be one inch of space between the two knives, and then when you have marked with a hot iron on both places, and you measure the glowing iron so that it comes up to the bone, and cut the vein in two places; and let them be distant between the two cuts because this cautery is not continuous throughout. And this is the form of the cautery.
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When tears flow from the veins that are above the forehead of a fever patient, and there is no profit from any medicine applied there, and you see the face of the sick person reddening, and feel on the forehead a trembling as if from shivering; and if the eyebrows are thin and moist so that the hairs of the paper (eyelids) fall out, and the eyelids are heated and burned by the heat of the tears, then this treatment is needed.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And they called this treatment in the past "concussion cure," and it is done by making three incisions on the forehead of the patient with this illness who has hair there: one incision as long as two fingers in the middle of the forehead going downwards towards the nose, and the other two incisions are each two fingers apart above the eyelids, and take care not to cut the arteries that are located at both sides above the eyelids; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two jaws, and let each wound be the size of three fingers wide.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	and have ready a piece of sponge and many cloths to wipe away the blood, then take the spatula heated in two places as shown here:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision that is drawn from the temple to the second incision; and scrape away all the heart that is between the two slits up to the soft tissue that is on the bone, then do likewise from the middle incision to the other second one, and then remove this spongy material.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you insert the tool called "cultellarium" into the first slit, it is very sharp on one side and not sharp on the other side. This is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And direct the cutting edge of the tool towards the flesh near the heart, and the blunt edge towards the bone, and push it in until it reaches the middle slit. And cut all the vessels that descend from the head down to the feet so that the incision is continuous right up to where the heart opens, and then do likewise in the middle slit up to the other side; and then drain out the blood evenly, and press the area to stop any bleeding. Then place a bandage of soft cotton in each slit, and cover it with cloths moistened in wine, oil, and rue, and make sure that no pus forms there; and on the third day untie the stitches, and apply a great quantity of watercress, then treat it with basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other treatments for wounds until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	This is an extract from "Le Grand Chirurgie" by Guy de Chauliac
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	If it happens that catarrh comes on suddenly, and you see the eyes thin and small, and weakening of sight, and burned papers, and hair falling out, and there is deep pain in the head, and the sick person sneezes; then know by these signs that those matters and that catarrh come from many veins, and the cure for it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And the treatment is to make the patient lie on their back, then make a large incision in the middle of the forehead and another one wide enough. 1 inch. And begin from the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision go down to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves that move when eating; and once the bone is uncovered, wipe out all the blood with a sponge, and then open up between the two lips of the incision and place old cotton and linen bandages there. Then tie on top cloths moistened in wine and oil, and make sure no hot abscess forms; when it has healed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to form, then treat it with drying agents that encourage flesh growth.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take 2 parts of wheat flour and 4 parts of colophony, and make a plaster out of it. And apply it to these wounds to encourage flesh growth throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	The term "estoupement des oreilles" translates to "stopping up the ears." Here is an example of how this phrase might be used in context:
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of four things:
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When a stone falls into the ear or some other thing that does not fit in the ear nor grows there, then place the ear towards the sun. If you see the stone, then distill a drop of violet oil or sesame oil, then use tweezers for extraction; and when the sneeze occurs, make him sneeze with condition, and stop his nostrils when the sneezing comes, and wrap around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and hold the ear above. Many times fire comes from this treatment; and if it does not come from fire, then extract the stone with fine tweezers, of which here is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps out with tweezers, that's good. If not, then extract with a fine, small hook; and if it does not come out with this, make a reed of straw and stick the end of the reed into the earhole hard, and stop what is around the reed with soft wax so that wind cannot enter with the reed; then blow fire strongly, for often fire comes thus as we have said; and if it does not come from fire in such manner, take glutinous substance which birds use, and put some of it on an instrument that is pointed for this purpose, and put a little cotton around it; then press the glut on the stone or whatever thing it may be, and blow fire.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not come out from all these things that we have said, then hurry to cut the ear before inflammation and spasm comes, and the manner of cutting is thus: first bleed the patient from the cephalic vein according to his strength, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn his ear upwards, and make a small crescent-shaped incision in the root of the ear where it hangs; and let the incision be as large as you can get to the stone, then remove it according to your power, and suck it quickly into your mouth; and continue the treatment until he is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it's a grain that is inside and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer one thin, subtle spatula according to this shape:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	"Make an incision of that grain. But do not do this when you think the grain is moist due to ear moisture, until you have cut off many pieces; then extract it with fine tweezers and tongs, as we have said, so that the extraction is easy."
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	"Therefore, when water flows into the ear, the patient must use sneezing first and plug the ear with plenty of cotton. And they should lie on that same ear where the water is. If it comes out by itself, that's good. But if not, take many pieces according to the length of your thin and light fingers, heat them a little over the fire; and the patient puts one into the hole of his ear, and sticks out on the other side, and puts another piece on top of the piece that is in the ear; and keep doing this from piece to piece until all the water comes out, and thus it should all come out; And if you see, take a reed and put one end into the ear, and hold the other end near the fire until the end of the reed is burned; then repeat with other reeds until all the water comes out, as we have said about the pieces."
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	"For the removal of the animal, if it is small-bodied like a flea or similar thing, treat it as we have said in the division. But if it is large-bodied and can be felt, bring tweezers for its removal; this is the easiest thing to remove from the ear."
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	"For the removal of earthworms from the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the division and in the chapter on distillations, and if the treatment does not help, then you should examine the ear in sunlight: if any worms are visible, remove them with fine tweezers; but if they are not visible, take the tube made of this shape:"
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.
