Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	"And let it be narrow below and wide above. And put the most subtle end into the ear according to the size of the patient's suffering, then suck strongly on the entire tube; do this often until all the worms come out. And if they refuse to come out, stuff cotton around the tube as I have said in the chapter on stones; and if they still do not come out as we have said, bring distillation remedies that ancient doctors have proven effective against worms, which you will find in the chapter on distillations; and use this instrument to distill your oils and medicines into the ear, of which this is the shape as you see:"
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	"And let it be made of silver or thin brass with a small hole below and wide above for distillation. And for pressing inside the distillation, use an instrument well-made for this purpose. And if you wish to take one razor and wrap cotton around its tip carefully; then pour your oil or juice into the tube along with whatever medicine you desire, and place the tube in the ear. Then insert the razor with all the cotton into the ear and press gently with your hand until the oil is distilled into the ear. And warm the patient's ear beforehand, and let the distillation be done in a small pot warmed over the fire before being distilled into the ear; and make sure it is not too cold, for the medicine would not then be as effective."
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Chapter: "The Stopping of the Ears"
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without a hole in their ears; and the same applies to adults due to injury or flesh grown inside the ear, which sometimes goes deep into the ear so that it cannot be seen; and sometimes there is one little opening that can be clearly seen.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, that which comes deep inside so that it cannot be seen is difficult to treat in many cases. And in the case where there is an opening visible, you should place the patient's ear towards the sun and look inside: if you see any polyp appearing, then perform the operation described below:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	"And let it be sharp and cutting both before and behind, full, so that it does not wound the ear; if the prolapse is of flesh born in the body of the ear, hold it with fine forceps and cut it lightly, until all that flesh is removed."
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	"And if the prolapse is deeply within the ear, take a fine, sharp razor and heat it slightly over fire, then apply it to the body of the ear. If you feel the prolapse where the patient feels pain in their hearing, pierce it lightly, taking care not to injure the nerves of the ear; then place a gauze according to the width of the opening into the ear, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment."
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	"Continue this process for several days until the wound is healed. Then take a gauze and moisten it in rose water, powdered vitriol, and apply it. If you see swelling of the ear, then remove the gauze and replace it with another gauze moistened in cerote made from rose oil and wax, until the swelling has gone down; then cure it until it is healed."
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	"And if there is discharge of blood, take a sponge and wring it out in cold water, then place it on the ear. Use other remedies that stop the discharge of blood, which are found in treatises on distillations."
de la char des papieres	"What is written on the paper"
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	"This is the remedy that comes from paper of the eyes when they are moist and dried out. It is necessary to stretch them with tweezers and forceps, then cut it with a scalpel at its roots; then apply powdered vitriol."
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	"And if a thread of blood oozes out, then cauterize it with a lenticular cautery and cut it afterwards. This is more effective than cauterizing first. And often repeat this process until there is nothing left of its roots; for when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not grow back."
de la gresle	"Hailstorm"
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	"Many times pieces of paper come with things like hailstones in their shape and hardness, and therefore this disease is called 'hail'; it is a gathering of thick moisture on the paper above and below. The treatment is as follows: ensure that the hail does not move from one side to the other, which is easy to know; then make an incision wide enough, then carefully scrape each part, then take it with tweezers and cut it. If you cannot cut it without piercing the paper a little, it doesn't matter for the patient; and if the crack is large, stitch it up and heal it until it is healthy; but if it is small, do not use force, as ointments will restore it quickly and inwardly."
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	"And if the hail is descending into the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper over, and grasp the hail with tweezers and cut it on both sides; and if the paper is separated by the incision, it does not matter; and when the hail has been cut, rinse the wound with salt water, and heal it inwardly until the patient is healthy."
de la graisse des eulz	Here's a possible translation for "de la graisse des eulz":
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Eosinach is a substance that enters into the fabrics of papers above, and this happens more in children than in adults, greatly afflicting their eyes; it brings them catarrh in the mornings, and they cannot look at sunlight because tears rush to their eyes; therefore they often lie on their faces and sleep like that, and their papers are under their eyebrows wet with fluid, making the swelling and appearance covered with eosinach which opens into the eye. And when you press below there with your fingers, you feel the eosinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of removing it is as follows: the patient puts his head in your hand; then takes one linen cloth and prepares a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that contains eosinach from each part, then places it on top; and presses with his fingers on both sides so that the eosinach is gathered within the circle; then makes in the middle of the moistness with the sharp spatula a cut as wide as the wound made when bloodletting, and cuts the skin deeply until you reach the eosinach; and in several positions comes out eosinach from the cut, resembling the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then take out with one piece of lint gripped between your fingers behind, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is dispersed; and make sure that you do not stuff in the cut, but wipe all the spatula up to the eye without cutting or hurting it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if eosinach does not come out at the beginning of the cut, then gently widen the cut a little until it appears; then remove it as we have said above, then moisten cloths in hot water and cold water, and place them on the wound, and press with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there are men among them who grind salt and place it on the wound to corrupt the moisture that remains; then treat it until it is healed. And if a hot ulcer forms at the wound, then treat it with soothing emplasters until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	hairs from the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs appear on the papers mixed with others than their natural ones and are entwined, they harm the eyes and cause diseases such as habitual tears, softening of the papers, and albugine, to such an extent that it causes destruction of the eyes. And there are four ways to treat it: either by cauterization with fire together or by hot medicine according to what is before or after cautery, and it can be done either by incision and suturing or by tweezers, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must put the patient's head in your hand, then turn the paper from the eye with your left hand; if it is folded over, that is good; if not, then insert a needle with one thread on top. And whether it is near the edge of the paper or where the hairs are growing near those hairs, and pull one thread upwards along the entire length of the paper, and turn it towards the razor; then make an incision underneath the paper, below the hairs attached, with the spatula cutting from the large pupil to the small one. Then remove one thread, and place a small tent made of cotton and cloth under the paper, then press on the paper in the shape of a cone, like a mortar pestle, and nevertheless it is necessary that the shape be according to the quantity that you see lifting up the paper which is divided into two parts.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	"Then for those who need it, cut a large quantity of the paper according to how the paper is softened; then make a cut all along the lines that you have marked on both sides, and start from the larger line towards the smaller one; and let one of the cuts be near the natural hairs, as thick as a root; then insert the needle into one of the two angles of the heart, then pull it through entirely; then join the two lips with a stitch using a needle with one thread of fine wool, and wipe away the blood, and make the superfluous threads stick together on both sides with any sticky substance if you see this being done; but if not, do not worry about it, then leave the stitch and the threads for three or four days; then dress the wound without stitching using dry and constricting substances, because paper revives at the joining of the wound and its assembly, but stitches are harmful (as the ancients said), and this is done without fear."
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	"And if there is another way to do this: And it is that you mark the paper with a shape like the leaf of a myrtle, as we have described, with three points diverging according to the shape shown below:"
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	"Then cut that which is above the small forces equally according to the shape shown below:"
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	"And if you lack power to hold the forceps, and the thing is not even, then take a needle with one thread, and place it within the figure; and place another thread beside the large ear, and the second thread beside the small one, and assemble between your two hands the threads evenly; then raise your hand evenly, and raise all the skin upon which you have marked, as we have explained, then approximate the two lips of the wound by suturing, and treat it until it is sound; and if an abscess forms at your incision, soothe it with cerote and similar soothing ointments."
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	"And sometimes it happens that the hairs of the paper become inverted. In such case, you must use what we have said about incision; but the suturing in one and the other is more complicated."
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	"The treatment of the canals is as follows: Convert the paper and make the slit within it according to what I have said, then make two fine canals by art equal in length to that of the paper and the width of the spatula; cut at both ends where you hold the threads. Then join one thread evenly onto that which lies above the paper of the eye, and strain both canals tightly from both parts; leave it thus for several days, and the skin that is strained will harden, darken, and shrivel until it adheres."
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	"If it takes too long, cut it with some force, and treat it until it is sound; and when the wound is healed, and the paper has been removed, the hairs will no longer point; this is the form of the two canals that you should make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:"
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	"The operation is as follows: Take a fine needle and thread it with one thin, soft silk thread; then join the ends and tie them evenly, making the length of the threads a palm's breadth. Then take another short, fine silk thread and tie its end to the threads; then the patient should place his head in your hand, and be near the sun so that the operation may be clearly seen, for it is a delicate and subtle one. Then insert the needle throughout the canal into the root of the hair, joining it, and pierce it quickly through the paper until you draw it out above the natural hair; then pull the hair up to the canal, and place it in the canal if there are one or two or three or more hairs; then withdraw your hand so that all the hairs come out of the canal into the paper with the natural hair."
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	"And if the canal is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, then pull the canal downward along all the thread that you have ordered, until the canal comes out of the hole above and you can see it through the vision of the eye; then pull out the canal and the thread, close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair settles in its place and flesh grows over it. And if the hairs are small, accompany them with a long natural eyebrow hair, and raise it with that one which you leave, until it is separated and then lift it."
de la porriture de l’oil	"Treatment of eye inflammation"
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease called 'aleacrati' or decay comes to the eye, there are two kinds of it: one natural, and the other unnatural. And it occurs suddenly from a wound, or from an incision or cautery, and from similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the manner of working on it is that you should cut this joint and open its lips, and put linen wicks inside, and leave them until it heals; and you should not use in its treatment things that dry and constrict. For if you do so, the illness returns worse than before; but rather use softening things, such as fenugreek; and rose water or altar water and linseed cooked, and applications of diacylon melted in some oil, and wrap it with a wick, and treat it thus.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your treatment are that you should take care that it does not heal in its former shape; and these works that we have mentioned serve only to prevent this illness from returning in its former shape.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes into the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This disease that is underneath is truly called "axacrati", and it is natural and accidental. The accident comes from wound or cut and cautery and things similar; and the way of working on it is that you should take a needle with one doubled thread, and insert it into the flesh, and make it pierce from the left eyelid so far to the right that the threads come out in two holes of the flesh; then stretch the flesh above all the needle, and cut it with one broad spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper returns according to what it should be, that is good; if not, then take a razor and put it in the cut, and twist the paper, and make two cuts on either side within the paper; and let the holes of the two cuts be at the two angles of the incision that you have made, and make one angle such that when they are assembled, the figure is like the figure of the letter "gamma" in Greek; then remove that flesh according to the quantity that its sides are gone underneath, from what covers the paper, then join the two separated parts, and sew them with a wool thread; then treat it as we have said with softening medicines and bandages until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from cut or suture or cautery, it is necessary that you make one full cut underneath the hairs of the paper, and according to what has been said before; then separate between the two leaves of a bandage, as I have said; and one should do the work according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and wise masters arrange various devices with all their power to make the figure return to its natural shape; and the sick person himself, according to what is necessary for treatment and instruments in many dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the suddenness of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this soldering occurs in many men in such a way that the paper above is stuck with egg white, and cannot move nor perform its natural tasks, then you must insert the point of a razor below the paper and lift it up; and stretch it with forceps until you cut what is attached to the spatula's tip, which should not be too sharp nor too cutting, so that the patient can bear it if the spatula is too sharp or cuts the eye; and let your incision, from which you scrape off this assembly, be light, so that the paper returns according to its natural form; and all of this assembly is healed, and sometimes they make in the eye salted water, and lift it with fresh water and collyrium; then place a linen bandage between the paper and the eye, and put wet wool moistened in egg yolk on top of the eye; and after the third day use collyrium and compresses until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	Of the angle of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the angle is of two kinds: one is nervous and resembles a hard, dry skin, and another which is not nervous but resembles moist, congealed skin, such that when touched with iron and tried to grasp with forceps, it cannot be done; both of these semblances begin towards the large tear gland and gradually increase until they cover all of the eye's vision and movement.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is as follows: the patient puts their head in your hand, then opens their eyes; and lifts the paper with your hand, then grasp the angle with small-forceps double, and stretch it upwards; then take a needle, and put one horsehair or cow hair or ox hair on it, along with some strong thread; and double the point of the needle slightly and insert it into the angle, and pierce through with the whole needle, and tie the angle with a thread and stretch it up, and scrape off all around the angle that surrounds the pupil and the sclera up to the top, then cut the remaining part at the root of the tear gland using the spatula subtly and small-forceps, leaving the natural flesh of the tear gland so that by the incision tears do not flow in their accustomed manner; and sometimes stretch the angle with tweezers only, and thread, as we have said; then scrape it off entirely with a soft spatula.
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the spatula does not touch the delicate tissue and break it, nor pierce the pupil; and after the incision sprinkle some crushed celandine into the eye, and use collyrium made of litargire, leaving it overnight; then cure with whatever is appropriate until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the angle is not nervous and you cannot insert the needle and tweezers cannot enter, this semblance of angle is often cured with medicines; and as I have described in the division, it appears that there are several kinds, and if you see one cut open, then open the eye of the patient and take a light spatula slightly bent in this manner:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And gently lift the angle upwards and if it does not seem to thin out and you see that the reason persists, then distill from your mouth into the eye collyrium made of litargire and red collyrium and crushed celandine, and stop up the eye overnight; then recommence the other operation according to this same manner until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there is any obstacle in the eye that prevents you from operating, such as a hot aposteme, then use milk first and cure the hot aposteme until it is healed; then recommence the operation as before until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh of the tear gland causes great harm to the eye, then suspend it with tweezers and cut off a part of it but not all, so that tears do not flow there; then distill red collyrium made of litargire into the eye.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	And about the flesh that grows on the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	Sometimes in the eyes of some people red flesh grows and covers the pupil and restrains upon the papers and turns towards the forehead, resembling a pomegranate flower; and the operation is thus: the patient puts their head in your hand, then opens their eyes and grasp all that flesh with suitable tweezers and holds it firm with forceps; then cut off the first layer of flesh and continue cutting until finished, taking care not to wound the eye during the operation; and let the incision be made by the spatula which we have mentioned in the incision of the angle and use small-forceps to remove the sebaceous material, as shown in the figure below.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	And when the incision is complete and all the flesh has been removed, then fill the eye with crushed celandine or distill red collyrium and similar corrosive medicines into it, and put cotton soaked in egg yolk on the front of the eye so that it is secure from hot aposteme; and if anything remains and hot inflammation arises and you suspect a hot aposteme, then leave the eye alone and cure the hot aposteme with things that calm hot aposteme; then return to your operation until it is healed, and do likewise for any flesh that grows in the eye in this manner.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nonetheless it is necessary that you alleviate the cure of each weak eye by the natural way; and by the artificial way, in surgical operation with iron tools; and do not put your hand into any of these operations unless you see that these members are able to withstand this operation.
des voines des eulz	And about the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	The veins that are red and cover the eye are called sebaceous veins, which hinder vision and weaken the eye every day. It is therefore necessary at first to examine whether the eye in which sebaceous veins are present is healthy, and if there is no other visible disease besides sebaceous veins; then grasp them in this manner: tell the patient to put their head in your hand, then suspend those veins with tweezers according to your judgment, using double-ended subtly bent tweezers in this shape:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And hold two tweezers by degrees on one body according to this shape:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then carefully squeeze those delicate veins,
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot collect all this in one hour, then apply a plaster to the eye of things that alleviate the pain of the eyes, and let it stay for several days until the pain is alleviated and an abscess is formed, then resume according to this method which is stated beforehand until he is healed; and this is the form of the treatment:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	Physicians call a "fistula" an "arissati": when you cure it with cautery and with medicine that is hot and burning according to what I have said before, and it is not healed, then there is treachery in it. You must cut open the abscess where it must burst, and draw out all the moisture that is inside until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed and you see corruption and blackness, then bring everything from the instruments that are present here according to this form; it is called "aspre chief" (sharp knife) and should be made of iron with a point like a chisel as shown in its current form
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it on the site of the corrupted bone, then twist it between your fingers and press with your hand until you know that all the corruption has been removed. Do this several times, then return the site with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the site is healed and flesh grows, and the body of the bow is healed, and remains like this for forty days, and it does not renew itself nor form an abscess, and no bad accident occurs, know that it is healed. But if not, then there is no other recourse but to bring back the fistula to the opening of the nose according to this method: you must uncover the bone a second time with iron and hot medicines, and when it is uncovered, take one drill in this form, and let the head of the iron be at three angles, and let the shaft be attenuated up to the head as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the bone near the eye socket and hold your hand away from the eye a little bit, then twist the drill until it pierces the bone and you feel that the sick person's breath comes out. Then return to the site with drying medicines as I have taught you, and when flesh grows and the site hardens, then the matter will go to the nose. This is easier for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	About the issue of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the eye opens entirely and nothing disturbs it nor diminishes its size, then you must bind the patient. Then rinse the eye, then place cupping glasses or hot jars without burning to suck out matter, then put on the eye a linen made of aloe, acacia, incense, and sarcocolle, then strain the eye with bandages and cloths in this manner: take soft cloths, double each one four times, then place them on top of each other according to how much the eye needs; then strain it with a firm bandage from above, then restart the cupping glasses to suck without burning. Then remove the cups and leave the eye strained day and night. If the linen moistens too much, you must change it often. Then remove the linen after the day and night, and if you see that the eye is improving, that's good; but if not, then restart the bandage and linen and cups until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	About the bursting of an ocular vein
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a disruption occurs in the ocular vein and opens up and paper comes out like a grain of resin, it is frightful to see. Then if you want to cover it, the procedure is as follows: take a needle and pierce it into the root of the part below until it reaches the part above, then take another needle with one doubled thread from the part by the eye socket; pierce this through and leave the first needle in place according to its position. Then sew up the site with the doubled thread and tie one part of the vein around it and strain it well, then remove the needle and place on the eye damp linen soaked in egg albumen. Leave it until the thread sticks with the vein, then treat the eye with comforting substances until the wound is healed. And sometimes the wound is restrained by the vein on each side with a circle of cloth until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye becomes greatly inflamed, then pierce it with a subtle spatula that comes out from the back of the eye and corrects the moisture of the albuginous humor and lets the eye descend, and enter into it quickly. Then remove it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	About the brow of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This ailment called "alcunnati" is nothing other than a vein that has assembled in the eye, resembling descending water, yet it is not water; and the manner of its appearance during operation is thus: Make the patient sit on one prepared and straight seat, then take the head between your hands from both sides, and move the muffler until you see the vein rise up towards your eyes; then prick it in with a needle, and do not allow it to descend nor let any light enter, and have the patient view things as they used to. And if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the descent of the vein is not aligned as we have said, then make the patient sit between your hands, then take the spatula and cut through the corneal cloth one point along the continuity of the conjunctiva with the cornea and the crown until the vein comes out; and when it has come out, distill warm water mixed with honey into the eye, or water in which fenugreek has been boiled and mixed with honey, then treat it with another cure until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	Water of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have the likenesses of waters in division, and those which it is necessary to pierce; so we do according to health. It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the light of the sun, and close the healthy eye tightly; then place the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eye is left, or in your right hand if the eye is right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eye is right; then place the point of the instrument near the crown by the thickness of a thread in that blenchor of the eye at the part towards the lesser lacrimal, then push the instrument called "almagda" gently and turn your hand until it pierces into the blenchor of the eye, and feel that almagda reaches the empty space; and it is necessary that the measure of the way of almagda be to the depth of the measure of the space which is from the pruneole until the end of the blackness; and this is the crown of the eye; then you will see the bone in that paper through the clarity of the corneal cloth, and then place the instrument up to where the water is, then press it down one way after another. If the water descends now, then the patient sees before them and the instrument in their eye.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After a short rest, if the water rises along the second way, place the finger with the instrument, and when it is well inserted and does not rise, then withdraw almagda gently by turning your hand little by little; then put back into the water a bit of red silk, and remove from this eye inside. Then place over the eye compresses or moistened wool in rose oil and egg yolk, and tie with the healthy eye. Nowadays, we and those of our time place over it finely crushed cummin with egg yolk.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have very hard eyes, then you must take the instrument called "alberit", of which this is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And therefore pierce only the conjunctiva and not too deep, but make a subtle cut, then place almagda as we have said; and at the completion of the work prepare for the patient a pleasant bed, on which he sleeps on his back in two dark rooms; and let him be deprived of all movements, and take light foods, and not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and let him be tied according to his condition up to the third day; then untie him in that same dark room, and test his sight, and show him some things, and then retie him for seven days; and it is not necessary that you do this during the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you do this, because the water rises hastily.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	If any inflammation occurs, then untie the eye before the seventh day, and apply to it the remedy for soothing inflammation; and when it is soothed, then uncover the sight and place on its face a compress to cover it for some days, and let him remain in that same dark room. And then let him come out little by little, and turn back to his house; and know that no disciples should meddle with this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from Jericho, who told us that in some country they make almagda pierce the eye, from which they suck out the water, but nevertheless I never saw any such thing in our land, nor did I ever read about it in books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the likenesses of the forms of almagda, so that those who do not know them may see them, and they should be made of pure silver:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	"And their heads of these same subtlety are two, and one behind has three angles."
de la char sor le neis	"of the flesh on the bones"
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	"Sometimes various flesh joints are born on the bones, some of which resemble scorpions with many feet. And there are some where the flesh is colored like fire, and there is soft flesh of bone color. Therefore, in that flesh which is soft and not fiery-colored, you should make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; open their nostrils, and apply oil to those joints and rub them vigorously. Then cut off as much as you can hold with the spatula with its sharp edge on one side until you know that all the flesh has been removed."
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	"And if there remains anything that cannot be cut off, then open it with one of the light and sharp instruments so that nothing remains. And if it swells or becomes inflamed, then treat it as is necessary; but if it is malignant swelling, then hurry and cauterize until the blood stops flowing, and all the flesh has been removed, then apply oil or vinegar to the bones."
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	"If the bone opens and moisture reaches the palate, know that it is healthy. But if moisture does not reach as it should, know that there is newborn flesh in the bone above; then the instrument will not come for cutting: therefore you must take a thread of linen, somewhat thick, and wet your hands with it, and have between each knot a doit or less. And the patient puts the head of the thread into his nose with some force, and draws it in smelling until it comes through the nostril into the mouth; children at school often do this, and it is easy for whoever wishes to do it. Then hold the head that comes through the nostril with one hand, and the other head that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and know which ones are on the thread in turning towards you. Do this until you know that the knots have rotted that flesh; then pull out the thread, wipe away the blood, and moisten it in Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the nostril as before. Do this for three days or more, until the ointment has corrupted all that remains of the flesh. Then put a bandage of plaster on it for some days until it is healed; if it needs drying medicines, use them. And this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, by which one distills oils and medicines into the nostrils:"
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	"And it should be made of silver or bronze, resembling an open lamp like a tube with its conduit likewise; and if you wish, make a closed tube, and the instrument full for purging the head; and let there be many holes at the top to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid."
de la char sor le neis	To remove flesh from the nostrils
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	"Often there appears on the head of the nostril a disease called "telul", which grows and becomes large so that it is visible to look at; therefore you must cut it off at the beginning and remove all of it, then put on it the cautery or the burning medicine. And if one waits too long to cut it until it has become large, take care if it is hard, of dark color, and poor sense; do not touch it with iron for it is an engrained swelling, because when it is cut, great mischief comes upon the patient. But if the swelling is soft to touch, not of dark color, and you see that it can be completely cut off, then empty the nostril and cut it without fear, and cure it afterwards with drying and restrictive things."
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nostril is cut and cauterized
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	"Know that when a fissure occurs in one of these cartilages it profits little, except in some men. Therefore, whenever this happens to someone, you should see if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then sew up the two lips with stitches, and cure it until it is healed. But if the lips are already separated on both sides, you must cauterize all the parts of their skin until they are dry, then sew up the two lips together with stitches, and tighten them, and sprinkle over them powder of dragon's blood and crushed incense; and put over the powders a piece of strong plaster or another adhesive plaster, and let it adhere for some time, then cure it with ointment until it is healed."
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	"The manner of stitching is that you sew the wound together: either with needles, as we have said in abdominal suturing; or with thread, as I have told you."
des apostemes des levres	Of the swellings on the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many men have within their lips hard abscesses, resembling grains of millet, small and large. Therefore, you must turn the lips, cut into each nodule, grasp it with forceps and cut it in every part; then apply powdered vitriol after the incision until the blood is stanched. Then apply the ointment of Aesculapius, and dress the area with dry things until it is clean.
de la char des gencives	Of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times fleshy growths appear on the gums, which the ancients called "albulus"; you must hold them with forceps and cut at their root, allowing the vein or blood to run; then apply powdered vitriol or other restrictive and drying powders to the wound; if this flesh grows back after the incision, which happens often, then cut it again and cauterize it: it will not return after the cautery. These are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	Of boils
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes escarps appear at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, which are ugly and sharp; sometimes the teeth are black and yellowish-green and worms come to the gum, causing foulness; therefore you must make the patient sit between your hands with their face in your lap and scrape away at the escarps until nothing remains; do the same for blackness, greenness, yellowness, and other stains until they are all removed; if what caused them is removed first, that is good; otherwise restart on the second day and continue on the third until everything has been scraped off; know that teeth require various forms of instruments for scraping according to the task at hand, as those used to scrape between teeth differ from those used to scrape around them; have all these forms and others ready with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you are treating a toothache, it is necessary to wait before extracting until the pain has ceased, for one should never perform such an operation while the patient is in pain. For it is a delicate matter that requires great skill and offers no excuse for failure.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Therefore, when the patient is suffering from a toothache, it is necessary for you to be certain about which tooth is causing the pain. Many times the pain may seem to be coming from a healthy tooth, and the patient might have it extracted believing that will relieve their pain; however, the pain does not disappear after this incorrect extraction, as we have seen happen too many times already. Therefore, once you are certain about which tooth is causing the pain, make sure to scrape all around it with a sharp spatula to protect the gum on all sides. Then grasp the tooth firmly with your fingers or use forceps to apply pressure gently at first, until the tooth is well loosened; then secure the forceps tightly and hold the patient's chin in your lap between your knees so that they cannot move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, if it does not come out easily, use any of these instruments and insert them gently into each side of the socket, wiggling them as you did before. If the tooth is pierced and movable, you must fill in the hole with wadding where the piercing is located; then extract it carefully with forceps so that it does not break during extraction; afterwards, work gently around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	Be sure not to break the tooth during extraction and be aware that leaving even a small piece behind can cause greater pain for the patient due to the root remaining. Beware of acting like ignorant surgeons who, in their haste and recklessness, sometimes break the socket and fail to follow the procedures we have described. They often cause serious illness by leaving roots or breaking the socket, as we have seen happen many times before. Once the tooth is extracted, rinse the area with wine, vinegar, water, or saltwater; if bleeding occurs, which is common, sprinkle powdered vitriol on the wound; if that does not work, cauterize it with a hot iron.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments used to extract teeth should have long points and thick handles so that they do not bend when extracting a tooth. These are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	"And let them be of heavy members so they do not bend at all during the pulling, and let them be of good iron well-made, and let them have teeth for holding moves."
de la racine des dens	"from the root of the teeth"
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains in the tooth, then you must place on the wound cotton moistened in butter for one or two days until the area is softened, then insert the pliers called "algefri," making them inside like a file, this is the form.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these pliers, then you must uncover the flesh all around the root and place the instrument called "althali," that is, tweezers, this is the form.
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And it should be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out, this is good; if not, then help yourself with all the instruments, these forms come later.
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this instrument which has two handles, this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are placed on the surface of the teeth, and this instrument resembles large pliers, here is its form
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And these instruments should be strong enough not to break, and know that there are many dental instruments; and also other instruments which are not counted. And the wise master finds his instrument himself according to what his works and the disease show him, for there are such diseases where the ancients did not teach any instrument because of their diversity. And if one breaks one's cart or other bones where it could be useful, then one searches among the instruments that are necessary, as I have told you, and helps with gestures, this is its form
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And they should be large and hold well to hold the bone so that it does not escape but can grasp and remove it. Then restore the place with appropriate medicine, and if there is rot in the bone and it is small, then remove it with all this instrument
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When teeth appear not according to their natural shape, and their form is ugly, especially in young women, then you must know if the tooth is close behind the tooth and not in its proper place, and one cannot set it right or file it: then scrape it; and if it is against the tooth, take this instrument whose form is like a small beak and has iron pointed at the end
