Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And gently tap with your hand every day for the hardness of the tooth and so that you do not move the others. And if it is apparent so that one can file it, then use a file like this whose form is like
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the file used to make needles. And gently file the tooth little by little every day so that it does not move too much until it falls out. Then smooth it at the end with any plane and if the tooth is too sharp and cuts the tongue, then file off its sharpness until it is even enough not to cut the tongue nor corrupt speech
quant li dent lochent	When teeth lock
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When front teeth are locked together, either from a blow or fall, and the patient cannot bite down on what they eat without it hurting, and you have treated them with constricting medicines but they don't work, then you must constrict them with a gold wire because silver wire turns green and decays. And let the wire be medium size neither too thick nor too thin according to the space between the teeth. If you see that the teeth are crooked, take the wire and double-ended pliers between the two healthy teeth, then insert the ends between the loose teeth if there is one or more until you carefully reach the healthy tooth on the other side. Then start covering it again up to where you started, and hold your hand gently and steadily so that they do not move. And let your knot be at the root of the tooth so that it does not escape. Then cut off the ends of the wire with pliers and join them together between the healthy tooth and insert it in such a way that it does not hurt the tongue. And then leave it as tight as possible for as long as it can stay, and if it comes loose or the wire breaks, then tighten it with another wire. It will last like this all its time, here is the form of the teeth and the figure of the arrangement of the two healthy teeth and the two loose ones as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, it should be replaced in its place little by little as we have said. And only those who are wise and skilled should undertake this task, and sometimes they make the shape of a tooth from cow bone and put it in the place where there is a gap and tighten it with wire as we have described, and it will remain in place for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cut the frenulum of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Sometimes the frenulum of the tongue is present at birth or due to an injury from a wound. The procedure is as follows: open the patient's mouth and have them tilt their head back while you lift their tongue with your finger. Then cut the nerve with scissors along the frenulum until the tongue is completely released from its attachment. If there is hardness or callus present, due to a healed wound, use an needle and cut along the frenulum. Be careful not to cut too deeply so as not to harm the artery below. After cutting, rinse the area with rose water and sage or cold water and place a linen bandage underneath the tongue each night to prevent reattachment of the frenulum. If bleeding occurs, sprinkle powdered vitriol on the wound. If bleeding continues, cauterize it with a gentle cautery iron, then treat the wound with other appropriate remedies until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it is of dusky color or black or hard, but the patient does not feel it, do not touch it because it is a chancre. And if it tends to become an ulcer and there is moisture present, then use a needle and make a small incision with a sharp scalpel and remove it from both sides. If bleeding occurs during your procedure, sprinkle powdered vitriol until it stops bleeding. Then continue your procedure until all the flesh is removed. Then rinse the area with sage and honey and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Throat abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Sometimes swellings called "godaths" appear in the throat, which are properly called "aphthae," and there are two types. If they are hard, dark-colored, and of small size, do not touch them with an iron instrument. If they are red and have a large root, do not touch them with an iron instrument either, especially if bleeding is present. Instead, wait until they burst on their own. If they are white, rounded, and have a fine root, then prepare your instruments to cut them out, but first make sure that the swelling is warm and calm. Then have the patient sit facing the sun with their head in your lap, and have them open their mouth while you insert your fingers between their teeth and press down on their tongue with your other hand, as shown below. Use a thin, sharp instrument made of silver or brass:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can you press the tongue against all this instrument? And when you see the boil, take the lancet and insert it into the head of it, and twist it up above as much as you can; then draw out some of the cloth with it, and cut off the instrument, of which here is the shape, resembling a crow's foot; and its ends are curved, one towards the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, then use pincers, of which here is the shape
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And let it be sharp on one side and pointed on the other; and when you have cut off one of the kernels, then cut off the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle with hot water and salt-water, and if there is any bleeding, gargle with water in which pomegranate skins have been cooked, or myrtle leaves, or similar things, until the blood is stanched; then treat it until it is healed. And sometimes other boils appear in the throat besides the two kernels, so cut them off likewise as you would the two kernels.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I treated a woman who had a boil that had grown inside her throat, specifically one small boil; it had almost completely closed off her throat so that she could not breathe because the passage was blocked, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if left like this for one or two days. The boil had grown so much that there were already two needles stuck through its two openings. I therefore acted quickly, and inserted a lancet into one of them, then twisted it outward and drew out a large portion of bile; then I repeated the procedure on the other opening of the boil, opened her mouth and pressed down her tongue; afterwards I inserted the lancet into these boils and cut off a part of them, but only a little blood came out. And thus the passage of the woman's throat was opened up, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I kept cutting away at this boil for a long time; it would always grow back again and fill in the space that I had cut open, becoming very large; finally I cauterized it inside her throat: thus it remained without growing any further; and I left these parts, and do not know what God did with her afterwards.
de l’uve	The eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When the boil appears on the eyelid and it is swollen and elongated, it is called “perpendicular”; if it is below thick and round, it is called a “stye”. When it has been treated as we have said in the chapter on division, but the treatment does not help, and you see that the hard boil has healed, and it is thin, then you must cut it off; and one that is round and assembled and not elongated. And it is blood red or dark colored or black, then you should avoid cutting into it. For there is great danger to the patient in this case. Therefore, when you see it, according to its size and length, you should have the patient sit before the sun, and press their tongue with the instrument we mentioned earlier; then insert the lancet into the eyelid and draw it downwards and cut off one of the two instruments that I mentioned in the chapter on cutting kernels. And make sure not to cut more than the natural limit of the eyelid; for if you cut more, you will harm the voice and speech. And after the incision, use what we said earlier about the treatment of kernel boils, until it is healed. And if the patient is afraid of being cut, then you should use cauterization with a thin hot iron. The manner of cauterization is as follows: Have the patient put their head in your hand and press their tongue with the instrument mentioned in the chapter on cautery or with tweezers; then heat it with very hot water so that it is not too thick nor too clear, and apply the pointed end of this instrument carefully to the boil, of which this is the shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it has at the top a small vessel where one puts the medication, like the horn of a spoon, and puts the instrument with all the medicine on the eyelid; and the patient should lie on their side so that saliva and mucus flow from their mouth away from the medicine and the eyelid, so that it does not reach the throat and cause swelling. Then hold your hand over the medicine and press it onto the eyelid for about half an hour until you see that it is darkened and the bites of the medicine are calmed; and if necessary, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, wet the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument with all the cotton into the canal above until the cotton touches the eyelid; do this often until the cauterization is complete, then let it dry and fall off after 4 or 5 days. And if you need to start the cauterization again with the medicine, then restart it, and afterwards wipe around the eyelid with cotton soaked in oil, and clean what is around the medicine; and rinse with cold water and gargle until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more gentle than cutting or cauterization. If it is treated with fumigation in this way, take calamint and hyssop and origanum and rue and camomile and chamomile and similar herbs, and mix them all together or some of them into one pot; put a little incense inside, and make it boil; and the pot should be well sealed with earthenware, and there should be one small vessel like this inside the pot:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And whether it be of silver or bronze, and whether one of the heads is placed in the mouth of the patient until the vapor reaches the boil through the tube, until the boil is killed; afterwards it should be begun again frequently, until the boil dries out, and ensure that this is not done at the beginning of the appearance of a hot abscess, for many things can happen there; and do not do this unless it is towards the decline of a hot abscess. And if this instrument is not present, then take a tube and put an egg-shell at its end so that the patient's mouth does not get too hot; for the egg-shell lets out vapor without scorching the mouth, and this is good treatment together with health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times, a bone or fish spine, or some other thing, gets stuck in the throat; therefore you must pull out what you can see, and press the tongue with the instrument so that you can see it move; and whatever is not visible and is stuck in the throat, you must make the patient vomit before the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps then the thing will come out through vomiting; or the patient has swallowed a piece of sponge, or a piece of flaxseed, or a root of lettuce, or one morsel of dry bread; and tie a thread to the sponge, and then swallow it; and when it reaches its place, it will be visible, and then pull it out; and if it does not come out from what we have said, take one instrument made of lead according to this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at its end so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have its end raised up high; and take care not to touch the epiglottis, lest the whole thing go down, nor push the bone in too far; and it is better for the patient themselves to insert the instrument, for they will know where the thing has lodged itself; then draw it out gently along the entire length of the instrument until it comes out completely.
de la sansue de la gorge	de la sansue de la gorge
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	The blood is treated, as I have said in the division, with the cure of medicines; and when this does not help at all, then look into the throat of the patient towards the sun, after you press the tongue with the instrument that I have told you about. And if you see the blood clot, then draw it out with a small hook or with fine forceps which are suitable for this purpose. And if these do not suffice, then take a heated awl and insert it into the throat of the patient, then insert one hot iron at the end of the awl, and do this often. And if the patient continues to spit water all day, then take a full cup of cold water, open the mouth, and pour it in without letting him swallow, and move your hand about; and as soon as the blood feels the water, it falls.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafoetida using the instrument that I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will fall without trouble. And the manner of fumigation is thus: take one pot which has live coals in it, and let the pot be covered with a cloth pierced in the middle, and let the hole of the tube be placed over the opening; then throw your fumigation onto the coals, and let the patient put the end of the tube into his mouth, and close his mouth so that no smoke escapes but goes all the way to the blood clot. And now the blood clot will fall, and if it does not fall, then recommence the fumigation many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty foods and salted things, and drink no water at all. And then it will be necessary for it to come out by this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one treats the blood clot is this: when it can be seen, it resembles curved tongs for entering into the throat; and it has the shape of a crow's beak, and has sharpness like a file, so that whatever it takes hold of, it cannot let go. And here you see its form:
li chapistres des apostemes	Chapter of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	There are many kinds of abscesses, as remembered here from one and another in this book, and they are divided into two types: perforation and incision; and there are two ways of being similar to each other, the first is by its own appearance, and what it holds moisture. And the second way is for those places where they are on the body, because the abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and the abscesses of a fleshy place are different from those that come in joints, and each one has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	"And so there are abscesses that one should not pierce until the bowels have fully died; and there are some such that must be pierced when they have grown hard, even if they do not die according to their course, like abscesses near joints. For when an abscess forms near a joint, and it is left alone until it becomes putrid all around, it may happen that the ligaments and nerves of the joint become corrupted, which causes contraction in that limb. But if the abscess is by the principal member, and you delay piercing it until it has fully died, it will harm the principal member; but if it is near the fundament, one should pierce it before it dies. And one must not pierce a hard abscess without completing digestion first, except for the one near the fundament, lest it burrow deep down and become extended inside, and a fistula forms that cannot heal in a short time."
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	"And you must know the hour for piercing an abscess that has died according to its course, and this is when the pain has ceased, and the division of the fever, and the decrease of the pain and redness, and from bursting and sharpening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and you must make the piercing lower down where the abscess depends more, and where it opens most; and let the piercing be long like the body of a finger, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints near nerves and arteries, and in all smooth places where there is no wrinkle."
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	"And in those that are wrinkled, according to the shape of that member. And when an abscess is in a hard place, it is better to leave piercing until digestion is complete, as we have said before. For if you pierce it beforehand, the body of the venom will be extended from it and will be full of much filth; and perhaps its lips and depth become hardened. And there are some abscesses that must be pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the members need. And you must make small holes in small abscesses, and large holes in large ones, with many cuts according to the size of the abscess; and there are such abscesses where one must press the heart and cover it when it has become as hard as a dried fig and is softened, then one must do as for boils. And there are some that are cut into three angles, and there are some whose covering is like the skin of a walnut, like abscesses in the armpits; and there are such where one makes a round incision, and other incisions and similar cuts."
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	"Those that have no head, like soft superficial abscesses, must be pierced plainly. And when the abscess is large and has swollen greatly, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus at once, but draw out a part; then stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw out some more again; do this many times gradually, until all the pus comes out, especially if the patient is of weak virtue, or pregnant woman, or small child, or old man decrepit. For the spirit may sometimes jump with the issue of the pus, and perhaps the patient dies, and you are not aware of it. Therefore beware of this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, examine the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a plain cut, then prepare lint bands or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess and there are many holes, then it is necessary to put in each one a bandage so that they come together; and if you have cut off a part of the skin in the abscess and have sewed it around, then it is necessary to fill it with dry cotton or linen cloth shavings without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then remove it, and cure it with ointment until it is healed."
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if bleeding occurs in your operation, then prepare cold water and a vessel, and moisten one cloth, and put it on the place where the bleeding is occurring many times. And if the bleeding continues, then bring treatment and care, and the powders that I have said for the hands in this book, and if it is in wintertime, and the place where the abscess is very nervous, then it is necessary to put on wet lint bands and cloths in hot wine and oil; and if it is in summer time, and the place is fleshy, then it is necessary to put on wet lint bands and cloths in cold water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said before; then untie the abscess and wipe it clean and cure it, as it should be, until it is healed."
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	"And this one must know universally in the cure of abscesses: I have told you how one should proceed with the cure of abscesses, and here is that chapter."
des soros	Here are some translations of the word "soros" from Middle French to English:
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	**Line-by-line translation:**
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And cutting into an abscess that is hard and moist, it is easier, for they have little blood in them. And there are some of these abscesses on the head where there is no moisture, and of those abscesses I once saw one on the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess just like a hard, rough, and white stone, and could not be broken; and if one had cut into it, one would have made as good a wound as from a stone. In other abscesses coming to the head, except for those which come to the heads of children and at the roots of the ears, the opening should always be made at the lowest place possible, so that the bowels may exit; and they are treated as is necessary.
des scrophules	scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Many times these abscesses occur on the neck, and below the buttocks, and also in the angles, and sometimes they come elsewhere on the body, and they are many, and they are interconnected with each other. And each scrofula is properly inside its own skin, like the nut and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and the appearances of these scrofulas are many. There are some that contain moisture, and there are also malignant ones that do not want to obey treatment. Therefore, in one that you see well disposed for touching, and is similar in color to the skin, and moves from each part and is not hard against the nerves of the neck nor against the artery nor the duct, and is not deep; then it must be cut through on top, and scraped from each side, and the two lips of the heart are opened at the angles if you have need, as we have said for abscesses of the head; and drain it little by little, and make sure that you do not cut into the nerve nor the vein, and do not use a spatula or cutting instrument, so that the hand does not slip, and do not go too deep, lest you cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut into the vein or the artery, and it does not allow you to work, then put in the wound powdered vitriol, or some powders that stop bleeding, and compress the wound; and leave it until the abscess is appeased, and the wound begins to soften and start to decay. And when the blood is stopped, then return to your work until you finish it. Then search with your index finger if there remain any small scrofulas, and cut them out and clean them. And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrofula, then it is not necessary that you cut into that scrofula at its root, but tie it off with a strong double thread, and let it fall by itself without harm; then dress the wound with soft cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cut out the entire scrofula, then it is necessary that you bring together the two lips of the wound and sew them up immediately, because there is no remaining excess for the size of the scrofula. Then it is necessary that you cut into the root of it, and draw out pus, and sew it up as we have said. Those scrofulas that contain excess matter, pierce where it appears more open; and pierce in this way as the one mentioned earlier, depending on it, then bring it tents with ointment and similar things, so that it rots what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, then dress it with ointment between the flesh until it is healed.
de squinance	de squinance
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and wrote about the operation of cutting a throat, but I never saw it done in our land, and that is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have quinsy, it is necessary that the opening of the throat called "epiglottis" be cleared; and one does not receive help through this, for all the veins and the vessels of the patient are hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in two glands.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the vessels, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid suffocation which comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is therefore necessary, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, that we do so below three circles or four, a small cut across between two circles or by the amount of the cut in the soft palate, not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and this area is so connected to the epiglottis that there is no flesh there, and the vessels are long in length.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the master is fearful, then he should stretch the skin of the throat all around the onyx, then cut the heart until it reaches the chin; and avoid the blood vessels, if you see any, and then cut the soft palate as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the section of the pharynx that jumps forward through the area that has been broken, and by the loss of voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open a little.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour of doubt about strangulation has passed, bring together the two lips of the wound in the heart and sew it up entirely without the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause flesh to grow until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that one should not do this until the throat is completely blocked off, and the patient is judged to be near death, and his breathing has failed.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Therefore, cut the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus death is prevented.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	And therefore the ancients commanded that the wound be left open until the worst of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And then they commanded that the wound be sewn up and cured until it was healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a young woman took one knife and stabbed it into her throat and cut part of the arteries of the lung.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to heal her, but found her already dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found that the blood issuing from it was not from the veins or arteries but only from the throat, and the breath was coming out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried and sewed up the wound and treated her until she was healed;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	"And it happened to the maiden that she was hoarse of voice, and afterward returned to her former state."
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	"Therefore I say that in the cutting of the epiglottis there should be no fear."
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	"This type of swelling is called 'throat hernia' and appears as a large, dark purple swelling, occurring most commonly in women;"
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	"And it occurs in two ways: naturally, or due to accident; or else by nature there is no cause."
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	"And accidents occur in two ways: one resembles fatty tissue, and the other resembles swelling that comes from an artery;"
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	"and there should be fear, especially in the case of small ones, where it is necessary to operate carefully and examine the entire cavity;"
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	"If you find it like a fat nut and not attached to any vessel, cut it like a fatty tumor, and remove it completely if possible;"
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	"And search everywhere carefully, and treat it as necessary until it is completely healed."
des nous	of fatty tumors
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	"There are many kinds of tumors, all of which I will describe in detail;"
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	"And now it is necessary that I explain the difference between a fatty tumor and an abscess."
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	"I say that an abscess is hot and feverish until the suppuration has passed, at which point it becomes filled with pus, and then the fever and heat subside."
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	"With a fatty tumor, there is no heat, fever or pain, and it contains sebaceous matter within its own sac, appearing in the same color as the skin, beginning like a pimple and becoming larger;"
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	"And there are two kinds of fatty tumors: fatty or moist, with many appearing in the colors mentioned earlier."
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	"When treating a fatty tumor, it is necessary to first examine and express the contents using an instrument called the 'intromittor', according to the shape described in the following chapter."
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	"The method of examining an abscess in a fatty tumor is to press gently on the most moist area you find and twist your hands slowly until you feel that the instrument has pierced the skin, then proceed according to the size of the abscess;"
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	"then remove the intromittor carefully, taking care not to let anything spring out."
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	"If moist corrupt matter flows out, whatever its color may be, incise it as described for other abscesses;"
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	"But if no moist matter comes out after using the intromittor, know that it is fatty, and then incise it in a cross shape, grasp it with forceps, lightly scrape off the skin on each side, and remove the fatty tumor along with its capsule without tearing it."
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	"And if you cannot remove it intact, then take it out in pieces until nothing remains."
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	"For if anything is left behind, the fatty tumor will grow back many times;"
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	"and if a little bit remains and the skin becomes inflamed, sprinkle some aqueous corrosive powders on it, apply pressure to the wound, apply a soothing poultice for hot abscesses, and treat it with other remedies until it heals completely."
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	"And if the fatty tumor is large, cut around its edges like two lips of the wound, and treat it as one would a wound that enters flesh."
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	"And if a vein is beating nearby or another complication arises, quickly apply powdered vitriol to the area, leaving it on for two or three days until the wound becomes suppurated and the inflammation of the blood subsides, then return to remove any remaining fatty tumor."
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	"Here are the shapes of intromittors: there are three sizes - large, medium, and small. There are also four square ones called 'albarets' and one round one called a 'breb'. There are also three sizes for encircling fistulous abscesses;"
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	"and they are like needles used for cauterization, made of brass, iron, or silver. The yellow ones are the most valuable, and blackened ones are more suitable for encircling fistulous openings;"
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	"and they come in three sizes - large, medium, and small - according to the size of the opening."
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	"The shapes of forceps are very similar, as you can see here: large, medium, and small. There are also forceps with two openings, available in three sizes;"
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	"And there are forceps with three openings, also available in three sizes. There are also forceps with two openings and those with a single opening, both available in three sizes. All of these are necessary for their respective uses."
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	"The tips of these instruments used for cutting are sharp. There are also some that only cut on one side, which are used to scrape fatty tumors so as not to injure veins or nerves;"
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	"And among these intromittors are the tweezers that can be placed in one's hand so that the patient does not notice them during the opening of abscesses;"
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	"and they come in three sizes - large, small, and medium - as you can see;"
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	"but they are only used for fine work, such as legs, arms, breasts, angles, and similar locations;"
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	"and sometimes another small instrument resembling a fistula probe is made in this shape, used to staunch bleeding:"
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	"And it is sometimes placed at the location where veins and arteries are severed or where there has been excessive bleeding. Sometimes they are made in this larger size:"
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	"Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to decay, making them resemble women's breasts;"
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	"and remain unsightly and swollen, and anyone who wishes to treat them must follow the shape of this line B up to G;"
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	"then scrape away the fat, apply a medication for wounds that penetrate flesh, then bring together the two edges of the wound to suture it closed, and treat it until it heals."
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	"And if the breast hangs down and is soft due to its size, like those of women, then make two incisions above it, resembling two slits;"
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	"So that one incision is connected to the other at their ends, with the larger line containing the smaller according to this shape, from line B to line G;"
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	"then scrape away the skin between the two edges and remove the fat. Then proceed with suturing and applying powders as mentioned earlier, along with any other necessary treatments until it heals."
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	"And if it does not heal, or if the incision was not complete because the patient would not rest, or due to bleeding, then you must fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment;"
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	"And leave it until it consumes the remaining skin and fat, then treat it until it heals."
des apostemes des asselles	"Abscesses of the armpits"
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	"The abscesses that occur under the arms are usually hard tumors resembling scrofula or have rough surfaces, and some contain moisture."
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture must be cut according to this shape, from line b to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the boil has been drained out, then fill the wound with soft cotton, and leave it until the next day. Then remove all the cotton and dress it with an appropriate ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the boil resembles scrofula, then cut it as we have said for scrofula wounds, and if the wound fills with pus again, then apply a cauterization as we have described before.
de la routure de l’artere	rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When an artery is ruptured and the skin above it is closed, many boils often form, and the same occurs with a swollen vein and boil;
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if one recognizes it thus when it is for the artery, then the abscesses are long and deep
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when you feel it with your fingers, then there is one sensation of pressure; and when it is for the vein, then there appears red swelling
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is folly to cut this abscess, especially when it is under the buttocks and hips and neck and in many other places, where it is very large
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	Therefore, surgery with an iron should be avoided, and the one at the head must also be avoided, and in the case of swelling from an artery, cut through the skin above the length
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then open the incision like a mouth, and carefully separate the artery from the tissues until it is exposed
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	then place a needle underneath it and pierce it until the other side, and tie the artery with a doubled thread in two places, as I have shown you regarding the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	then pierce the place between the two ties with an intromittent until the pus comes out there, and let the abscess be opened
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	then dress the wound so that it drains freely until the tie falls off
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then treat it with ointment appropriate for this wound until it is healed
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	And if the abscess is on the vein's course, then you must stretch your hand from what you can reach of the abscess to all the skin,
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	Then place the needle underneath the spot you are holding with your hand, and pierce it so that there is one doubled thread, which you then draw from the other side.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	Then sew up the boil as I told you to, or tie it with one of two threads from either side.
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	If you doubt that the thread has gone too far, then insert another needle with one thread under all of the boil at the incision of the first needle, and tie the threads in four places.
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	Then cut off the boil until all the excess comes out, then cut away the excess from around the heart and leave what is tied.
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then place a cloth moistened in wine and oil upon it, and thereafter apply dressings and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of boils on the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Similarly, just as boils come to the artery and vein, so too do boils appear on the nerves when they are injured or from excessive exertion, etc.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And these appear most often on the joints and toes and in all places where there are articulations; they are painful boils, their color resembles that of the skin, and they have many different aspects without pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	And when it is squeezed firmly, the sick person feels pain, but it is not deep in the flesh, rather under the skin.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	"and moves well on all sides,
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And he who is at the head or forehead makes the skin like a sieve.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the boil is small, take some tweezers and grasp it at its root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is large, suspend it with a needle and lance it, then remove it and sew up the wound until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	of hanging warts
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	Sometimes it happens in bellies and not elsewhere, and is a disease called "fungus" because of its resemblance to them, and the roots are thin and the heads are large; there are some small ones and very large ones;
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	And I saw one man who had two in his belly that were more similar to mushrooms than anything else, and there was no difference between them; they were white, had fine roots, were already split open, and moisture constantly flowed from them.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I weighed them and found that one weighed 18 ounces, and the other weighed 6 ounces. The appearance of the incision indicates whether the patient is moist; the color of the flesh is white and moist with fine roots.
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	"If you cut into the shoulder blade widely, and if the fire cautery is present at that time, then be prepared for many excessive flows of blood during the incision. If bleeding overcomes you, then promptly proceed to cauterize."
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	"And if you see the patient afraid and fearful of the iron incision, then take one well-made linen thread, tie the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days;"
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	"And then tighten it again and continue to pull the linen thread until it cuts through the artery without causing injury. And if the roots are large, be afraid to cut them even for the abdomen, but you can safely cut half of it,"
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	"Then cauterize it so that it does not return. Then dress the wound and make sure you do not cut the thele (udder) which is of dark color, poor sense, and produces milk."
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	"For this is an incurable tumor, and I will discuss the treatment for cancer later on."
quant li boude ist fuer	"When the wound has healed"
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the swelling appears due to cauterization of a wound or rupture of a sinew, and it is on the belly and affects some of the bowels as happens in other lacerations, or from blood flowing from veins or arteries according to what comes before, or from windiness;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	And if it is due to the rupture of the sinew and the bursting of the bowel, then the color of the swelling appears like the color of the body, and there is little pain or opening from various places.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the bursting of the intestine, then it becomes more diverse; and when it is pressed with two fingers it sinks in and then returns, and sometimes it is hard, and greatly enlarges at the entrance of the anus during difficult labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to moisture, it is light and opens well when pressed by hand, not constricting at all; but if it is due to blood, then the swelling appears large and hard with these signs, and is fixed in place according to its quantity.
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to windiness, it is soft to the touch, and its appearance shows whether it is due to arterial or venous blood, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	It is necessary that you leave the treatment alone. For there is doubt and fear about it, as I have told you in the chapter on swellings, concerning the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if its appearance is due to the intestine or the bowel, then you must order the patient to extend their arm straight out and grasp the swelling all around with your hand;
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	then have them lie down on their back between your hands.
puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile,	Then go around the area that you have marked with your fingers to all sides of it,
puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	Then they cut off half of the abscess from above with one stroke.
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	Then they tie it tightly around with strong thread or silk string and make sure the bone is healed;
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	Then open the half of the abscess that has spread over the bandage, insert your index finger into it, and search for the intestine.
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	If you find it wrapped around the bone, untie it and put the intestine back inside the abdomen;
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	And if you find the bowel, take it with tweezers and cut off the excess.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	And if the artery or vein is against you, carefully go around it, then return to your work and take two needles and thread them with two strong threads, and sew around what you have done in a cross stitch pattern.
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	Then squeeze the abscess at four places above the needles and if necessary remove them, leaving it alone until it can rot away on its own; cut off any dead flesh.
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	Or you may cut it when it becomes soft and rotting, then cleanse the wound as necessary and dress it according to what we have said.
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And remove any blood or moisture that you find, then cleanse the wound and sew it up.
dou chancre	Of a chancre
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have spoken in the section on the signs of a chancre and how one should treat it with medicines, and how to avoid surgical treatment. Now we will discuss a chancre that is spreading to the marrow and requires great caution in its treatment. The ancients said that when a chancre appears where it can be scraped off like those found on the breast or hip, then all of it must be removed at the beginning; but if it is large and old, one should not approach it because I have never seen anyone heal from one, nor have I heard of any such case before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the operation is performed where it can be removed, as we have said, it is done thus: first purge the patient with black colic; then make them vomit if they show signs of repletion, and prepare the patient a good place to perform the operation. Then grasp the chancre with tweezers and cut it all around and remove it completely without leaving anything behind.
