If it is from thin mucous membrane and it is close at hand on two leaves, then hurry and round it off: put together your two index fingers, and have the woman lie on her back with her legs spread; then stretch the two leaves strongly until the thin mucous membrane is rounded out over the obstruction; then take wool soaked in oil, and place it on the leaf, and have the woman lie on her stomach each day so that it cannot stick together. And if the mucous membrane is hard and thick, then you must cut it away with a scalpel like a laurel leaf. If the obstruction is from born skin, then suspend it with tweezers and cut it away; and have medicines to stop bleeding such as aloe, dragon's blood, incense mixed together with egg white; then apply a wide plaster of lead so that the wound cannot stick together; and do this for a long time, and apply a tent of dry linen; then treat it with other treatments until it is healed. And when skin grows in the womb, you must cut it away according to this manner, unless it is enchanted black spots. For one should not touch an enchanted spot that is in the womb out of fear.
des emorroides	Emorroides est une maladie de la partie postérieure de l’anus et du périnée, causée par une dilatation veineuse ou un hémorragie de ces veines. Les symptômes incluent le saignement lors de la défécation, la douleur dans la région anale, et des masses dures à cet endroit.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	**Translation:**
des apostemes de la marris	Of boils of the anus
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	Many kinds of boils come in the anus, such as cancer and hard boils and herpes and hemorrhoids and fistulas and hot boils, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division. Therefore, I must say in this treatise about the hot boil that comes in the anus, which is not one of those boils that grow outside; and if you want to know how to treat it with iron, look first to see if the boil is hard at the beginning of its appearance, and full of heat and fever, and becomes red if you can see it. Then do not hurry to pierce it, but let it soften until the pain is eased; and then make the patient sit on one seat, with two small seats where he can lie down, and support his back and assemble his feet at the level of his thigh; and his thighs should be spread apart, and put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good bandage; then suck out the bag toward the right side, and bring the instrument with which one opens the mouth of the anus, about which comes later its form; and it is necessary that when you want to introduce this instrument, you first stick in the probe to know the depth of the anus, so that what enters into it does not go deeper than it should, nor burn the patient; and if the instrument is too large, it is necessary to cover the depth of the anus with cloths, so that the instrument does not hurt him; and he must put the funnel of the instrument on top, and dip the instrument. And when the boil opens and you can feel it with your hand, it is necessary to catch it at its head with a spatula; and when the bag is emptied, it is necessary that you put wet lint soaked in rose oil or green oil in the wound; and put the lint at the bottom of the anus, and put some more on top of the anus and on the linen cloth moistened with water where mallows have been cooked; then treat him after two days with ointment suitable for this purpose until it is healed; and sometimes lift the anus and the wound by washing with water and honey, and then with water in which lily roots and long aristolochia have been cooked; then go back to the ointment. And if the wound closes up in the anus, you must be careful not to cauterize with iron, but treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	Childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	It is first necessary that the midwife knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the sign is when you see the woman rush downwards, and desires to smell the air; then the child hastens to issue forth; then know that this birth is according to nature's figure, and the afterbirth is under its head, and the membranes with it. And when you see these signs, so it is necessary to press her belly lightly, so that the child issues quickly; for when it settles on its head, so is the afterbirth with it, and the mother is cleansed of her superfluities by good cleansing. And he who comes otherwise does not come naturally; for sometimes he comes on his feet, and comes forth the body or the head, and the hands, or he comes on his belly, or sometimes, and is turned perhaps over his neck, and through other evil figures; so it is necessary that the midwife be wise and subtle in these things, and guard herself from error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one must help her.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes on its head through natural issuance, and the woman labors with grief, and her strength is weak, then make her sit on a stool, or let women hold her; and arouse her nature with oil of olive or fenugreek cooked, and then put the midwife between her thighs the little spatumile of which here is the shape:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And cleave the afterbirth, and cut with your nail so much that the moisture which is within comes forth; and take hold of the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then you must cleanse the woman with a suppository of fenugreek with oil of sesame. Then make her sneeze with condiment, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now the child will be born. And if the two hands come forth first, then you must draw them back little by little, stroke by stroke; and if they cannot be brought back in, then put the woman on a stool, and lift up her feet high. Then turn the stool upside down on the ground, and take hold of the woman so that she does not fall with the turning. And if the hands still cannot be brought back in, and the child dies, then cut the hands at the wrist which is herefore placed, and draw out the child, and draw them back equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	And when the child comes forth on its feet:
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the child comes onto its feet, then one must raise it upwards;
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	And then turn it bit by bit until it is even
puis preigne .i. des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	Then take one of his feet and stretch it bit by bit
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	If he can jump up to the hips, then command him to grab it and make him sneeze
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	if he jumps, God willing
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if he cannot jump as we have said, then turn it bit by bit until it is in its natural shape
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is easy
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons dit, si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en .i. mortier;	And if he cannot jump as we have said, take mastic of aloe, oil of sesame, and molten gum, and grind them all in one mortar
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement,	and put this mixture on the nature of the woman inside and outside this ointment
puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	then make her sit in warm water up to below the ribs
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai .i. coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when she is moistened underneath, make her a wreath of myrrh and put it under her, leaving it for an hour
puis la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	then make her sit on a seat, then make her sneeze and press her mouth and nose, and gently take hold of her belly, for the child will now jump
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	From the outlet of the child onto his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the child comes in this form, then gently put your hands on him bit by bit
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor .i. lit;	then support him on his neck, and let his feet hang down, and let him lie on a bed;
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and gently fold his hands bit by bit, then put his hands on the belly, and remove the cushions underneath him until she is ready below
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if the child does not jump, then take his feet and move them suddenly, then move his belly upwards, then put your hands in
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	Pull out the child bit by bit; and tell the woman to push as hard as the child comes out
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	From the outlet of the child who comes from the thigh, keep one hand
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	I must engineer to bring back the hand
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if it cannot be brought back, then make the woman stand up and go away
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus .i. lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	if she cannot walk, then make her lie on a bed, and forcefully separate her legs
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then apply the mastic I have spoken about;
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	and if she does not give birth, then make her sit on a seat, then study how to bring back the hand
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and pull out the child according to its natural shape, and make her sneeze, then tell her to push as hard as the child comes out
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	From the outlet of the child on his neck, with his hands spread out and his face turned towards his mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	Then you must gently pull your hand out, then turn him bit by bit, and carefully pull him out
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when he is aligned, put on the mastic of old wax and oil as we have said, then tell her to move gently bit by bit
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	and when you have done this, make her sit on a seat and tell her to push, then make her sneeze
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In the same manner for all the afterbirth
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes out in this way with all the afterbirth, cut the umbilical cord with your nail until all moisture is emptied
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	and if the child's face and neck are bent down, cut the umbilical cord from the belly so that it is not retained, otherwise the child will die
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	then put the child inside until you have placed him as he should be, and tell the woman to push once more
adonques si istra legierement.	Then it will come out easily
de l’issue des gemelz	From the outlet of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four; and this is not a strange thing, although it happens rarely
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two are strange things, and do not live long if they are not named
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that they can be multiplied, but they are separated by the sac that divides them, which is attached to the belly
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	And sometimes they come out just as naturally as one single child
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they come out crying, then care for them as we have said, and let the midwife be skilled and act quickly and easily
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and do so in such a way that moves towards health
de plusors enfans	Of several children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vj. ou .vij., ou plusors jusc’a .xv., et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious,	Sometimes they are formed in the mother's womb one or two, three or four, five or six, seven or more, up to fifteen, and all are fully formed in the shape of a child according to the measurement of the wise Creator
et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	and therefore the midwife must know all these things, for sometimes such things happen
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	so she should do accordingly
de l’enfant mort	Of a dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you care for the woman with a dead child in her womb, as I have said in the previous section, and it does not come out, and you are forced to use your hands;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	then you must know whether the woman has a sound constitution, and whether she is afraid of death or not;
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	then the woman should be lying on her back with her thighs inclined downward and her legs raised;
et li ministre la teigne de .ij. pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and the minister should pull from two sides where she is attached to the bed so that she is not harmed by the descent of the child;"
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	then rub the mother's mouth with moist oil mixed with old wax and fennel seed and linseed, then grease the midwife's hands with these oils and mastic;
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere .i. leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu,	"Then place them gently on the mortar, then grind one spot where the ointments should be applied."
et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	"And make sure that if the child is dressed, he descends onto his head;"
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez,	"If you apply ointments in his eyes or on his neck or in his mouth or in his throat or under his beard or in his armpit or near the ribs,"
et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	"And if descending is on foot, then apply or insert it at the middle of the thighs."
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	"And it is necessary that he spreads the ointment with his right hand, places his left hand's curved part between his two breasts, and gently presses down with his whole hand, applying the ointment to any of these areas we have mentioned until the container is empty;"
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	"And this is the shape of the ointment:"
puis fiche encontre .i. autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	"Then apply another ointment, or a third one if necessary, so that the extractions are equal;"
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	"And then stretch it evenly by moving from one side to the other so that more can come out, and let the ointment be thickened for better holding, like this is the shape:"
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	"And if some remains, then anoint some of his armpits with oil and place them on that part, and draw the other part;"
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	"And if none remains, then place this ointment or another one higher up, and do this until everything flows out."
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement,	"And if one hand comes before the other, and he cannot bring it back because of the extraction,"
si covient que tu envoloupes sus .i. drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	"then you must wrap a cloth around it until everything comes out;"
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as .ij. piés.	"Then cut at the joint of the sole or the edge, and do the same for the other hand, and there will be two feet."
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee,	"And if the child's leg is thick and it is tight at the exit, or if the head is pointed and gathered together,"
si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	"then you must place the spine of a small fish between your two breasts, cut the head open, and extract the bone."
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	"or you could round it with the instrument called 'almidach', which is also shaped like the instruments that follow later on in this chapter;"
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	"And do likewise if the child has a large head naturally;"
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles,	"and then pull out the bones with forceps,"
et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	"And if the leg comes out but is still tight at the thigh, cut it open until the muscles of the thigh come out;"
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	"And if it cannot come out, then cut it into pieces at the thigh so that you can see;"
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	"And if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, you must pierce it until the muscles contract."
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	"And if the child is on its feet, then traction is easy, and directing towards the mouth of the matrix is also easy."
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a .i. drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	"And if it is tight in the belly or at the thigh, you must extract it using one hand wrapped in a cloth;"
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	"and cut the belly or thigh open until the muscles contract;"
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure,	"And if the other limbs are already extracted but the leg remains,"
si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	If the physician places his hand deep into the wound, and pulls it out to the mouth of the wound.
puis i boute .i. oncine ou ij., et le trai fuer;	Then he inserts one or two fingers in place and pulls it out gently.
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier,	But if the mouth of the wound is narrowed by heat-induced inflammation within it, then do not attempt to manipulate it
ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	but rather apply moist and fatty substances
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and use plasters that are softened, and especially those soaked in warm water to soften them
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the child is lying on his side, and you cannot lay him flat, then treat him as we have said for a living child
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	but if one lacks the strength to do so, then pull it out piece by piece and leave nothing of the afterbirth behind
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And once you have done this, treat heat-induced inflammation in wounds as we have said
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and if bleeding occurs, apply cold water to constrain it, and then use other remedies
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	I saw a woman whose womb contained an infant that had died, then another infant became lodged on top of it and also died
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, she developed inflammation in her vulva which swelled so much that it opened up and began to emit a foul odor
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat her, but after pondering for a long time, I could not heal the wound
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong attracting plaster and an bone emerged, then after several days another one appeared
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was greatly astonished by this, for the womb has no bones
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I concluded that they were bones from a dead infant
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em miglior point;	I cleaned the wound and removed many bones until the woman recovered well;
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	"And the woman bore a child for many days, and then gave birth to a small amount of water."
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	"And I have recorded this chapter first so that when the master finds something unfamiliar, he knows how to provide assistance."
dou ramener la marris a son leu	"to bring the dislocation back into place"
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here comes the shape of the presser, to which one applies the books; and at two turns for each of the two heads of the two ligaments.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	Nevertheless, the horns should be more delicate than the restrictor, and made of ebony or boxwood;
et soit li bouche dou fust .i. doi de large, et li marge des arbres .i. doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	"And let the mouth of the funnel be two fingers wide,
et enmi les .ij. liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	"And between the two limbs, there should be two bindings of this same material, closed at both ends with a length of half a palm or slightly more."
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les .ij. cornes.	"And these two bindings are passed through the mouth of the marrow to open when one turns the two horns."
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, similar but more refined and lighter, should be made from ebony or boxwood, resembling tongs;
et ait as .ij. chiés .ij. ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et .ij. dois de large;	"And let it have two joints, two articulations, each one a palm's length, and two fingers' width."
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor .i. lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes,	"And when you see the membrane open all around the instrument, then make the woman sit on one bed, with her feet hanging and legs spread apart,"
puis boute les .ij. ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	"then insert the two articulations joined together into the membrane, and hold the head of the instrument beneath between her thighs;"
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	"then open your hand around the entire instrument, just as you would with forceps evenly, according to how much you see the mouth of the membrane open, until the child does what it wants."
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	"These instruments are all mounted, and their appearances are multiplied. When the surgeon has prepared them, the operation is performed more quickly, and the instruments are taller for men because of their size."
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	"Do not disdain the instrument until you have prepared it, for its necessity is not excusable."
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	"When the membranes are retained at childbirth, you must command the sick woman to hold her breath, then make her sneeze with camphor water, and restrain her hands over her mouth and nose;"
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	"And if she faints because of this, so much the better."
Se ceu non, si prent .i. pot, et fai .i. pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	"If not, then take a pot and make one hole in the cover, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the membrane inside it, such as celery, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centory;"
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris,	"all these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked in the pot with water over the fire. Then put one end of a tube into the hole of the pot and the other end into the mouth of the membrane;"
et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	"and let it remain like that until the steam enters the membrane. Then make her sneeze, as we have said."
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	"If the membranes are expelled quickly."
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature,	"And if the membranes remain after this treatment and are not expelled, then command the woman to moist her left hand in oil of sesame or in mucus of althea, and then put it into the birth canal,"
et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	"and search for the membranes. When she finds them, let her take them and stretch them out little by little, so that the membrane does not tear during extraction;"
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	"but she must move it gently to the right and left, then pull it; thus it will come out and disentangle itself."
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	"And if the mouth of the membrane is very narrow, we have spoken about the treatment of sneezing and fumigation with herbs;"
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	"But if none of these treatments work, then be sure not to pull too hard;"
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	"but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the membrane be tied to the woman's hip, then she should be given an enema with tetraplacenta oil;"
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	"So that she can push and remove it, and expel it. But nevertheless, when she pushes, if a bad smell comes to her stomach and head, and makes the woman ill."
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	"Therefore, suitable fumigations must be used for this purpose. None of the ancients have proven fumigation with watercress and dried figs."
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	"The shape of the instrument used to fumigate the woman during the retention of the flowers and membranes is as follows:"
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	"It resembles a tube made of glass, with the narrow end placed in the birth canal and the wide ends held over the fire;"
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	"And let the fumigation be done over hot coals until she is gassed, then begin another one."
de percier lou fondement	"to pierce the anus"
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	"Many children are born without having their anus pierced, but they have been blocked by a subtle synechia:"
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	"Therefore, the midwife must pierce this synechia with her finger and not use a sharp instrument to avoid injury, and clean the opening so that she does not touch it;"
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	"then put on a cloth moistened in wine and oil, then continue with the oil treatment until it is healed."
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	"And if you doubt that it has not healed, then place a tube of lead in the opening and leave it there for a few days, removing it when the child is ready to be taken to its room."
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	"Sometimes this obstruction occurs suddenly due to a wound or an abscess; it is necessary to cut off that growth: it should be cured as we have said for the lead tube."
de la fistule dou fondement	"of the fistula of the anus"
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	"Fistulas that come from under the anus are nodular and grow larger than those that come from near the anus or in the space of the two buttocks,"
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	"If there is one fistula or more. And when that nodular fistula is old, it opens up and becomes moist with white pus or thin bowels,"
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	"and sometimes these fistulas are perforating, and they are recognized by the fact that there is evacuation or wind during defecation when the patient has a bowel movement, and occasionally a worm comes out."
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	"And there are fistulas that pierce up to the bladder and up to half of the penis; and they reach up to the hip joint and up to the knee."
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	"Thus one recognizes a perforating fistula of the anus that is not perforating:"
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	"And it is when you put your index finger in the anus and insert a fine needle made of silver or iron into the fistula when there is no tortuosity."
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	"And if there is tortuosity, then insert a thin lead tube or a horsehair until you feel the tube or hair with your finger;"
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	"and if you do not feel it and nothing comes out of the opening, neither evacuations nor wind nor worms, as we have said:"
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	"know that it does not pierce, so hasten to treat it."
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	"And when the fistula is perforating up to the bladder or up to the urethra, urine comes out of it and cannot be healed by medications."
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	"If it is pierced up to the hip joint, then the tube will come out at that spot;"
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	"if there is no tortuosity and there is constant pain around it, then it constantly emits bowels, and neither medication nor healing by ointment will help;"
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	"and in these perforating fistulas there is no other cure than surgery, and the foolishness of those who meddle with them."
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	"In that which is not perforating and is not old, there is hope for healing by iron, as I have proven,"
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	"And it is that the patient lies on their stomach between your hands and raises their legs up to their hips, with their hips inclined towards their belly;"
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	"then insert an iron or lead tube until you know where the tube comes out."
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	"If the patient feels it around the anus, then you must put your two index fingers in there,"
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	"then feel that the tube has pierced it; and if you feel between your finger the synechia or the flesh, then know that it is perforating;"
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	"but do not work on it unless one can heal it."
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	"It is said that sometimes they can be healed, but this happens rarely;"
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	"And the aid given there is to heat the fine cautery according to the width of the fistula, as it was said before;"
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	"And heat the cautery iron until it is hot enough to reach near the fundament; and do this two or three times, until you know that these broken veins have been burned, which resemble an feathers of birds."
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	"And then cauterize the wet tents until that vein bursts forth, then apply the ointment around the vein and bind it tightly."
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	"If it is cured in this way, that's good. If not, it cannot be cured any other way;"
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	"If the tent enters and does not pierce all the way to the thumb which is at the fundament, and between your two fingers there is a thick layer of flesh or skin, and you see that the fistula passes beneath this covering towards the heart;"
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	"If the opening of the beginning of the fistula is close by and you push the tent in further ahead, then apply the cautery afterwards until it reaches the head of the tent;"
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	"And the tent will be freed and fall out; then dress those broken veins that resemble feathers of birds, so that none remain."
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	"If the sinew breaks and tears between you and the work, cauterize it with fire or strong medicine."
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	"For the cautery of fire serves two purposes: it burns these adjoining veins together and stops the flow of blood and dries up the moisture."
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	"Then cauterize with moist tents or crushed substances until the place yields and bursts forth, and the burned vein appears in the wound;"
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	"Then treat the wound with ointments that bind tightly and harden the flesh, these are dry medicines."
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	"For when it is cauterized in this way, it is truly cured and does not return."
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	"And if the fistula comes right down from the fundament and is far from the body, push your thumb into the fundament and search for it."
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	"If you feel the tent and between your two fingers there is skin or flesh where it is about to pierce, then there should be no hesitation or doubt in using one of these three methods:"
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	"either you cauterize it as we have described, or cut it all the way through, or if you cannot push in tents, then treat it as mentioned first;"
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	"but do not cut too deeply lest you cut into the tissue that holds the fundament and cause involuntary evacuation;"
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	"then treat it as we have described;"
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	"perhaps it will be cured, or you can push aside that covering and clean it after cutting near the fundament with a tent or another pointed instrument;"
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	"then dress that broken vein in the wound as much as you can;"
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	"then strive to heal the wound and keep the fistula away from the fundament: this will be easier for the patient."
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	"And some fistulas are like this: when you insert the tent into the fistula, it is on the side of the fundament near the skin above;"
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	"If you take a tent with a hole at the tip like this:"
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	"And tie one end of a thread to the top of the tent, then insert the tent all the way into the fistula until it reaches its tip."
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	"If it passes through to the edge of the fundament inside, then pull out the thread from that hole so that you can insert your thumb into the fundament;"
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	"then pull on the end of the thread and bring the two ends together, tie them tightly together, and leave it for one or two days;"
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	"And sometimes tie it again until the thread cuts through those tissues between them and closes up;"
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	"then treat the wound until it is healed."
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	"If the fistula does not burst open on its own, make it do so by any means you can, unless it is too deep."
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"For it would not be good to cut too deeply and then treat it as we have described until it is healed;"
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	"The shape of the pointed spatula used to open a fistula is most often like this:"
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	"And on the other side it has no point so that you do not cut what should not be cut, as shown here:"
des emorroydes	"hemorrhoids"
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Fear is of two kinds: either it resides within the foundation, like grains of resin, and there are both small and large ones; blood also flows from the surface.
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	And there is one or more [emorrydes], which lack the foundation and are at the head of the foundation; but those that lack so much have little moisture.
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	And on the surface there is either a small amount of clear water or a small amount of blood, and they have the color of flesh.
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	And the treatment for those who have [emorrydes] within the foundation is that you should command the patient to walk in rooms until the foundation is expelled from them, and then their children will appear.
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	Then hurry, and grasp it with tweezers or pull it out with your nail, then cut it at its roots;
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	"However, if the sinews cannot hold them due to moisture, take them with one cloth, or cotton, or a piece of chamlet."
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	"And pull them with your two hands, then cut them and sprinkle on some hot powders that are in place of cautery."
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	"Or cauterize them as it is said in the chapter on cautery, then treat them with other remedies until they are sound."
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	"If the foundation cannot come out, then perform a cleansing enema on the patient using a biting and sharp laxative to wash what is in the fundament so that it can come out openly."
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	"If the patient strains, and if the threads are far from the fundament, then the treatment is easy."
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	"And it is that you grasp them with your nail or with forceps and cut them, then treat them as we have said until they are sound and the patient fears incision by iron."
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	"Then you must arrange the stitching in this manner: take one twisted thread, and put it into a needle, then draw the thread upwards and make the needle pierce from the other side, and turn both ends of the thread under the needle."
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	"and it should be loose; and tie the thread firmly, then knot the thread and remove the needle, and do this for all of them, leaving one untied to correct any excess blood."
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	"then place one moistened cloth in rose oil or wax on the fundament and put it on top of the fundament, and tell the patient to rest;"
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"and leave him alone until he defecates; then treat them with ointments and other remedies until they are sound."
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	"For the drying of the fissure in the fundament:"
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	"Often times a fissure occurs in the intestines due to drying, and this can happen naturally or when the patient is old and medication is ineffective."
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	"Then you should use the tip of a spatula or your nail to remove the scab above it without letting it get wet;"
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	"then treat it until it is healed as necessary;"
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	"And if it does not heal, then begin scraping more forcefully than before until it heals and becomes scabbed over;"
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	"then treat it until it is healed."
dou fremit	"For trembling:"
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	"A mouse is a small creature that runs throughout the body;"
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	"and sometimes it causes trembling and coldness, which can be felt throughout the entire body, but more often in the hands than other parts."
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	"The treatment is to take a feather from an eagle or a large owl and place it on the trembling area until the circle around it becomes warm;"
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	"then twist your hand around the feather all the way around the trembling area and place it throughout the body to reach its roots and remove the trembling from them."
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	"And if you wish to do this with a feather of brass or iron, then do it in this manner, and make sure that it is thin underneath and sharp above:"
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	"Do not pierce too deeply so as not to hurt the fingers or cause them to bleed. And if you wish, cauterize the trembling area, just as it is described in the chapter on cautery."
de la forme dou clistere	"Of the form of a clyster:"
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	"Sometimes a clyster is made of silver or lead, or molten brass or wax; and sometimes they are made of these small or large instruments, according to their size."
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	"Therefore, those that are used for the treatment of children and those who are weak and sickly should be small;"
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	"The form of a small or large clyster is as follows: wide where the belly is bound according to this manner:"
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	"And there should be an opening where the belly is bound, so that you can see it, and the waste should be pierced inside, and there should be two holes on one side and one hole on the other;"
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	"And the belly where the medicine is placed should be made of an animal bladder or parchment and pierced all around with small holes;"
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	"And there should be one nut of spice between each hole, then insert a strong thread made from thick wool twisted in ten or more turns into each hole and sew up the belly like a goat."
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	"And once the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument with a strong thread before performing the clyster;"
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	"And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold and grease the end of the clyster with oil or melted beeswax or something similar before gently inserting it;"
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	"Then the minister should press with both hands together until it is completely inserted, then remove the clyster and lift up the patient's legs at the side;"
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	"And if the medicine threatens to come out, then tie it in place as best you can. And if he lies still for the whole night, then it is even more beneficial."
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if you perform a clyster in an illness where the belly is inflamed and the medicine rushes out quickly, then repeat it until it is healed."
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	"And if the hemorrhoids are in the fundament or an aposteme, then use a clyster that is as thin as one for a child;"
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	"This is the form of a thin clyster where the skin is stretched taut:"
des plaies	Of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	"We have already discussed in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about the treatments for hands and medicines according to their fulfillment."
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	"I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where they are made, and what they are made with."
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	"The things by which wounds are made are: a blow from a stone, a cut from a sword or dagger or spear or club or similar thing;"
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	"or wounds made according to the parts of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or head, or thigh, or belly, or liver, and similar members;"
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	"And I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and I will begin with simple head wounds, since the memory will come in its chapter."
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	"I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, then make sure if it was caused by a blow from a stone or similar thing, and if the skin is completely torn and the wound is large,"
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	"and if it is a hot aposteme, then perform cupping immediately using the cephalic vein directly above the wound if possible, and make sure that the cupping is performed on the opposite side of the injured part;"
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	"And avoid letting the patient consume wine or heavy foods."
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	"And if he cannot tolerate cupping, then reduce his diet and do not let him drink wine or eat meat;"
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	"And place on the wound, if a hot aposteme comes, cotton moistened only with rose oil or with wine that has been thickened;"
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	"And if there is no hot aposteme, then place on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood and has not been moved by air, powder that I will describe a little later;"
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if the air has moved it, then place on it some ointments until it is healed."
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like one from a sword cut and similar ones, and its lips cannot be brought together by binding alone, then bring them together by stitching, as I shall say regarding wounds of the belly, concerning stitches.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is open to the bone, gaping and barely attached except for a small portion, then cut it away; afterwards treat the wound with medication, and replace lost skin with toughened leather.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	And order the patient to eat substantial foods like testicles and cooked wheat, as well as poultry and similar items.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	If you find rotten skin but not reaching the bone, then cut away all the rotted flesh and discard it, then dress the wound
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if there is an artery or vein in the wound which cannot be controlled by medication alone, then tie off the artery and if you find it dislocated, suture it with a thread
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if that does not help, cauterize it
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then their care is easy; you should place in this powder which binds before the art has moved it
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the manner of preparing the powder is as follows: take incense for one part; dragon's blood two parts; quicklime three parts, and grind them together finely
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and apply it to the wound, pressing strongly until the wound closes well and joins with all its blood;
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Then let it sit well, and leave it without loosening, unless it swells; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	Sometimes heat alone is applied when incense or dragon's blood are not available, but only after the art has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the physician has moved the wound, even in summer, then one does not put this powder there at all;
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	"However, apply some digested ointments or poultices made of barley flour with water and honey until it swells."
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	"Then perform other treatments until they are healed."
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	"And if a bone fracture comes with the wound and it is small, then remove it with delicate forceps;"
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	"and I will tell you about skull fractures afterward."
de la plaie dou col	"of the neck wound"
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	"If a wound comes on the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and one on the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut."
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	"If it is the nerve, there is no other treatment but to leave it alone and not apply anything constricting, because it harms the nerves and causes them to retreat;"
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	"and do not apply anything cold to the wound because the substance of nerves is cold, and their continuity goes with the brain, which is the highest organ;"
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	"but let the medicine be warm, such as hot water mixed with rose oil and cooked water also in soft water,"
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	"and other similar things according to this manner, and moist compresses."
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if the wound is large, then suture and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it heals."
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	"And if the wounds are deep, filled with pus and full of bowels, then pierce them lower down;"
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	"and if the artery is cut and bleeding occurs profusely, then tie it off, ligate it, and cauterize it if necessary;"
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	"And if the windpipe or the heart is cut, but the vessels that carry the flesh are preserved,"
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	"then suture the heart to the spine of the neck, and do not touch the windpipe, but put it back according to its natural shape;"
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	"and then bind it carefully, leaving it for a few days, then treat it with drying ointments until it heals;"
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	"And if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then scrape it."
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	"and if there are bone fragments, remove them all if you can, and those that you cannot have, leave them until the wound putrefies,"
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	"and then evacuate and ligate the discharge;"
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	"And if the wound is fresh, then sprinkle on it the powder that I have mentioned."
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	"And if there are bones and fistulas in the wound, then treat it as I said in its chapter."
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	"on wounds from a lance or a dagger"
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	"If it is a wound from a lance or dagger and the wound is deep, then observe if there are any signs of wind escaping from the wound where the patient inhales: know then that the wound is mortal;"
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	"and if it is not deep but fresh with blood throughout its length, then do not apply the powder at first or tie it to prevent the blood from flowing out."
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	"and go back to the heart and kill him;"
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	"but apply an attractive ointment there twice a day,"
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	"And if you have no ointment, then put some lint cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture."
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	"and make the patient lie on the wound for three days or four or more;"
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	"So that no spasm comes of it, nor evil trembling of the heart nor attacks of breathing;"
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	"and when you see these good signs, know then that the wound is saved."
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	"So treat it with compresses and other remedies until it heals;"
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	"And if it cannot heal nor close up, know then that there is a fistula present; so treat it as one should."
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	"And if the wound is from an incision made by sword or dagger and is clean, whether it is on the front or back, then treat it as those that are in front;"
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	"If it is large, then stitch it up; and if it is small, sprinkle powder on it. And if it is close to the bone and has cut off fragments of bone, scrape the wound clean and remove all foreign bodies if they are visible;"
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	"and if they are not visible, then leave the wound to putrefy, and ligate the discharge;"
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	"And for other wounds on other limbs, the judgment is as we have said."
dou derrompement dou ventre	"on rupture of the abdomen"
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	"The rupture of the abdomen may be large or medium-sized or small;"
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	"from a large wound some portions of the intestine or bowel often protrude through it;"
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	"And stitching is more difficult, and sometimes the smaller wound causes worse harm than the larger one;"
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	"for if one does not carefully replace them intestine by intestine they will slip back in again;"
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	"for as soon as the intestines feel the cold air they swell up and slip back more easily;"
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	"And also because the middle-sized wound is often worse than others, because many portions of the intestine are torn off at their place rather than between two;"
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	"And know that a rupture of the abdomen occurs in four ways:"
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	"The two common sutures happen during abdominal surgery,"
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	"And the stitching of other wounds on the body, plus two other stitches are common to other wounds."
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	"Still, they are more appropriate with abdominal stitches, and I will discuss each one and explain them."
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	"I say that when the wound is small, and none of the intestines have protruded,"
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	"and there is no urgency to reset it, then this is done in one of two ways:"
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	"either because the wound is small, as we have said,"
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	"or because the intestines are swollen due to the cold."
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	"And when it is cold, heat it in this way:"
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	"Moisten a sponge or one soft cloth in boiling water only,"
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	"or you cook in hot water with salt and cumin."
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	"And raise the intestines until the swelling has gone away;"
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	"and then apply this binding wine to draw it out."
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	"And when you see the swelling starting to disappear, moistening the intestines with water or decocted mallows,"
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	"for by this means the entrance is relieved somewhat;"
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	"And if it still cannot enter, then make a small incision in the wound with the instrument used for cutting hemorrhoids;"
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	"and the first dressing is one that draws out the wound,"
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	"which no one should cut into without great necessity."
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	"And this is the instrument for splitting it open:"
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	"Thus cut inside in the curve and do not turn back, as shown here:"
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	"And when the wound is enlarged and the intestines have protruded,"
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	"then replace them according to their natural form in their proper place;"
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	"If you are able to do this, for it is most useful."
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	"When the wound is large and is located below the belly,"
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	"then you must make the patient lie on his back;"
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	"And place his legs higher than his head."
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	"And if it is located below the belly,"
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	"then raise the head and chest higher than the lower parts;"
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	"And also, if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two sides,"
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	"then ensure that the wounded side is higher than the other."
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	"And thus one must arrange what I say for large and medium-sized wounds."
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	"For small wounds, apply what you have been equipped with,"
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	"then have between your hands one pitiful minister who will remove all the rupture from his hand."
et assemble les levres;	"And bring together the lips;"
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	"This is the common manner of suturing,"
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	"And it is that you take one needle or several, according to the quantity of the width of the wound,"
