puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	"then leave two fingers' space from the beginning of the wound, and there insert one needle with a good strong thread;"
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	"And pierce the two ends of the skin together with the two ends of the syringe;"
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	"which is beneath the skin inside, until you have pierced it from that side;"
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	"And bring together the two ends of the syringe, one on top of the other;"
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	"then pull it taut with a doubled thread on either side of the needle;"
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	"then bring together the two ends of the wound evenly,"
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	"And then leave two fingers' space and insert another needle;"
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	"then tie it with thread just as you did the first needle;"
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	"And continue to do this according to how many needles you need;"
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	"until all the wound is closed up;"
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	"And let the needles be moderate, neither too fine nor too thick;"
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	"for fine needles seize all the flesh, and large ones cannot penetrate well enough:"
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	"That is why they must be moderate."
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	"And it is not necessary to push the needles too deeply into the flesh and skin,"
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	"for they seize and open up the wound before the suture;"
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	"And then cut off the ends of the needles so that they do not bother the patient while sleeping,"
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	"And place tents or bandages on the ends of the needles for better support;"
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	"and leave them in place until the wound is healed."
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	"And this manner of suturing with needles is more suitable for small wounds;"
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	"for it suffices to use one or two needles there."
Li seconde costure si est commune,	"The second suture is common,"
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	"And it is to bring together the two ends of the skin and the two ends of the syringe together with one needle, on which there is a medium-strength thread;"
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	"And when you have pierced all these ends together,"
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	"then turn the needle back on itself at the point where you began, in the manner of sewing cloth;"
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	"And leave the thickness of a goose's egg between each suture;"
ceste costure sevent li home,	"This suture is used by people,"
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	"I sewed a wound that one man had in his belly,"
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	"who was wounded with a knife,"
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	"And the wound was more than a palm's length long;"
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	"And it opened into the intestines for about two palms' length;"
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	"And the wound was in his belly."
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	"I brought back the intestine and it was twenty-four hours later,"
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	"And the wound healed in fifteen days, and I dressed it, and he recovered."
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	"And the doctors had judged that he would die, but it was a miracle;"
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	"And I did not dress the wound with ointment because there were none to be found in that place, nor any medicines."
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	"And I put old cotton on the wound twice a day and washed it with honey water until he was healed."
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	"Now I will tell you the two proper manners of suturing:"
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	"Take the needle and push it from the outside to the inside;"
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	"When the needle has pierced the heart directly, then leave the end of the syringe where you pushed the needle;"
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	"And pierce it again from the inside to the outside on another point;"
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	"The purpose of this suture is that you sew like a furrier sews pelts,"
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	"And that you leave the syringe once on one side and take it up again on another, so that the suture is completely finished."
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	"The second manner of suturing, which Galen speaks of properly,"
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	"is when some people bring the two ends together naturally;"
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	"And apply one end of the syringe to the other end in this manner:"
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	"Insert a needle into the nearest midpoint and pierce only that point;"
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	"And leave the two ends of the syringe;"
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	"Then turn the needle back and pierce it from the outside to the inside;"
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	"as you did for the two ends of the syringe;"
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	"Then pierce both from the outside to the inside in two other midpoints that are on the other side;"
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	"And this is the most common and best manner of suturing."
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	"Galen said these words, and some testify to it,"
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	"That one should sew the belly with two needles, each having thread;"
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	"And one needle should be pushed in from one side and the other from another, like those who sew gutta-percha;"
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	"And know that when the intestine is inside the belly,"
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	"the suture is more difficult than in other places on the belly."
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	"The judgment of a wound is such as the judgment of other wounds:"
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	"And that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood before it has moved;"
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	If one resets the intestines, and the wound is closed; then place powder around the flesh.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	And if the wound has moved, then apply some ointment that is present until the wound is bowed.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	And tie the stitches, and let the skin be closed, and the flesh.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat the wound as others, until it is healed;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you do not have medicine, then apply [it], as soon as it begins to discharge pus or blood, old cotton.
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and move it two times a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you need no other medicine in many cases where the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound does not communicate with the principal limbs,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	then it is necessary that you moisturize light linen in warm tempered oil or rose oil
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and apply it around the angles and under the armpits;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if there is pain or putrefaction in the belly, which happens many times,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	If black wine enema causes pain, especially if the corruption reaches the intestines
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and pierces inside, know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine called "jejunum" cannot heal if it is injured
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and because of the thinness of its walls and the subtlety of its entire body, and its proximity to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the zebra jumps from the wound, it should be replaced just like the intestine while it is still fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it is old and has turned black or become worms, then you should tie off the blackened part so that no blood flows there
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	for there are veins and arteries there;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then cut what is between the ligature
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and place two clamps dangling from below the wound up to the front to facilitate the extraction when the zebra falls and the wound closes.
de la routure dou boueil	from the rupture of the bowel
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestine is round and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	If it can be restored in some men
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	For I saw a man wounded in the belly with a spear;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it swelled and became a fistula, through which there issued pus and wind;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I treated him as well as I could until he was healed, and the place was sound.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it healed, I doubted that the patient did not have some illness in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	"There was no harm done, but it remained in better positions, eating and drinking."
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	"And some experimenters said that when there is a small wound in the intestines, it must be tied in this manner:"
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	"Take large threads and then bring together the lips of the wound,"
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	"and when the thread has opened the mouth, then put it on the two lips,"
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	"So that it pulls its mouth open;"
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	"And then cut off its head so that it cannot untie itself,"
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	"then put another thread in the same way as before until the wound is completely closed;"
et cout la plaie.	"And then sew up the wound."
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	"These heads grow again in the intestines and cause no harm to the sick person,"
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	"And one can tie the intestines with a fine thread cut from an animal's intestine,"
en teil maniere:	"So that:"
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	"Take the head of this intestinal thread that is very lean,"
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	"And then tie to the head of this thread one twist of thin linen thread,"
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	"Then put the thread through the needle and sew up the intestines, folding it into the incision;"
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	"And this method of sewing with threads is no further than according to the way of faith and hope."
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	"And if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the small intestines, there is no skill nor healing except subtlety."
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	"whether it is a fistula or wherever it may be,"
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	"It should be known that every wound or boil, when it grows old, is universally called a 'fistula.'"
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	"And especially when it is deep and goes inwards."
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	"A fistula is according to the true definition a hard and white knot or node where there is no pain felt,"
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	"And it is also deep like the quill of a bird;"
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	"and sometimes it goes out clear and straight, and other times it is thick;"
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	"sometimes it is small, and other times quite large;"
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	"I have spoken about this in the division of wounds, that every wound which does not heal and has no flesh,"
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	"is only because of one of the seven causes:"
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	"That is to say, due to the thinness of blood or body;"
ou por sa malice;	"or because of its wickedness;"
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	"or because there is hard flesh inside and on the lips which does not allow new flesh to grow;"
ou il i a trop de bowe;	"or because of too much depth;"
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	"or because the wound is porous and the material is of poor quality;"
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	"or because the medicine used for treatment is not good."
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	"or because the corruption is in a manner of pestilence,"
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	"or because of the property in the region where digestion is slow, and healing is delayed by nature."
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	"or because there are veins or bones present:"
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	"I have already shown all these causes, signs, and remedies for medicine in the division."
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	"Now it is fitting that I tell you about the cure of fistula which is done by manual work:"
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	"It should be known that fistula occurs in all parts of the body;"
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	"for there are fistulas which come from large veins and arteries, and nerves,"
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	"or in the sinew, intestines, bladder, or some of the ribs,"
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	"Or for the spine of the back, or for any joint of the hands or feet;"
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	"And if it comes to the property of the main member, and similar places."
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	"And all fistulas that are of this manner are of harsh healing, and there is nothing but labor, and ignorance;"
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	"And if there is any fistula that does not come to the place that I have mentioned, you can trust its cure,"
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	"and recognize it if you please, take a tent of iron or bronze, if the fistula is straight, put it there;"
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	"And if the fistula is twisted, seek one with a subtle lead plate,"
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	"because lead bends more around the twistiness;"
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	"And if the fistula has many perforations and you cannot properly search it with tents,"
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	"then use a clyster through one of the perforations."
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	"for moisture cuts from one perforation to another and cleanses it;"
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	"then search for the source of its bleeding as much as you know if there is bone or nerve involved and how deeply it is embedded;"
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	"And ask the patient carefully about the pain they feel when pressed by your hand, and where they feel it;"
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	"and once you truly know where it is located, whether it is far from a joint, nerve, artery, or vein,"
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	"then cut according to what I have told you."
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	"And remove the faulty flesh and rotting tissue that is inside;"
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	"And then dress it until it is healed,"
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	"But if the fistula is very deep from a straight place, you must cut deeply as far as you can;"
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	"then insert moistened tents medicated with hot water and bring them up to the head of the fistula,"
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	"until the medication corrodes the remaining surplus at the bottom;"
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	"And then apply fresh bandages soaked in healing oil until it is healed."
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	"And if it does not heal with this method, then cauterize it as we have said,"
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	"But if the bone is rotted by the fistula, cut it."
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	"If veins or nerves do not bother you in the main limbs, as we have said;"
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	"And if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackness, scrape it clean until all the corruption is removed;"
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	"then dress it with fresh bandages until it is healed."
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	"But if it does not heal, then retreat backwards as before,"
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	"So that you know you have not gone too far:"
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	"If you uncover and search until you reach the bottom,"
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	"And remove all the corruption, then close up the area;"
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	"And if it heals this way, that's good."
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	"But if not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach;"
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	"So there is no other remedy but to leave it alone:"
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	"And if there is a small rotted bone that you can grasp with forceps,"
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	"extract it using an appropriate instrument;"
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	"If there are many bones, crush them all and leave none behind;"
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	"And if the moisture opposes you and there is no error or fear,"
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	"then cut through moisture, flesh, and bone, and expose the bones."
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	"And if you cannot remove them within an hour, then apply something moist to the wound to promote rottenness,"
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	"and leave it until the area around the bones has rotted;"
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	"And then you will have easier access to remove the bones."
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	"And if it is a large bone such as those in the thigh or calf,"
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	"scrape away the corruption until all the blackness is removed;"
puis restoure la plaie;	"then close up the wound."
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	"And if there is much corrupted flesh extending to the bone marrow,"
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	"It must be scraped clean down to the corruption and then dressed until it heals;"
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	"And I will tell you about a fistula that happened in one man's leg,"
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	"So that you may take an example and aid yourself in your work."
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	"A young man of about thirty years had pain in his leg due to some cause inside his body;"
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	"so that the matter came into his leg and formed an abscess without any apparent cause for opening it;"
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	"But the physicians foolishly probed so much that the abscess opened;"
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	"And as they removed much matter, it became a fistula with many openings through which flowed much pus and moisture from the body;"
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	"and many doctors treated him for about two years, but none of them knew anything about the art of surgery;"
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	"So I was called in and saw his leg and the treatments they were using;"
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	"And the large amount of pus flowing from the openings;"
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	"The young man's body turned red and had a yellowish hue."
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	"I inserted a tent into one of the openings and then searched for all the others;"
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	"And found that some opened against each other in every part of the leg."
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	"So I quickly cut into one opening until I exposed a part of the bone,"
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	"and found that it was rotted and pierced through to the bone inside;"
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	"I scraped away what I could see of the rotted bone and thought that there was no other corruption besides what I had removed;"
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	"But as soon as I began to dress it with healing medicines over time, it would not heal;"
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	"and when I reopened it, I exposed the bone again just like before;"
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	"I found that the corruption had spread further into the bone, scraped it clean, and then removed it, and tried to heal the area;"
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	"But I could not make it heal until I cut around about a palm's width of bone, exposing its entire marrow;"
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	"then dressed it with medicines, and it healed quickly."
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	"And there was no need to reopen the wound except for the weakness of the patient who could not tolerate it;"
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	"and my fear that he might die."
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	"For he often bled from evacuation, but he was completely healed in the end;"
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	"And in place of the bone grew hard flesh, and he was well-disposed with no harm or trouble afterwards, either then or later."
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	"And if a bone is broken anywhere in the body, it must be set in this manner:"
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	"Take a splint and attach it to the head of the exposed bone,"
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	"And command someone to hold it extended upwards;"
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	"Then take another thicker linen bandage and wrap it around the flesh above the bone,"
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	"And extend the head of the splint so that you can pull out the corrupted flesh from underneath;"
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	"And uncover the flesh above the wound so that the bone does not rub against it and cause injury;"
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	"Then place a hot iron or a stone slab underneath the bone to help burn away corrupted flesh;"
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	"And continue doing this until you can see and feel that all the corruption is gone, then repeat once more."
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	"If a bone has rotted but not yet opened up, and the corruption is in the middle or in some part,"
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	"Then uncover all the flesh around it and place a hot iron underneath;"
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	"And then scrape away the corruption from one part to another with an instrument about the length of the corruption, as we have said;"
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	"If the corruption is at a joint, cut out the corrupted joint and scrape away the bone around it from another side;"
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	"And if corruption is present in the continuity of two joints, then there is no other remedy than cauterization."
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	"And if corruption is found at the wrist of the hand or at the ankle, it is very severe."
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	But nevertheless you must inquire about this wound, how it appears to you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse it in every way that you can, but without the vein or nerve causing resistance.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that there are many ways to cut and shape these bones according to their arrangement and appearance.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	And their thickness and their fineness,
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	And therefore one must prepare for each type of work its own instrument.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	Also know that the work will show you the tool with which you will have need, according to the knowledge of this art.
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	And witness to the ways of illnesses;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	If you think about the instrument that you need according to what is appropriate.
dou feu	Of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The flesh rots either due to an internal cause or due to a lack of warmth;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	And when you have medicated this corruption with the treatment of medicines, and they do not help at all.
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	Then it is necessary to cover that limb up to where the corruption occurs
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	So that the patient escapes from death or from the greater evil of losing the member.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	And the sign is that the limb becomes black as if it had been burnt by fire;
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	After the blackening, then that corruption spreads from member to member
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	And spreads throughout the body; so hurry to cover it
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	And if it is due to the sting of venomous beasts such as sea scorptions and vipers and similar ones
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If the corruption is at the top of the thigh, cover it and do not let it come up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the hand, cover it at the joint so that the corruption does not reach the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	And if it reaches the arm, cover it above the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is too late.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	And there are no remedies so powerful that their quantity cannot overcome them
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	And likewise when the corruption comes to the foot: if it reaches the first joint, cover it after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	And if it reaches the foot, cover the whole foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	"And if it goes up to the leg, it cuts at the knee joint;"
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	"And if it comes upon the knee, there is no other recourse but to let the patient die."
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	"and the method of covering or supporting the limb is to tie it above and below,"
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	"And extend one bandage downwards from one of the ties, and another upwards from the other tie,"
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	"and you remove the flesh between the two ties up to about an inch wide so that the bone is exposed."
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	"then cover or bind it, and place a linen cloth on each side so that the bandage does not touch the healthy flesh,"
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	"And if the patient suffers from another injury or wound."
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	"And if bleeding occurs when you operate, cauterize it immediately,"
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	"or apply some constricting powders; then return to your treatment until it is complete."
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	"then bind the wounded limb with a proper tie and care for it until it is healed,"
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	"I will tell you what happened to one man."
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	"a blackness that seemed like burnt with fire,"
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	"And this corruption first appeared on his big toe of his foot, spreading to cover the entire foot."
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	"and when the man saw the corruption, he quickly covered the foot and it became healed."
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	"And some time later, the corruption reappeared on his hand's big toe, and he came to me,"
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	"I applied things that caused blisters after cleansing his body, but I could not stop the corruption."
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	"and he asked me to cut off his hand, but I did not want to because I hoped that the matter would be blistered away,"
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	"I also feared that if I cut off his hand, he might die."
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	"for the man's strength was weak; he became completely discouraged and returned home,"
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	"and quickly covered his hand and it became healed."
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	"And I have told you this story only so that others may do likewise when there is need."
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	"Sometimes an ulcer occurs in the flesh and remains for such a long time that it collects a large amount of pus,"
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	"And then it grows round and bursts open, releasing the pus like water from a vase."
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	"And the skin above is as thin as fine muslin,"
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	"and they do not reach down to the bone or nerve, and such an illness is called 'healthy.'"
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	"It is not called a 'fistula';"
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	"But if it extends so far that it reaches the bone deeply, then it is called 'fistula'."
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	"And the skin should be cut all around, and even more so if it is thin, like a piece of cloth;"
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	"and do not worry about its corruption."
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	"And if you think the skin will tear and the corruption is deep inside,"
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	"If the skin is thick with flesh, cut it like this:"
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	"Observe if the breast is large and the belly that accompanies it has a foul odor,"
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	"Then perform an Egyptian clister made like this:"
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	"Take equal parts of hyssop, oil, and lead, and place them in one vessel over the fire,"
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	"until the medicine turns red and thickens like honey;"
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	"Then take some of it according to your need and mix it with water and honey,"
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	"And use this mixture to perform the enema on the breast, closing the opening."
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	"And leave the medicine inside for two hours, then remove it by squeezing;"
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	"Do this repeatedly until the breast is softened and the stench is removed."
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	"Finally, perform an enema with water and ashes,"
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	"When this medicine is not available, take some ashes from burnt grapevine wood, and pour water over it,"
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	"Then strain it and use it for an enema until you know that the breast is well cleaned."
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	"And if the patient cannot tolerate this treatment, or neither the Egyptian medicine nor the water and ashes,"
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	"Then use an enema of water and honey with a little bit of crushed lead;"
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	"Or use an enema of honey mixed with wine that has the property to cleanse and wash,"
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	"And let the wine make the flesh shrivel."
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	"And once this is done, if you are confident that the breast has been well cleaned,"
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	"Then perform an enema with medicine that promotes flesh growth,"
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	"And take some diachylon plaster and mix it with rose oil and wine;"
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	"Or use an enema with other medicines and oils that I have mentioned earlier in treating oils."
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	"And if the opening of the breast is too small for the nozzle of the enema to enter,"
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	"Then carefully widen it with an iron probe and insert a wick soaked in Egyptian oil;"
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	'Or basilicon oil, until it is widened."
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	"And if the wound is too wide, then fold and leave only enough space for the enema to enter;"
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	"And if the hole that the bow makes is above, then cover it with a cloth or place something below it."
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	"For when the bow is inserted deep, do not let any flesh enter;"
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	"And if you cannot cover the breast below as you wish,"
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	"Then arrange it so that the bow points towards the lowest point where it is inserted."
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	"For when the bow is inserted deep, do not let any flesh enter;"
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	"And if you cannot cover the breast below as you wish,"
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	"Then arrange it so that the bow points slightly downward and nothing of the bow remains inside;"
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	"And take some consolidative medicines to apply on the breast,"
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	"And then place a linen cloth over the entire breast;"
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	"Then tie tightly around the opening of the breast, using a bandage that is slightly wider than the first one;"
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	"Then apply a soothing oil on another cloth according to the size of the opening,"
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	"And place this cloth over the opening of the breast to ease the pain of the bowels, but do not remove the outer linen bandage except once after many days."
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	"Remove the cloth covering the opening of the breast frequently in order to remove the bowels,"
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	"And know what comes out from the bowels: whether it is venomous or little or enough, digested or undigested;"
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	"Be cautious if the patient feels pain or not, and whether there is an abscess or not,"
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	"And when this treatment has been applied in such manner for several days, observe the nature of the discharge that comes out from the opening of the breast;"
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	"Then know that the breast is becoming hardened and approaching healing;"
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	"And then untie it in the morning or on the third day, and when you open the wound,"
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	"Then change another cloth and renew the ointment."
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	"And if after many days the breast still discharges undigested bowels, know that the breast has not yet healed."
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	"But if subtle poisons come out after a long time, do not despair of healing,"
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	"For healing is approaching. There are people for whom the insertion of flesh into their wounds takes a long time, and others for whom it happens quickly;"
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	"And if undigested bowels continue to come out from the breast after many days, know that the breast has not yet healed."
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	"But if the breast is slow to harden and remains moist, then apply medicines that are dry in substance but moistening in virtue;"
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	"Such as Egyptian oil, for it contains much vitriol, which is the last medicine."
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	"Take Egyptian oil and mix it with rose oil and old wine in equal amounts;"
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	"Then cook this mixture together until it thickens, and use it; also honey cooked and increased does better."
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	"If Egyptian oil is not available,"
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	And you take myrrh and aloe wood and incense, grind them, and mix their powder with honey while it's on the fire;
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then dip one cloth in it, place it on the breast, and apply it several times a day, administering an ointment at length
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of celestine lily, which is also like wheat flour and millet flour;
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	And in the use of simples or composites: grind them, make them into powder, mix them with honey that I mentioned earlier, and apply them;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	And if the treatment is prolonged, and not cured by this treatment
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then know that the corruption has gone deep, and has impressed upon the bone, or in hard members, or in joints;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if it is a fistula treatment, just as we have said earlier.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the boil of the fingernail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Panarice is a boil that arises under the fingernail of the thumb
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or of the foot, or perhaps arises on other fingers;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it is old and one doesn't pay attention to it, then a black boil appears
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and they run and burst so much that they reach the root of the nail, sometimes even reaching all the way to the tip;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and the corruption comes as far as the bone, with painful stench, and the skin around the nail is swollen and red in color.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it according to what we have said earlier, but the treatment does not help
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	then you must cut into the flesh with an iron all the excess that remains under the nail
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	Cautery is very helpful if the bone and nail are sound;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the nail presses against the flesh, causing pain and inflammation;
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	If you must place the bandage under the nail where the flesh points
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and raise it up, and cut this delicate flesh gently and lightly
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and place on the remaining flesh burning and corrosive medicines to remove all;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption is in the bone, cut it out and cauterize it, for as long as the corrupted bone remains there, it cannot heal;
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see that both are corrupting, then cut one off like it is said before
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it until it heals
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is inflamed and swollen, causing great pain, you must heal it first;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut the nail of the little toe in an oblique manner across
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and be careful that the incision does not go all the way to the flesh underneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain;
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if it happens, put something on it that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain in the wrist
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	Some people's wrists may be very fatty by nature
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and sometimes there is bone or nail
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and some have their origin in the root of the joint or in some toes.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	Those that originate in any toe nail do not move
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and those that originate at the joint of the toe may move;`
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The incision for one that is fatty should be light like this:`
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it off at its root with a wide little toe nail clipper.`
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those that originate from the root of the joint are difficult to treat: hold down and cut off.`
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In those that originate where the nail should be on the little toe, first cut around the flesh until you reach the bone;`
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cut the bone with an appropriate chisel and treat it until it heals.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The scabs that come on both toes together are caused by birthmarks or scars from wounds or burns or similar things.`
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	You must cut off this adhesion so that the toes resume their natural shapes;`
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then place between them moistened gauze or cloth soaked in rose oil to prevent them from sticking together;`
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or else put between them thin slices of lead until the skin is healed as it should be.`
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If scabs come on any of his toes with the palm, cut off that adhesion as necessary;`
Des vils	Warts
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Warts are large outgrowths filled with melancholic excesses that appear on various parts of the body;`
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and they occur more often in the legs of those who walk and work and carry things than in others.`
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore you should administer to him sometimes a purge for the colon, and then treat it with the basilica remedy.`
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The treatment of warts is done in two ways: one is to cut them off and draw out the black blood;`
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other way is to lift up the growth and draw out all of it.`
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The incision should be made in this way: first raise the leg with very hot water until the large vein is softened;`
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then squeeze the leg from above towards the thigh down to the part below the knee;`
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then cut off the growth at one point or two or three, with a wide incision;`[TOOL_CALLS] et tu la doie si que li sang noir en coule fors de dedens.
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then raise and draw out dark blood with your hand from one end to the other until as much blood comes out as the patient's strength allows.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	And then apply a bandage, commanding him to bind himself with fresh meat around his black collarbone;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and restart evacuation and drainage when the veins are full, which harms the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The elevation of the leg should be done in this manner: raise the leg of the sick person, especially if there is a lot of hair
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then place him in a bath and heat the leg with warm water until it becomes red and the veins dilate;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	And if you have no bath, heat it by the fire and then tie the limb at the vein of the long bone at the top of the knee or below at the ankle joint;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then close the skin with sinew and scrape the vein from each side until it becomes visible when touched
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and when it is seen red and black, and as it enters the skin it appears like a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then place the knife underneath until the vein is raised from the skin, then pierce it gently with sinew
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then tie it in another location three finger widths away and scrape the skin above the vein until it becomes visible
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then raise it with the knife as you did before and pierce it with another sinew as you did at first;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	then make another tie or several ties if necessary, then raise it again and tie it at the ankle joint.
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then draw it out and lift it up to the second tie; then pull it out tie by tie until it is completely free, then tie it off.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	And if you cannot pull it out and raise it, then insert a large needle with strong doubled thread through the vein
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and tie it and pull it out, then place a knife underneath and twist your hand back and forth until it comes out completely
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	And make sure that it does not slip away, because if it slips away, you cannot pull or raise it and it will harm the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And once you have completely treated it, place wool moistened with red vinegar and rose oil on the wound site to cleanse it.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the vein is contracted, twisted, and coiled together, and not straight as we have said
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	then you must cut it crookedly without tying it off and pull it out as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the knife used to tie veins is curved and does not cut through, so that it does not pierce the vein
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and has a large curve because if it were thin it would cut through the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and this is its shape:
De la voinne civile	"Of the civil vein"
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is injured in legs, in warm regions where no herbs or trees grow, and on earth where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	And sometimes it occurs elsewhere than the legs, which happens due to rot that comes beneath the skin
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	just as it enters the body like serpents and worms, injuring between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the sign of the onset of this vein is that there is a very great inflammation in the leg
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the location changes, and the vein begins to protrude forth like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the skin opens up, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of lead weighing between one and a half to two pounds, and tie it
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and let the lead hang on the leg, and each time that some of it comes out at the opening, wrap the bandage around the lead and tie it again;
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, then cut off a portion of it, wrap the remaining part around, and do not cut it at its root until it has all come out;
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh and cause inflammation and rot in that place, and bad illness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	Therefore, it must be treated bit by bit until it reaches its head, and nothing should remain in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	And sometimes this vein, when treated, is five or ten palms long.
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	And once a man came to me whose vein was twenty palms long; when it was cut, it made one hole or opening, and pierced through to its depth
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that everything comes out of it. Then let the matter that was inside be emptied, and apply poultices to prevent rotting for several days before treating the wound as one would a boil.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And sometimes there are many veins, especially when it opens up at the ankle or on the foot
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and there are many holes from which much blood flows. Therefore treat it as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of worms that are born between the skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This illness is called in our land "cattle disease" because it often affects cattle,
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	"And there is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, which travels throughout the body ascending and descending."
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	"and it is felt well as it goes from limb to limb, until it arrives at the skin where it will stay;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	"And it is a cause of putrefaction of certain humors, like those that come from worms and serpents in the belly."
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	"and its harmfulness is doubted, for when it goes through the body and climbs to the head, it comes to the eye,"
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	"sometimes it enters and destroys the eye; this happens often."
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	"When you see it being drawn out and extracted, one can only be sure that it is there when it moves:"
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	"So then you must tie the wound both above and below with a very tight strong ligature,"
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	"then cut open and draw it out, and if the worm is deeply embedded in the flesh and you cannot find it,"
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	"then cauterize with fire until it dies."
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	"And the greatest harm that it does is that it can cause blindness, as we have said;"
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	"And if you see it coming near the head close to the eye, press down firmly on the eyebrow below it, then cut open and draw it out."
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	"And one must use medicinal treatments to cleanse the body of corrupt humors causing disease,"
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	"and beware of rotten foods."
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	"Of the pain that comes from windiness"
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	"This illness is called in our land 'vaquir' and it is a pain that occurs in certain limbs,"
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	"And then the limb moves from member to member; and I have seen what I tell you."
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	"I was called to a sick woman, and when I uncovered her arm, I saw a small swelling in the hollow of her arm;"
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	"and shortly thereafter, she saw rise up at the shoulder like a worm,"
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	more swiftly than anything else, like quicksilver as it flows from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain departed from that place and fastened itself in the shoulder,"
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	"and then shortly after it spread throughout her body until it reached her other arm;"
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	"Then she told me that she was always turning around the body, as I saw her."
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	"I wondered greatly how she could move thus from limb to limb because I had never seen this disease behave in such a way."
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	"However, I had often heard it said that pain can move from place to another,"
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I had never seen this happen in the manner that I saw it in this woman;"
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	"and I thought to myself that it was perhaps because the woman had a dry body and exposed hollows,"
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	"and thus appeared that constrained wind."
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	"but they do not appear in this manner to those who are delicate and have moist bodies and filled hollows."
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	"And when you see someone cured of this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears as we have described,"
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	"if the skin above and below suddenly raises up and then sinks down until that constrained wind escapes from its hiding place;"
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	"and cauterize the spot. And if you do not see it with your own eyes,"
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	"then have the patient take remedies to expel wind such as fetid pills and pills of serpentine, and other similar things."
Des saiettes	"Regarding Sighs"
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	"Sighs are various according to their appearances and the parts of the body where they occur."
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	"The varieties of sighs include those that have large points, small ones, those with hairs or bristles, and those that are smooth;"
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	"and some that have two angles, some that are long, and others that have fragments or bits."
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	"And those sighs that occur in any limb do so in two ways: either by growing out from the main limb,"
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	"such as brain, heart, liver, lung, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar limbs."
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	"Now when it occurs in any part of these limbs, the signs of death that I will tell you about later will appear:"
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	"but you must be careful to remove this sigh because death comes afterward in many dispositions;"
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	"And when this ill sign does not appear and the sigh is not deep, then draw it out and treat the wound."
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	"When a sigh falls into the brain and pierces the bone, causing the optic nerve that is above the brain to spring forth,"
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	"it indicates that there is a sigh in the brain. Other signs include darkness before the eyes and dimness of sight, redness and swelling in the eyes, inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasm and mixture of understanding, vomiting of bile;"
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	"and perhaps there will be fluid from the nostrils or ears; sometimes speech and voice are lost."
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	"And suddenly moist white matter like feathers flows from the wound, and also sparks of flesh are emitted;"
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	"If these signs appear to you, then be careful about treatment, and draw out the sigh if it is not already inside."
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	"The signs that a sigh has fallen into the heart are that it is near the left nipple and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty;"
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	"and sometimes the sigh moves like a bird's feather; black blood appears on the surface; coldness and cold sweat come forth; fainting occurs:"
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	"You must then be certain that death is imminent."
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	"The signs of a sigh that has entered the lung are that foam comes forth from the wound, the throat swells up, the patient changes color and sighs loudly and asks for cold air."
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	"And if the sigh enters the covering of the lung, it is near the ribs. There will be much wheezing and great pain, with loud sighs; all the shoulder limbs move."
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	"And if a sigh falls into the stomach, sometimes undigested food may emerge from the wound."
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	"And if a sigh falls into the abdomen and much wind rushes out through the intestines, there is no hope for recovery or for drawing out the sigh."
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	"And if a sigh falls into the bladder, urine flows forth and there is diarrhea; the patient feels great pain. You should know that the wound is mortal."
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	"The other limbs such as the face, neck, throat, shoulder, auxiliary limbs, spine of the back, forearm, thigh, and similar limbs are safe according to various conditions."
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	"When a sigh is in the nerve or artery and it is not venomous (as I will tell you happened to me so that you may do likewise),"
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	"It happened to one man that a sigh fell into his eyelid at the root of the nose:"
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	"I drew it out from beneath the ear's fatty tissue on the other side and he recovered without any injury."
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	"And I drew out another sigh that fell into the fat of the eye below the eyelid:"
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	"and the sigh was inverted, and I could only grasp its tip facing the skin;"
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	"It was as large as an archer's bow without touching any bone or ear; the eye recovered and suffered no ill effects."
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	"I drew out another sigh from the throat of a Christian man, and it was Arabic in shape with ears:"
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	"I shaved his beard and worked so carefully that I drew it out, and the Christian recovered."
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	"And I drew out another sigh from a man who had fallen into his abdomen, believing he would die;"
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	"but after thirty days had passed, his condition did not change."
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	"I cut into the sigh and hooked it out through its hollow end, drawing it forth without any ill effects occurring."
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	"And I saw another man in whom a sigh had fallen into his back and the wound was healed over;"
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	"and the sigh remained inside him without changing his natural disposition."
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	"He suffered no harm in any of his natural works or functions."
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	"And I saw another man into whose face a sigh had fallen and the wound had healed over;"
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	"and it remained there without causing him great pain; many others are similar."
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	"I drew out another sigh from one of the king's nobles, who had fallen into his nostril;"
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	"And it was slightly inclined towards the right side and entirely inverted;"
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	"I was called to treat him after three days had passed, finding the wound very narrow."
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	"I probed for it with great care and did not feel anything;"
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	"And he felt pain and discomfort beneath his right ear."
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	"I thought that it was due to the tip of the sigh;"
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	"I applied a plaster made from atractive digestive ointment so that the wound would not swell;"
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	"And then I saw the sigh's opening."
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	"I applied the plaster for several days, and the wound healed again, but the patient remained ill for a long time;"
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	"until he felt the sigh inside his nostril one day; he told me so."
