Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	"I applied a hot, corrosive medicine to the wound for many days until it opened."
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	"and I tried [to close] it, and felt that the head of the joint was in its proper place;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I applied this hot medicine to the opening of the wound until the head of the joint became clearly visible;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	"And the time limit of four months was well exceeded."
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	"And then she opened the wound where I had put forceps, and tried to pull it from one side and the other, but could not remove it."
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	"So I did not stop trying and devising ways of instruments until one day I took them with well-made forceps."
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	"As will be explained at the end of this chapter, so that I could pull it and heal the wound."
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	"And the physicians judged that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:"
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	"I then restored it, and the wound was healed, and the patient was completely healthy."
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	"Now I have told you about the extraction of some teeth,"
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	"So that you will base your treatment on what I have not mentioned, because books cannot cover everything;"
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	"But the wise master compares little things and what is present and lacking,"
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	"Finds nine works and nine instruments for dealing with extraordinary things that happen in this field."
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	"I say that teeth leave the members where they are implanted only in two ways:"
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	"Either through the place where they entered or through another part."
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	"And that which jumps out through the same place where it entered is an entering tooth, and sometimes happens now."
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	"And if it does not jump out now, let it remain until the flesh has completely grown around it and the exit is closed;"
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	"And also if it is implanted in the bone and cannot come out, leave it like that for some days, and move it every day;"
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	"And then it will come out, and if not, surround it completely with one thin drill until the place around is widened, and then pull it."
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	"If the tooth is implanted in the bone of the head and goes as far as one of the cavities of the brain,"
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	"Do not pull it out, but let it remain until it becomes aligned after some days,"
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	"because if the tooth comes as far as this, it is the wisdom tooth."
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	"And if the tooth is implanted only in the bone and does not come to the surface,"
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	"and the patient remains for some days without any bad symptoms, then it can be pulled."
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if it is very deeply implanted and cannot come out, then apply poultices around it as I have told you; then treat the place until it is healthy."
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	"If the tooth is buried in the flesh of the body so that one cannot see it, search for it with all diligence;"
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	"And if you feel it, pull it out with some appropriate instrument."
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	"But if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the tooth,"
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	"then cut until the wound is large enough;"
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	"And pull the tooth if you can, and if there are roots to which it adheres,"
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	"then cut away the flesh that is stuck on both sides of the root as much as possible,"
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	"Then break or bend the ears of the arrow until you can pull it out."
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	"And carefully make sure not to break the arrow while pulling it out."
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, then wait until the place around is properly prepared, then pull it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	But if there is an obstruction of blood flow that opposes this, follow what we have said about treatment in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and beware of incising the nerve and the vein, and devise how you can move and pull out the bone without danger.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	Whether quickly or slowly, whether firmly or gently; and place the patient according to how it was when the bone fell in upon him
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for that is the greatest help that can be done, and if you cannot do otherwise, then place it according to what the signs indicate.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The bone that protrudes from elsewhere, where some part of it is visible, or where the skin appears swollen nearby:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Cut thereupon until forceps can grasp it, then extract it. If it comes out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand around until it enters into the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it alone for now, and then resume the extraction until it comes out completely
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	And if any fragment of bone remains, push it all back in
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	And if the fragment falls out and you see that you need to administer a splint, then apply one made from soft wood.
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the point of the bone enters into the wood of the splint; and then bind it firmly in place.
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if the bone is impacted, apply a splint with a pointed end entering inside to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the bone is infected, it is necessary for you to cut away all the flesh around where the veins are located if possible
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	Then treat the wound as it ought to be treated.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the bone falls into the thigh, or belly, bladder or ribs and is close by, then cut thereupon if you can
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and take care not to cut the vein and the nerve, then extract it, then sew up the wound if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And treat it until it is healed
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to treat bones is similar to a bird's beak, and here is an illustration of that shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds of them: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the bone fragment.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the binding splint is also like the feather of a bird
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	to bind at the point of the bone fragment, as shown here:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	Here is the shape of forceps for grasping and pulling:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	There are 21 common veins of which 6 are located at the head.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	That is to say:.ii. veins behind the ears called the two "ear veins";
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	"And the two arteries that appear in each temple;"
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	And two veins which are in the two arms of the two eyes, which are called "aspires".
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	And the vein that is within the forehead; and the vein that is at the head of the nose
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	And the two sinews which are in the neck
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	And the two veins that are above the mouth, and these are the veins called "augereich".
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two veins that are beneath the tongue
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins commonly known are five in each arm
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	The first is the cephalic vein, and it is on the right side, which common people call the "vein of the head".
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	And the second is called "fast", and it is composed of the cephalic and the basilica
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and common people call it the "vein of the heart"; and the basilic vein is on the left side
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	And they call it the "vein of the belly", and it is above the forearm
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and this is the one that can be seen most clearly in the elbow pit
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the salvation vein is the vein that lies between the little finger and the ring finger, which has two branches
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	In the leg and in the foot there are three veins: one is under the hollow of the ankle on the left side
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	And the second saphenous vein which is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein called "Ness" which is in the ankle of the other side
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg there are three veins underneath those
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The knowledge of the veins that follow after the ears helps old catarhatics and migraine sufferers
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	And the qualities of the knower are such that he should raise the head of the sick person
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the place where the veins are with a coarse cloth, then make the sick person turn their neck towards one side
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until you see two veins appear behind the ears in two places that depend on the head
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	then press with your fingers where you feel the pulse under your thumb, and squeeze gently
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	Then take the lancet and insert it beneath the vein until it reaches the bone, then lift your hand up along the entire length of the vein upstream
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut through the skin and the vein with two fingers wide apart, and let the blood flow out until you see enough
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then press and bind it, until it is healed
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	And I have already spoken of the incision and cautery in the first book
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	Knowledge of the two arteries that are in the two temples is helpful for old migraine sufferers
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and useful against sudden illness, customary ophthalmia and for treating tears that flow from the eyes
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	And these are the qualities of the knower:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	"And it is necessary for the patient to stretch their neck so that the two veins appear clearly;"
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	"And feel the pulse under your two fingers, and then squeeze inwards;"
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	Then lift your little finger up high onto the vein above, and insert the lancet underneath.
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and raise the vein up, and cut it, just like you did with the other two veins, and let blood flow according to your needs
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then release the patient, and press your thumb on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on top;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	Then tie it tightly and leave it until it is healed. We have spoken about their cutting and extraction at the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The healing of the frontal vein is just as valuable as the cephalic one for treating old facial diseases, migraines, and redness;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	Its quality is that the patient twists their neck until the vein appears
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the instrument called "fossor", of which this is the shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein, and press firmly with your hand or something else, allowing blood to flow out according to the desired quantity;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then untie the patient's neck, and tie the vein tightly until it is healed. Often this operation is done with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, the flames should not be too narrow, and tie it diagonally, because the bone is close by, and sometimes the flame breaks when it is too thin.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The healing of the two veins that are in the two arms helps with the eyes, and with dandruff, redness, and inflammation of the eye, and with facial diseases;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	Its quality is that the patient twists their neck in any direction, just like before
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then heal it, and make the healing diagonal, a little long and a little wide because there is no flesh in that area.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is too thin, it may break. Then apply pressure to stop the bleeding, until you have enough blood. Then tie cotton on top and tie it tightly.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The healing of the vein in the nose is useful for ague, sudden madness, and facial diseases,
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	As migraine pain and redness come to the face, especially when it's chronic.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	The symptom of the illness is that the patient strains their neck first, then strains their nose towards your left hand.
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	"And take a long, subtle flame, and insert it between the two nostrils."
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	"because the passage does not open well, and breathing will now begin to return;"
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	"And do not cut too deep, and let blood according to your need, then bind it with a bandage for one night, as it is quickly restored."
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	"This is the form of the fever:"
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	"The juice of two onions aids in the treatment of ulcers, and the beginning of measles, and many diseases, and empetigine, and corrosion, and herpes, and eruptions;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	"And the quality of this juice is that the patient will stretch his neck beneath both his arms, as we have said;"
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	"and let the master be standing above the head of the patient, and the patient lying on one seat,"
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	"then wash the vein with warm water a little bit, then let blood temperately, as much as is necessary;"
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	"then do the same to the other vein, then untie the bandage, and press both veins moderately,"
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	"so that the patient is not strangled; and leave him until morning, so that the wound is healed."
De la sainie des leivres	"On the juice of oats"
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	"The juice of the veins of the lips above aids in coldness in the mouth, and corruption of gums, and fissures of the lips, and nose and around."
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	"And the quality of this juice is to make the patient sit in front of you, and press his neck as I have said;"
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	"then turn the lip, and look at both veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left,"
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	"And know them by these signs: they are black, and there are small black veins around them:"
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	"then cut both of them, but if you do not recognize them, and are in doubt,"
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	"then cut the largest one on each side, and do exactly the same for both veins that are above and below, for it is the same manner."
De la sainie desoz la lengue	"On the juice beneath the tongue"
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	"The juice of the veins beneath the tongue aids after the cephalic juice, and is for the stretching of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth."
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	"And the quality of this juice is that the patient sits between your hands in front of the sun, lifts his tongue and looks beneath on each side for a black vein:"
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	"then cut both of them, but do not go too deep, for beneath are the arteries."
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	"The veins of the arm which are commonly used are let according to two manners:"
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	"either by piercing with one blow of a broad mirror or a fine olive-shaped blade like a cutting edge, and is called ‘anesil’;"
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	"And they are broad and fine according to the width and stretching of the veins."
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	"The shape of the mirror blow is very well known, and is wide as you see:"
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	"And it is necessary to use it to open the veins of the head that are smooth and full of visible thick blood, which contain thick and turbid blood;"
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	"and this is the shape of the olive blow:"
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	"And it is more pointed and fine, and is for letting the veins that have thin, lemon-colored blood."
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	"The juice of the basilica vein, which is one of these veins, aids diseases that are beneath the throat, neck, breast, and abdomen;"
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	"And it is necessary for the surgeon to let it freely and beware of the artery that is beneath."
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	"And if he cuts the artery and blood begins to flow profusely, then it is necessary to stop it, as I have said;"
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	"and the blow should not be piercing, but cutting like an ‘anesil’."
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	"And if the basilica does not appear manifestly, then it is necessary to draw it out and change to another [vein]."
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	"or you want any part of it, or you let in its place the vein on the arm: it appears manifestly;"
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	"And cut it with the ‘anesil’ blow, as we have said."
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	"And if you want to know the place of letting, then it is necessary first to draw out the arm and touch the place until you feel the pulse;"
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	"then mark the place with ink and then tie the arm, and cut the vein with the ‘anesil’ blow;"
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	"and be careful not to strike the artery when you see the place swollen, for it is from the artery. Avoid it therefore."
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	"And if you see something protruding upwards like a child’s urine, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is blood from the artery:"
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	"then hurry and press your finger down firmly, then remove your finger if the bleeding stops, which often happens;"
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	"if not, tie the arm and leave it thus, and do not move the patient; he should be quiet and not move until he is healed."
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	"And if the bleeding does not stop and he faints, and there is no doctor present, then cut the artery if it appears, for its head contracts; and stop the bleeding."
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	"And take a piece of fig bark, split it open, and take one half and tie it tightly around until the next day;"
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	"If the bleeding stops, that is good. If not, then treat it with powders that stop blood, as we have said;"
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	"and the stopping of bleeding is not harmful in many positions for the small place of the wound and the power of the ligature of the arm."
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	"The letting of the vein in the middle helps to draw off blood from the head above and from the body below,"
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	"because it is composed of the basilica and the cephalic veins, as we have said;"
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	"And it is necessary for the surgeon to beware of the nerve that is beneath, and not to go too deep, lest he find the nerve;"
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	"and it swells and the sick person is harmed, and perhaps he cannot heal."
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	"And this nerve often appears, and if it does not appear in some men because of its thinness, then you should let it with the ‘anesil’ instrument; and avoid the nerve to your power."
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	"And if there is a vein between the two nerves, cut it lengthwise;"
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	"The letting of the cephalic vein helps to draw off blood from the head and aids eyestrain;"
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	"And it is necessary to let with a piercing blow using the olive-shaped or mirror blow, for this vein is the safest of all veins because there is neither nerve nor artery beneath it."
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	"Nevertheless, one should seek out the easiest place and do no harm if one misses on the first try; then one begins again;"
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	"And sometimes the place swells in some men when one misses on the first try, but it does no harm."
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	"The quality of letting depends on your judgment."
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	"The first thing you should know about letting blood is that letting is not prescribed except for preserving health;"
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	"and to avoid future illnesses;"
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	"And letting should be done in one of the three veins found on the arm: namely, the cephalic, basilic, and median cubital veins;"
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	"And one should let blood at the beginning of Lent, in autumn and winter after meals, when the sign of repletion appears;"
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	"And one should let blood on the first or third day, after two or three hours from noon."
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The sick person who is given this medicine has no fixed time for taking it, but whenever there is need by day or night, in all hours and at all times;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	nor should this medicine be given to children under 14 years old, nor to women who are pregnant until after their seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should the elderly over 60 years of age receive this medicine.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when someone wishes to take this medicine in any way, it is necessary that they first cleanse their bowels with a light enema
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if there is much retained feces, so that the veins do not draw the harmful impurities from the bowels into the main limbs;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	nor should this medicine be taken by those who are too fond of meat or those who are drunkards, until they abstain from such habits, nor by those with dropsy;
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and beware of taking this medicine after a bout of colic pain, vomiting, diarrhea, excessive menstrual flow in women, hard labor, wakefulness, fasting, or any weakness throughout the body caused by external injury or internal illness.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	Then subtly dissolve the humors if the skin is thick, through foods and drinks and medicines, if you have the power to do so;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	Then enter into a bath, if nothing prevents it, in order to subtly refine the blood
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and take this medicine on an empty stomach around the third hour of the day, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	And guard yourself that day from work, overeating, and lustful activities, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be at ease and joyous, and let the one administering the medicine be taller than the recipient, and rub the arms three or four times with a friction cloth.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	Then remove the lien around the middle, for if it is too tight or loose, the blood will not flow properly;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	And then rub the place gently with the hands until the veins swell and can be felt;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	Then let the one administering the medicine moisten their finger with a little old oil, and then place their left thumb on that vein below the place where they wish to administer the medicine
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein is neither too full nor empty when struck.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that flee like strings when struck, and some that are filled with windiness
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	so that when one places the finger on top, it retreats with the finger, and cannot open the vein, and thus one is of these;
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	And if it opens the vein, then the wound is too narrow, so that the one administering the medicine must be skilled in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens on the first attempt, that is good. But if not, then begin again a little below or above that place immediately, if the place is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the place is swollen and the patient is afraid, let it be left alone for one or two days without binding the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	perhaps an ulcer will appear there. Do not enter into a bath, and then resume administering the medicine if it pleases him.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	And if the opening is small, or the blood flows subtly and you doubt that enough blood is issuing forth as you wish, then strike with the whole finger directly into that same opening.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And open it a little quickly before the place becomes swollen, for this happens many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the place becoming swollen, do not resume administering the medicine, and apply a little oil mixed with lime, for it lightens the body of blood and is very beneficial in this place.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And thus administer the mixture of oil each time you administer medicine to the veins, in order to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	And this same mixture also helps against trial and bowels, when it is applied to the place, for it makes the blood flow more subtly and spreads it out if it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there appears a large ulcer there, which happens frequently, especially when the vein is not opened but only touched that one time and the opening of the vein is small
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	then hurry and apply a sponge moistened in hot water mixed with salt to the place, and let it remain for an hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	And you must do this after the blood has issued forth from the vein, and if there remains on the place some blackness or greenness for a few days afterward, it will not harm him.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if you wish to apply something else, then use a little aloë or myrrh mixed with juice of calamint, masterwort, or the like.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times an ulcer and appearance appear during the administering of basilica: therefore place your hand upon it, and if you find the place soft under the pressure of your hand, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore be sure not to apply anything that we have spoken of here, for perhaps some blood will flow from the artery; but make one plaster dry to harden the place, and then cleanse it with another cleansing until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw off the blood according to each person's constitution and the color of their blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it issue forth until it becomes red. And if it flows thickly, let it flow until it becomes more subtly flowing. And if it is too hot, let it cool before striking again.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And for one who is full and fat and needs bloodletting, it is necessary to make a larger wound and use a wide finger
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for one who is weak, do the opposite: make the wound small and administer often, and it should be administered by cutting across, not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this manner of bloodletting is safe from excessive loss of blood and injury to the nerves, and it is more beneficial than bloodletting by length or breadth.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for one whose body fails during bloodletting, it is necessary to give him bread moistened with juice of pomegranates; if he is overheated, draw off his blood three or four times
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if he is of cold complexion, let him eat before bloodletting bread moistened in syrup of musk or aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if he faints during bloodletting after losing much blood, it is necessary for him to inhale broth of meat and fragrant syrup
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use other things that we have spoken of in the chapter on syncope for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to evacuate one arm and have bloodletting done again afterward, it is necessary, when he is weakened by much bleeding, that he be bled a little at a time according to his continuous strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wishes to evacuate one arm after the first bloodletting and has a strong body should be bled seven hours after the first bleeding or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wishes to have bloodletting done on another part of the body should be bled on the second day or the third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For there is much blood in the body that has already become heated and causes fever. Therefore, it is necessary to draw off a large quantity of blood and widen the wound as much as possible until it flows evenly.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	And since you observe all conditions for bloodletting and place your hand on the pulse when bleeding begins, ensure that the mouth does not come in place of the wound.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	"And this happens many times when the surgeon is negligent; "
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	"And it's not enough to simply untie the arm and make blood flow out a second time when the hole is closed by pressing hard upon it,"
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	"nor if it is curved, should he quickly extend his arm, for this would be harmful."
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	"But let him remain until it bleeds again the second time; or else poke with the tip of the flame until the blood that is frozen at the mouth of the wound flows out,"
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	"And pour on some watery salted water, then press lightly upon it."
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	"But if the vein is swollen, do not let go nor squeeze too hard until the inflammation has subsided."
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	"And if it becomes necessary to draw blood a second time, do so either in the same vein or in another one, or even in the other arm."
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	"The vein in the arm is opened in place of the vein in the head because it is more accessible."
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	"And the method for bleeding is that the patient immerses their hand in hot water until the veins are red;"
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	"then tie it moderately so that the vein appears well; then make the cut now across, not too wide nor too long;"
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	"and make the hole wide; bleed as close to the joint of the hand as possible. If blood cannot flow out, immerse the hand in hot water and let it bleed into the water until enough blood has flowed."
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	"And if this is done in summer, do not immerse the hand in hot water, for it is better to do so in winter than in summer."
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	"And bleeding from this vein is safer than from any other veins because there are no arteries or nerves present."
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	"The bleeding of the vein at the base of the thumb is beneficial for all diseases of the liver, and this is how it should be done:"
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	"Press the hand gently and immerse it in hot water until the vein swells enough to be visible;"
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	"And make the cut across; if you cut too deep, it will not matter."
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	"But do not cut too deeply because nerves lie beneath all skin and flesh;"
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	"Then immerse the hand in hot water again if the blood is frozen in the wound and cannot flow out."
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	"And when you have drawn enough blood, apply oil and a little salt to quickly cauterize the wound, and do this for each cut."
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	"The bleeding of the vein in the left hand is beneficial for those suffering from mumps, and it should be done in the same way as I have described for the right hand."
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	"The bleeding of the vein at the elbow is beneficial for all diseases that affect the lower body;"
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	"such as those affecting the buttocks, retention of urine, and diseases of the loins, thighs, and old legs, and similar conditions."
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	"The qualities of this bleeding are that the patient should immerse their foot in hot water and rub the vein until it swells;"
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	"then tie above the ankle; the vein is at the ankle, and many nerves run below the foot;"
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	"So cut either where the largest vein or nerve appears, or at the ankle."
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	"And if you bleed on the foot, beware of the nerves that lie beneath. Make the cut across, like cutting a slice; and let the blood flow freely."
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	"And if blood cannot flow out, immerse the foot in water again and allow the vein to empty completely."
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	"If the first cut does not bleed well, make a second one higher up because the spot is scarred;"
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	"do not worry about nerves, as we have said, and do the same for the elbow of the other arm."
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	"The location of the sciatic vein is on the outside ankle, and bleeding it is beneficial for lower back pain when caused by hot blood."
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	"The qualities of this bleeding are that the patient should sit in a bath and press four fingers above the ankle while twisting;"
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	"otherwise the vein will not open. But if it does open, bleed as much as you can, and make the cut across."
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	"And it is important that you cut deeply because the spot is hard, and many people have this vein blocked."
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	"But if you cannot find it, bleed any vein that appears on the back of the foot near the little toe, but beware of nerves;"
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	"And let as much blood flow out as you can see, then untie the bandage, apply cotton and press firmly; now it is bled."
Des sainies de ventouse	"Regarding bleeding with leeches:"
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	"Leeches are made from horn, glass, or earthenware and can be used in two ways: either by pricking and drawing blood, or without pricking."
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	"And this leeching that does not involve pricking can be done in two ways: either with fire, or without fire;"
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	"and bleeding by pricking and drawing blood is performed at fourteen locations on the body."
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	"The first location is entirely on the head, and the second is within the neck;"
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	"and two more on each side of the neck, plus one beneath the chin;"
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	"And bleeding at the shoulders, and bleeding above the hips;"
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	"and bleeding on each arm and bleeding on each leg."
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	"And bleeding at the ankles. And note that leeching does not draw much blood except for small veins scattered throughout the flesh."
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	"Therefore it does not weaken anyone, unlike bleeding from veins;"
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	"And it should not be administered in any case where the whole body is filled with excess matter."
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	"But if it is necessary to leech due to illness or custom, we will administer them every hour at the beginning or end of the month, and also in between during each season."
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	"For there are some people who, when they need to be leeched, have heavy heads;"
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	"And others find that they experience fullness and redness in their face, head, neck, and darkness before the eyes;"
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	"And some people find a drop of blood in their mouth, and they have an enlarged tongue that bleeds easily."
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	"Some people dream of seeing blood and being wounded or bitten, etc."
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	"And when we see these signs, especially during the month, we will order them to be leeched three hours after noon."
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	"The bleeding of the temple helps with headaches ... that come to them, but it should not be done after evacuating the entire body."
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	"And this leeching is in place of bleeding from the cephalic vein;"
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	"But those who have a cold temperament or are phlegmatic should not use it, as it causes them great harm."
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	"Therefore elderly people and those with cold-headed conditions should not use it."
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	"And those who often bleed themselves become forgetful. Therefore, the leech should be placed a little lower to avoid forgetfulness."
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	"Leeaching on the neck is in place of bleeding from the head and basilic veins. Therefore it is useful for those with narrow chests."
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	"And it helps with breaking wind from the stomach, coughing, and excess."
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	"However, it should not be placed too firmly, as if it sticks too tightly, it can cause forgetfulness or harm to the stomach or heart."
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	"Windings around two ribs of the neck are helpful for headaches, and eye pain, migraine, strangulation, and toothache root pain."
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	"And it is located at the entrance to the basilica; and you must order the surgeon that he press his hand on setting, that he not cut the artery, nor let blood flow."
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	"Windings under the chin are good for mouth disease, gum decay, and similar mouth diseases; and they are located at the entrance of two lips."
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	"The shoulder windings are good for diseases that come from heat and swelling."
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	"Windings of the ribs are as beneficial as three veins of the arm."
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	because it attracts blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	And instruct the senior not to cut too deeply, for the place is bare of flesh, and lies under nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping glass placed on the buttock is useful for hemorrhoids and lower diseases, and the cupping glass must be large and made of bronze, so that it can draw well; and sometimes if it is too fine, it may break and cause large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	Cupping glasses on the legs draw openly because they attract blood from all over the body and are useful for old pains in the kidneys, sciatica, bladder, and joints; they replace two sophenes and two ankles, but they also weaken the body after prolonged use and cause swelling in various conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying the cupping glass is as follows: first apply it empty, and suck moderately, then place it quickly and move it evenly without stopping until you see the skin turn red and swollen with blood visible on the surface. Then remove it and replace the cups, taking care to observe the condition of the body because some people have thin flesh and tender pores, so you should strike only once, make the wounds wide but not too deep, and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to thin out the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to strike a third time. And when we want to draw only a little blood at a time, one stroke will suffice.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we want to draw a lot of blood, we should strike repeatedly. And if the blood is thick, we should strike deeply, and the endpoint is when the heart pierces suddenly
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And for those who have thick skin and hard flesh with tight pores, you should oil the places of the cupping glasses with aperitive and dissolventive oil
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in summer, with violet oil or sweet almond oil or pumpkin seed oil
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in winter, with mustard oil or lily oil or chamomile oil or something similar
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excessiveness is thick and cold, use almond oil or balm oil or aniseed oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And for those who have tender flesh with large pores, it is not necessary to put any oil there
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but after the cupping treatment, they should be washed with rose water or cold water or mulberry water or pumpkin water or porcellain water, or something similar
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have a lot of moisture should rise using this method: with myrtle water or sumac water and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have a lot of excessiveness should rise with old wine or sour water or decoction of anise or chamomile or similar things
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	And one should not apply cupping glasses before or during the bath, but afterwards, one hour or two hours later; and do not sleep after the cupping treatment.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And it is necessary that he/she washes himself/herself when they are about to undergo cupping treatment and when they have finished being cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware of those who are cupping themselves if they are choleric in temperament and if their blood is too hot and inflamed
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	They should take cold things such as pomegranates, endive, lettuce with vinegar, and similar things
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And eat young kids, castrated ram meat, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those with cold complexion should take honey syrup and medium fragrant wine that is between old and new, and eat little meat of young kids and small birds and pigeons.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	And on the day when they will undergo cupping treatment, they should drink more than they eat
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	Some people should be given treacle or musk sometimes before or after cupping to strengthen the main organs
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And let the blood be subtle, but those who are hot should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The cupping glasses that are placed without striking are those placed on the liver, spleen, abdomen, face, back, and buttocks. These areas do not tolerate being struck.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	And it is only done for attracting blood from one member to another.
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	For example, we place cupping glasses on the breasts when nursing to remove viscosity from that member. Similarly, we place cupping glasses on the abdomen and face to reduce the size of those members
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	And it removes pain when there is congestion or stone, by its attractive virtue it may dissolve the congestion or remove the stone from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	And thus it does when placed on the liver and spleen when there is retained wind
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	These cupping glasses are administered empty for suction only. Sometimes they are used together with fire, and sometimes they are filled with tepid water
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	like in diseases of the pleura, and in this manner one fills the cupping glass with hot water alone or with water in which suitable herbs have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the cupping glass administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it should be two fingers wide and half a palm deep, and have on its side around the middle one small hole like that of a needle
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	"And if made of brass, soften it first so it does not scorch the patient when applied to the limb;"
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	"And have in the middle a transverse rod of brass or iron, to place an oil lamp upon,"
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	"and they should be large or small depending on the diseases and age of those who take them;"
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	because the cupping glasses for children are different from those for adults, and those for thin people are different from those for fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	"One should thus place this cupping glass on the limb:"
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	Take a candle wick or one linen thread, and insert it through the hole in the cupping glass.
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	"So that the brightness is at the bottom of the cupping glass so it does not burn the patient."
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	"Then place it on the limb and hold both thumbs over the hole we mentioned so that when one wants to do so, steam can be released, and then remove the cupping glass."
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	"And apply the ointment as before, and repeat it often if necessary."
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	"In the case of the cupping glass used for the disease of pleurisy in an acute state, it has neither spout nor hole, and is not administered except when it is full of water, and is placed on the limb alone."
et c’est li forme:	"And this is its shape:"
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	"Suction cups are used only in limbs where it is not possible to apply cupping glasses due to their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similarly the ears."
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	"And in areas of bare skin, such as the back or neck, and other similar places;"
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	"The quality of its use is that when one finds suction cups which are in fresh water that is clear and without impurities, then those should be taken."
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	"And places them in fresh water for as long as they become familiar with it and have nothing inside them;"
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	"Then clean the veins and cupping glasses, then rub the limb until it becomes red, and place the suction cups on it."
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	"And when they are full and suck, if this is a place where one can apply cupping glasses, then apply them for that helps very much afterwards."
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	"If not, then lift the limb gently and then rinse it with water, well done, and then squeeze it."
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	"And if the limb is too dry after the body of the suction cups, then moisten one cloth of linen in cold water and place it so that the cups are stretched."
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	"And if the cups are multiplied, then apply powdered vitriol or chalk, etc., until they become tightened;"
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	"Or you can put on the limb half of peeled fava beans and leave them there until they stick to the limb, it will now be tightened;"
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	"And if more are needed, then take other suction cups."
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	"And if the suction cups do not want to adhere, then rub the limb with fresh blood or prick it with a needle until the cup adheres."
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	"Then place them on and as soon as they sense the blood, they will adhere;"
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	"And when you see that they are full, then apply a little powder of ground aloe and salt or ashes, and they will now suck."
Ci comence li livre des brisures	"Here begins the book of fractures"
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	"This chapter is very necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the treatment of fractures and dislocations."
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	"Know, dear son, that foolish physicians neglect this chapter, as they have never seen any of the ancient books nor read a letter from them;"
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	"And because of this reason, knowledge of this subject is rare in our land, for I found no good one among them."
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	"And I know nothing about it except through the knowledge of ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have treated this subject with experience and by custom throughout my life;"
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	"And I have already described for you in this chapter what is contained therein, and I have summarized it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the tools that are used, just as I did in these two preceding chapters."
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	"It is therefore necessary that we say in the prologue of this book the contents of the words and chapters where wise men place their understanding and remain on the truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others."
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	"I say that when fracture, dislocation, torsion or concussion occurs in anyone, it is necessary for you to hurry and clean the injured on both sides, if anything is not whole, such as weakness of body, childbirth, or old age;"
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	"Or if the time is not very hot or too cold, and avoid cold foods, such as cold drinks, chicken meat and rabbit meat, do not drink wine nor eat fatty meats, and do not eat too much food that fills the veins with blood, until you doubt the formation of a hot aposteme, nor an expansion of matter in the limb; then bring the sick back to their usual diet."
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	"And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that the sick person be nourished with foods that cause good growth and are moistening, such as cooked wheat in water, rice, testicles, pears, apples, cow's milk, eggs, fresh fish, and similar things."
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	"For with this nourishment muscles grow back more quickly and the fracture heals faster;"
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	"And know that the bones of old and decrepit people, nor those that are too tender like the bones of small children, cannot be well restored or united according to their nature due to the weakness of the limbs;"
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	"But rather use a large splint to support the broken bone and join the limb together until it regains its former strength; do not remove any part of its work, and therefore it is necessary to nourish them with fatty foods, as we have said."
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	"And know that fractures are diverse in many ways."
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	"For the fracture of the head is different from that of the arm or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures."
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	"There are fractures that occur suddenly, like falling from a horse, and others that occur gradually, like the splitting of a feather for writing."
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	"And there are fractures with wounds, and fractures with only a small crack."
