Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	"And each kind has its own method and proper tool for restoration, according to what the fracture comes into its place;"
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	"and a fracture of bone is known by the fact that the place is twisted and clearly visible through defect, and it sounds when pressed with the hand;"
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	"and when there is no twisting or sound upon touching, nor does the sick person feel much pain, then there is no fracture."
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	"But he may well have twisting, or cracking, or a small fracture."
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	"So do not move him by hand, but apply the medicines that come later and then gently immobilize him."
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	"And know that fractures that occur suddenly and separate the two parts are to be aligned evenly until hot inflammation comes;"
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	"and if hot inflammation comes, let it rest for some days until the inflammation is appeased;"
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	"then align it as evenly and gently as possible, and know that its restoration is easier than that of one with fragments; then immobilize it as necessary."
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	"And if the bone has broken fragments, then extend it on both sides if it is an arm or leg, or use your hand if it is a small limb, or use two cords or one cord and your hand;"
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	"and place the limb according to its natural shape so that when the broken parts of the limb are aligned, then carefully place the fragments in their proper places without causing injury or pain to the sick person;"
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	"And join the two ends of the bones according to their best forms."
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	"And feel it well with your hand if it seems not to be properly set: then raise it carefully and do not immobilize it too much nor press upon it as those do who cause hot inflammation and contracture in the limb through their improper handling, as we have often said."
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	"And when the limb is set, then instruct the patient well not to move it, neither waking nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other manner;"
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	"And ensure that the limb is secured so that the patient feels no pain."
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	"For if he feels any pain, then it is not set properly, and it must be put in such a position that he feels no pain;"
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	"And make sure it is reset correctly so that there are no twists when it is restored."
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	"The condition of the fractured limb depends on what I have told you."
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	"Know that fractured limbs are diverse in size, length and shape."
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	"But there are small limbs, such as arms and hands and similar ones; these should be wrapped with soft and fine linen cloths;"
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	"And those which are thick, such as thighs and legs; these should be wrapped with a wide and firm bandage, for the wide bandage encircles the entire large limb and squeezes it evenly on all sides so that there is no gap."
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	"Then tie it around with light bandages, three or four turns according to the limb, and tighten your hand slightly on all of the bandage. Then go up above the fracture and tighten less, so that the fracture can move a little away from the fracture."
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	"And loosen the bandage a little by little until you grasp most of the healthy part, then take another bandage and wrap it around again over the fractured area;"
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	"Then return to the part below the fracture and tighten it moderately, not too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first binding above;"
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	"Then place linen bandages or cloths between the bindings so that it is all even, then tie everything together with one strip, and then put on well-made splints if there is no inflammation or swelling."
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	"And if there is inflammation or heat, then put on something that cools and reduces heat and swelling, and leave it on for a few days;"
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	"Then tie around your splints, and they should be half the width of a strong cane or of oak wood used for stakes, or of date palm ribs, and they should look like this:"
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	"But the splint that is placed on the fracture itself should be a little thicker and wider than the others;"
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	"And it should also be as long as necessary for the limb's size or length;"
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	"Then tie around the splints just as you did in the first binding, then tie a bandage on top of them smoothly, as in the first binding over the fracture;"
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	"Then pull it tighter and loosen it again; and the thread should be medium-sized, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen;"
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	"For if the threads are thick, as I have seen in the works of foolish people who make their bindings with twisted flax cords, that is a great error. For the binding cannot be even if it is too thin, and there should not be more than two fingers' width between each splint."
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	"And if the patient is wounded by the edges of the splints after the bandaging on healthy areas, place linen bandages or wool wadding underneath them so that it does not bruise."
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	"When the wound is accompanied by a fracture and the skin is broken, I will speak about its treatment later on."
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	"And know that one should not bind all broken limbs with splints on the first day."
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	"For when a limb is large, one should not put splints on it until after five or six days, or more, depending on the likelihood of heat and inflammation occurring;"
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	"And here is the way that ancient poultices were made to restore fractures, dislocations, and twists: Take flour from the walls of the mill and mix it with many eggs. Use this mixture, neither too thin nor too thick, as needed. This is the common method for applying a poultice to restore fractures in various conditions, especially in women and young children, because it is not too hot nor too cold."
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	"Another method for making a poultice that restores fractures, dislocations, and twists: Take of bdellium and ladanum and wild marjoram and asafetida and gum arabic and myrrh, each 10 drams; aloes wood, 5 drams; aloeroot, 7 drams; grind them into a powder and mix it with many eggs. If the person's complexion is hot, use this poultice, for it has a good composition and quickly restores broken bones, and it is beneficial to many people."
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	"Another method for making a poultice that is beneficial for twists: Take of myrrh and vismalva, each 10 drams; myrrh and aloes wood, each 7 drams; acacia gum, 6 drams; balsam of Armenia, 10 drams; grind them well and mix with water or many eggs, and apply it."
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	"Another method for making a poultice for joints and dislocated bones that soothes pain and reduces inflammation and fracture: Take new linen and moisten it in warm water mixed with hot oil, then apply it to the area. This poultice does not restore, but it is good for soothing heat and inflammation, and it removes pain properly."
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	"Another method for making a poultice that restores broken bones: Take dried fig leaves and dock leaves, grind them together, and make a poultice."
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	"Another method for making a poultice to restore broken bones and to soften the remaining inflammation: Take of violet root, camomile flowers, violet petals, wheat flour, each one part; grind them together and mix with wine. If the limb is hot, mix it with coriander water or water, and apply it."
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	"Another method for making a stronger poultice when hard inflammation comes to the restoration of a limb: Take violet root, flax seed, balm, meadow saffron, and sagewort, each one part; grind them together and mix with salt water or fresh water or wine according to the heat of the limb and its rest."
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	"Hippocrates says in his book that one should not put anything on a broken limb to restore it except cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else more. He says that it should be between two, neither too soft nor too hard."
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	"And it seems to Galen that one should put dry and slightly warm things on a broken limb to restore it, such as myrrh, aloe, frankincense, and similar substances, as we have said."
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	"Another method for making a poultice that is beneficial for wounds and pain: Take myrrh and the cut hair of men or feathers of birds, and violet leaves, each an equal part; grind them together and make a poultice with it."
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	"And then remove it after a little while, and make sure that the patient does not feel any pain or movement of the bone from its place; do not remove it for many days."
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	"And if pain or itching comes to the place, without rest or swelling, then hurry up and remove it, and take away the poultice immediately; and take a light cloth and wet sea sponge, dip it in water, and wipe the place until the itching stops and the pain is appeased."
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then allow the limb to rest for an hour, then place dry linen moistened in water or rose oil on it, and tie it with a bandage until you are sure of a hot abscess.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let the inflammation of the limb rest, and let the pain be relieved, then resume the bandage gently, and a little plaster, and do not pull it too hard as before; and continue until it is healthy.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is hot and red and painful and swollen are all gone, and you need plaster and bandages again, then resume it, just as you did at first equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if the limb receives none of what we have said, do not untie it until after three or four or five or seven days; and sometimes leave it for twenty days, according to what is seen, until the fracture heals, and the alignment of the flesh approaches.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Then tighten the bandage more than before, and let the flesh grow together, as I have said previously; and if you see that the place dries out too much, know that no nourishment can come there.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Then apply warm water compresses all the time you untie it, and do this every third day, and slacken the bandage a little.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	Thus nourishment comes to the limb by this procedure, and it quickly remedies what foolish doctors do wrongly, namely setting the limb incorrectly: this is evil, and such procedures are poor, and I see nothing else but leaving it alone and working correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of the various types of fractures
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many different kinds of fractures, with diverse appearances, and their causes are distinct:
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Because it has fractures caused by blows from a sword, and the collarbone removes all the bone down to the socket which is beneath the bone, just like an axe on wood; and therefore this type of fracture is called "hachure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	When the sword strikes the bone from above without piercing it, and this type of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound of these two fractures is large or small
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is percussion that embeds, splits, or crushes from a fall onto stone, or from other similar causes.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating fracture that approaches the bone tissue beneath the bone or is above it, and this wound can be large or small
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a fracture that penetrates into the bone as thin as a hair, and this split is small, and therefore this type of fracture is called "capillary".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is caused by striking with stone or falling or something similar, and pushes a fragment of bone downwards, like a hammer hitting a pot, so that fragments enter inside
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more often in those who have moist bones in their head, such as the heads of children
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And all these types of fractures have small fragments that are disconnected like stars; and I will speak about this in its proper place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all types of fractures by the displacement on them, by careful inspection, and by the corrupted flesh that is above them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary fracture is recognized because when the bone is uncovered and rubbed on, the fracture appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In treating a fracture, pay attention to any accidents of illness, and if you see no evil accident, such as vomiting of bile, loss of consciousness, extension, pallor, fever with chills, inflammation of the eyes, etc., in many conditions, he cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any alarming accident and hope for healing, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wounded person first comes to you, especially in winter, it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day after the injury.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, you should hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue beneath the bone does not become corrupted and the accidents we have mentioned do not occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the fracture of the bone reaches the tissue that covers the brain, it is necessary for you to split the fractured part in this way: take the head of the wounded person and uncover the bone in all possible ways and gently on the surface of the wound
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and if blood flows or a hot abscess appears when the bone is uncovered, help him with what is necessary, and fill the place with gauze moistened in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	and let the wound rest until the hot abscess is calmed and you are assured that there will be no bleeding; then begin to remove the bone around it in one of two ways:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	"And then I add another cut, greater than the first one."
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	"The second method is that you have many different cuts, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed and made of iron. And work lightly so that you do not injure the head."
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	"And if the bone is prominent and hard, then you must pierce around it before you administer cuts with trepanation, not so deep that they penetrate the soft bone, and each one should have a margin or circle on top to prevent the point from passing through the bone; and you should have several of these, so that each one fits in its place on the blade of the bone, so that you have trepanations for all testicles. And this is the form of the three kinds of trepanation:"
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	"The qualities for piercing around the broken bone are that you place one trepanation on the bone and turn it with your hands until you feel that the bone has been pierced; then remove the trepanation a little further away, and do this all around, then cut with scissors the space of the bone that is between the holes, and do this as subtly and lightly as possible, so that you can remove the bone by hand or with any of the tools you have such as tweezers; and make sure that you do not touch the cerebellum or the medulla oblongata."
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	"And when you have pierced and removed the bone, then it is necessary that you cut off the remaining prominence of the bone with another tool resembling scissors, but it must be thinner and more delicate than other scissors;"
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	"and if there is anything left of the small bones or any scales, then remove them lightly with one of your tools; then dress the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said."
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	"And the other way of operating is that which Galen recommends, which is safer; and he praises it very much, these are his words:"
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	"It is first necessary that you expose a part of the bone where the fracture appears more openly, so that when you have exposed this part, then place beneath the head of this lenticular knife, of which here is the form:"
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	"And do not cut on one side, but the blade is pointed on both sides so that the cutting edge is towards the bone; then strike gently with a small hammer, so that you cut the bone all around lightly, and be careful of the dura mater beneath."
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	"If it is adherent to the bone, then remove it gently, for it can be removed well without harm and without fear."
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	"And if the fracture of the bone does not reach the dura mater, and the bone is only cut on top with small pieces, then it is necessary to remove this prominence and remove the scales with a fine razor that you should have in various quantities, so as to accommodate each place according to the operation and shape of the fracture."
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	"So remove first with large razors, and then with more delicate ones, and do not stop doing this until it is completely done."
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	"In each of the other capillary cuts and subtle fractures, it is necessary to adapt your action according to its direction; this is something that cannot be responded to by anyone who has dedicated their study to this art."
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	"And if the spinal cord is exposed, then you must take one linen cloth according to the size of the wound, and soak it in rose oil, and place it on the wound;"
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	"then take another cloth doubled in two or three layers, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first cloth; and do this as gently as you can, so that you do not compress the spinal cord, then apply another linen bandage above, and do not tie it too tightly but only enough to keep it in place."
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	"and leave it like this for one or two days until the inflammation has subsided, then untie it and apply medicines such as lily roots, fine wheat flour, incense powder, and aristologus, and similar things; make a powder of these things and place it on the wound, and apply Mondelfian medicines without biting them."
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	"And make sure that the wound is always clean, so that you do not leave any ointment or allow blood to collect there, for when blood collects on the dura mater of the brain, it corrupts and causes great harm to the patient; for when something irritating is placed on the spinal cord, it becomes necrotic above."
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	"Therefore be careful, if any bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt."
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	"And if blackness appears outside due to the medicine that was applied there, then you must take one part of honey and three parts of rose oil and glue together on a cloth, and place it on the spinal cord;"
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"then apply the treatment according to the methods of treatments that are necessary until he is healed."
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	"Know that sometimes both parts of the nose above are broken, or only one is broken by itself, for these are two bones; and the lower one is cartilaginous and does not break, unless it is struck or twisted, then it heals."
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	"And if one of the two parts is broken, then you must insert your little finger or a probe into the nostril and place the break evenly on your index finger inside, and press from behind with your thumb until the nose regains its natural shape;"
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	"and do this gently, and make sure that the patient does not feel pain due to your operation."
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	"And if the break is in the upper part of the nose and your finger cannot reach it, then you must insert a small rod with a rounded end into it."
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	"And if the break is in two places, then do likewise, and try to restore it on the first day if possible;"
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	"But if not, then after the seventh or tenth day, when the inflammation has subsided, insert into the head of the nose a bandage made of linen cloths, if the break is in one part."
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	"Or insert another one on the other side if there is a break there; and let the bandages be so thick that they fill up the nostrils."
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	"And some restorers say that the bandages should be soaked in butter and changed every day. I do not think this is good, but rather they should be soaked in a mixture of egg yolk and millet flour; then leave the bandage until the bone has hardened and the cartilage has stiffened."
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	"And sometimes feathers from a goose are inserted instead of bandages into the nostrils, with one soft cloth wrapped around them, and if the break is held in place, then let the patient blow gently through them; do what you see fit."
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	"And if inflammation appears in the nose while you are working on it, then insert there wax or cotton soaked in rose oil or a little bit of diacynthion."
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	"And if inflammation does not appear in the nose, then apply a plaster from behind made of sesame flour and incense powder mixed with egg yolk, then place light gauze over it and do not bind the nose;"
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the fracture is small and broken into many pieces, remove it with appropriate instruments, then stitch the crack and heal it with suitable remedies, such as plasters and ointments.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound inside yet, then treat it with compresses, and put on plaster splints until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	On the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is fractured below and there is no wound outside, and the fracture is only on one side, not completely broken into two pieces, it can be easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is on the right side, place your left index finger in the patient's mouth and feel for it; if it is on the left jawbone, place your right index finger inside your mouth and gently press on the fracture from outside with your other hand until it aligns.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jawbone is displaced by two fingers' width, you must apply traction forcefully until it is aligned.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if there is displacement or fracture of teeth, thread them with gold, silver or silk thread. Then apply cerote on the broken jawbone and place a double cloth over it. Next, put on a well-made bandage or a piece of leather cut to size according to the length and width of the jawbone, and tie it securely behind the head. Tell the patient to rest and eat soft foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the position changes, untie it on the third day and then reapply what was loosened. Then apply a plaster made from flour mixed with albumen or sesame flour, after removing the cerote. Next, place a light linen over the plaster. If the plaster dries and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until it heals; many times it heals in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if swelling appears, apply what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is both fracture and wound together, examine whether any piece of bone has been lost. If so, use appropriate instruments to remove it carefully.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	If the wound is narrow, widen it with a cautery according to your needs.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these fragments, and none remain, then sew the wound if it is wide, and place one of the bandages suitable for this, to encourage flesh growth until it heals.
de la forcele	From the scalpel
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The scalpel has broken several times near the shoulder blade, and there are three types of breaks: either it is broken off in two places without any fragments, which is easiest to reset; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	The operation is as follows when there is no wound: you will need two assistants so that one can hold the scalpel which has been broken while the other extends the neck towards the part; then align the break between your hands so that the shape is correct and there is neither appearance nor displacement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, place a round cloth or linen sponge under the patient's shoulder according to your needs; then lift the scalpel and grasp the sponge with your hand so that you can align the break correctly.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the blade of the scalpel forward because it has gone in deep, then have the patient lie on their side with a pillow under their shoulder and place a small cushion underneath. Then have your assistant press down on the shoulder so that the bone of the blade is lifted up.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then align the break with your hands and if it is displaced, you must cut upwards. Gently remove any fragments and if the bone cannot be realigned due to any obstruction, use one of the cutting instruments you have to remove the obstacle underneath the scalpel while protecting the tissues.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	It should resemble a spoon and not be sharp. It should also be wide enough according to the size of the bone and the power of the surgery, with two ends: one wide and one narrow like the edges of the wound you made when you exposed the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And once you are sure that there is sufficient granulation tissue present, close the wound. If the edges of the wound are small or in doubt, pack it with gauze and bandages according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if granulation tissue is not present, soak a piece of gauze in rose oil mixed with honey and vinegar, and apply it to the wound.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The treatment of an uninjured bone fracture is to apply a plaster made from the powder of millstone and egg albumen over the bone, then apply light dressings on top. If necessary, place a pillow under the limb.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very wide bandage (about one palm wide), place a doubled gauze pad on top of the dressings and plaster, then take a soft strip (about three fingers wide) and wrap it around the bandage so that the ends of the bandage hang down.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	Then place the strip across the fracture and twist the bandage up over the neck and under both healthy and injured limbs. Secure each part separately so that the binding holds the fracture securely in place without moving on the broken bone. Check this daily and when the bindings become loose, tighten them as needed.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	And have the patient lie on their back and place a small pillow under the injured shoulder while they sleep to elevate it. Lighten the load on the broken bone by aligning the shoulder or tying the arm to the chest, but do not untie it unless necessary for up to 20 days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	Then restart the plastering if necessary, secure it and leave it on until the bone is healed, which usually takes 28 days but can take less time for some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Treatment of shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It sometimes happens that the shoulder blade breaks without displacing the shoulder joint, and cannot be felt except by touch. In such cases, apply the plaster according to the shape of the fracture, and mold it according to its natural shape as much as possible. Then sprinkle powdered millstone with egg albumen on the skin, followed by light dressings, a doubled gauze pad and then a wide and soft strip slightly larger than the shoulder blade. If any sharp edges are felt underneath the strip, fill them in with linseed poultices so that the strip lies evenly. Then secure it firmly with a large bandage to prevent the strip from moving. Check the binding daily and tighten it whenever it loosens. Make sure the patient lies on their side during healing. The shoulder blade usually heals within 20-25 days, but once this period is reached, do not remove the bindings too early as the bone does not heal quickly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a fragment of bone sticks out and is not beneath the heart, cut it off and apply the treatment for fracture of the collarbone as mentioned earlier to encourage granulation tissue formation.
de la brisure dou pis	Treatment of elbow fracture
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The elbow is sometimes fractured in the middle, but this happens rarely. However, it often fractures on the outside. When the elbow is fractured in the middle, it drops downwards and causes severe pain, loss of movement, trembling, and sometimes vomiting of blood. The sharp edges of the broken bone can be felt and seen.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration of it is that the patient lies often on their back, and places one cushion between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and assembles the ribs of the two sides with their hands, and carefully puts them even in all ways they can, until the figure of the bone is as it should be; then places emplasters and compresses above the subtle point of salt or other light wood, and wraps it in one cloth, and ties it on the broken bone so that it does not move; and turns the tie around to the back and tightens it evenly, and re-winds the bandage every hour, and if it loosens, tightens it; and if it is necessary to untie it, for corrosion or for itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then hurry, and untie it, and remove the emplaster, and addresses what has come there in ways of cures; then resets the emplaster, and tightens it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	de la brisure des costes
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of the ribs happens only in large places after the back, and at the head inside, and they bend only because they are glarious; and one feels it well by examining the two sides.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And the restoration of it is that you put back the break even as it should be. Then places an emplaster, and ties it with a bandage if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the break of the ribs is leaning inward, then the patient feels very great pain and piercing, as from pleurisy, because the bone pierces the lung; and they have difficulty breathing, and cough up a lot of blood, and it is a serious condition, and the ancients used to put great effort into treating it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And there are some who say that one should give him foods that swell the belly, to push back the break from within.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, lest abscesses come if they were not there before.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they are there, then heal them.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	"And they said that one should place cupping glasses on the spot to suck strongly, and this seems reasonable; nevertheless, there is doubt whether the cupping glasses will draw out the excesses to the location due to the condition of weakness."
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	"And they said that one should cover the spot with moistened wool in hot oil, and then place tents between the ribs to make the belt equal, after which it should be treated with pleurisy treatment, flesh, and medicine."
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear on the bone that pierces the flesh, there is doubt for the patient whether one must cut above the location of the broken rib and place an instrument underneath to ward off the spleen; then one should carefully trim the bone and gently pull it out, and afterwards sew up the two lips of the wound if it is large, and treat it with plasters until it heals. And if red hot inflammation comes, one should put moistened cloths in rose oil on the location; treat the location according to what is necessary for inflammation, and have the patient lie often on the side where they must be until they are healed."
de la brisure dou col	"de la brisure dou col"
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	"No fracture ever comes to the bones of the neck, and hardly does it bend; and likewise to the spine of the back."
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	"And when it happens to someone and you wish to know if they will recover or not, take heed if you see their hands softened and swollen and lifeless, and they cannot move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it. Know that it is deadly in several conditions, and if they move and feel well when they are pressed and pricked, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured if one applies treatment."
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	"And if something similar happens to the spine of the back and you wish to know if they will recover or not, take heed if the feet are softened, and if the accident has happened to both hands, and wind escapes from the back without control; and when one lies them on their stomach, wind escapes without control. And when they lie on their back and want to raise themselves, they cannot do so. Know that it is deadly: do not labor in its treatment."
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	"And if this accident does not happen to them, then the matter is lighter."
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	"And the treatment is that you should watch if there is hot inflammation, then put rose oil or goose grease on the spine until it is appeased; then put on a comforting and drying plaster, bind it with a bandage, and tell the patient to rest; and they should not sleep on the part where they feel pain until they are healed."
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	"And if any bone dislocates, one must compress on the chest; and remove the bone, then bring together the two lips of the wound if it is large with one stitch, then treat it with ointment that penetrates the flesh until it heals; and if the socket of the bone is broken, which is called the 'socket of the cow,' put your left hand's pouch into it and place it level with the other hand with all your strength, then put on a plaster and a splint if necessary; then compress it, and if there is dislocated bone, open it up and remove it, and treat the wound until it heals."
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Here is the translation for "de la brisure de l’os de la hainche":
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	If it happens that the bone of the temple is broken, and if this happens, there occurs a slight diminution to the head; and it makes one lean forward, and declines towards the parted side, and pain comes to the patient at the place where it is broken, and pricking, and swelling at what is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the treatment is that you raise your hand up until you are above the break; and know what is the break and its shape; and if the break is at the head only, then set this break so that it is in its natural position.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long, or declines inward, then make the patient lie on their stomach so that the restoration of this break can be seen more easily.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it in its proper place, then put on the splint, then put a wooden or metal splint over it, and bind the break so that it does not move; and fill in the space under the ribs until the bandage is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on their sound side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if any inflammation comes, do not touch it until the inflammation has subsided, and put on what we have said before; and then return to the restoration, and bind it as it should be, if there is no bad complication; and that is the manner of treatment.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Regarding the break of the shoulder blade
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder blade is that which is between the ribs and the head of the shoulder bone. And if it is broken, it should be restored in one of these two ways:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie two joints together with two strings and hang them from above, and have the patient sit on one seat; then throw his broken arm onto the wood until it reaches the elbow, and place it in a curve of wood, then hang some heavy object or have the assistant pull it down; then put the break in line with your hands together so that the break returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another way is to place the patient on their backrest and have them put their hand on their neck, then command two assistants to each take one end of the break with their hands—the first one taking the top part and the second one taking the bottom—and extend each one towards its side.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if you see that the traction is too strong, then tie one string below the break and another above it, and have each assistant extend towards their side. And if the break is close to the head of the shoulder, then you should put one string in the middle under the elbow and another towards the chest, under the break; likewise if the break is towards the chest, it is necessary to put one string lightly without effort so that the break is level on the left side and on the chest; then put the break back together as it should be and tie it tight, especially if there are any gaps.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if there are gaps present, then do not tie it too tightly for at least 28 days, and put wet linen on it and rose oil until the inflammation is calmed; then tie it tight, and the method to tie it is as follows: place the splint on the break, then bring the arm close to the support and put your hand on the shoulder or chest; then put the bandage on and tie it tightly onto the support and arm so that the arm is in line with the stars, unless something prevents it or if the bone has moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is not moving back into place, then use stars (splints) and put one larger and stronger than the others on top of the break with two fingers' width between each splint. Each splint should be large enough to extend three fingers past the break on either side; then tie them on as I described at the beginning of this chapter for the break, tying more tightly and without stretching too much.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you see that the position of the splints and the tension are as we have described when you put the broken limb back in place, and you suspect inflammation, then leave it tied for up to seven days as we have said; then check every three days to ensure that there is no itching or swelling around the bandage, or that the limb does not become numb due to the bandage being too tight. Then adjust as necessary as we have described.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	And if no such accidents occur, then do not untie until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back, with their hands on their stomach; place one cushion full of even wool under the shoulder, and watch every hour during the day or night that the broken limb does not move or that the ligaments are not softened. Then straighten it through the power of medicine, and feed them the food we have mentioned earlier in such a way that initially the food is subtle; once they begin to recover, let it be coarse. And it is customary for the shoulder and leg to be reset within forty days altogether; then you should untie and administer baths and ointment medicines to set the joint correctly. But if the contraction is severe and twisted, it may take ten days or two months to untie.
de la brisure du bras	Of the break of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones called the two "fossicles", one of which is small and supports the wrist; the other is large and is located beneath it towards the little finger. Sometimes only the large fossicle breaks, or sometimes only the small one does, but both may also break together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small bone is broken, the setting is easy and healing is quick; but when the large bone is broken, healing is difficult and more painful than if they were both broken together. If only the small bone is broken, it should be gently extended a little and set evenly.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it is the large bone that is broken, then you must pull harder on the traction; extend it over one cushion and raise the palm of the hand higher than the other fingers, with the little finger lower than the others, and let the patient lie crossed on their back, with another cushion placed before them to prevent any discomfort. Then the ministers should stretch the upper arm at the part below the patient's hand using a sling or bandage; and another minister should apply traction from above. And then the physician should set it evenly according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if there are broken fragments in the fracture, then each should be placed back in its proper position; and if any fragment is too short to grasp with forceps, and you cannot restore it to its place, then cut off and remove the bone, as we have mentioned before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if there is also a wound from the breakage, I have spoken about it in the chapter on wounds specifically; so take care of it accordingly.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if swellings appear at the beginning of setting the bone, then take a cloth made from rose oil and white wax that is neither too hard nor too soft; tie it gently over the swelling until the inflammation has subsided. Then remove the cloth, apply the plaster made from flour with abundant egg, and place the splints on top. Make sure that the splint at the breakage site is stronger than the others and slightly wider; there should be six splints for the arm in various positions: whether the break is in one bone or two. Also, apply more traction above the break than elsewhere, and gradually decrease it as it heals, as I mentioned at the beginning of this chapter. Use soft, moist bandages on the break site to prevent them from being too hard or rough; use linen thread for tying that is neither too thick nor too thin, as we have discussed before. And recheck the limb and the splints after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	"And if some unfortunate event occurs in the limb, such as itching that affects the limb, then you must wash the limb with warm water until the itching subsides; and allow the limb to rest, not too tightly. Then resume the restraint, and if the ligaments are softened and the bone is separated, and similar things, apply treatment."
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	"And if it is observed that the bandaging cannot reach the limb because it is too tight, then you must soften it a little and leave it thus for several days until the inflammation arrives, and then apply restraint."
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	"And if none of the things we have mentioned occurs in the patient, then do not remove the sling for up to 20 days or until it is complete. Then the person places their hands on their neck and keeps their neck straight; they observe movement and avoid dislodging, and sleep on their back. Know that this dislocation can be restored in 30 to 35 days, and sometimes even in 20 days, depending on the compositions and complexions of the humors."
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that at the back of the hand and around both wrists, there are few fractures; it is mostly dislocation that occurs.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	"And when the palm of the hand is fractured or dislocated, then the patient must sit cross-legged and sit upright in front of them correctly. Then they place their hand on an extended table, and the physician extends the broken bones and aligns them so that they are well joined; and applies plasters and bandages if no infection occurs, then places a splint according to the quantity of the area affected; and is wrapped in one linen cloth."
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	"And if the fracture is at the edge around the belly of the palm, then make a splint of bandages and instruct the patient to tie it to their broken palm. Then bind it with a long bandage, and let the splint be made of soft cloth, as large as the palm of the hand, and bind it accordingly."
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	"And if the fracture is on the back of the hand, then you must place a splint above it and another below in the palm so that the hand is open and straight. Then bind it all around the hand, and make sure the binding between both wrists is secure."
